Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
Al-Ash'ari's Night Vigil and Concealed Worship
Ibn Asakir transmits a tradition about al-Ash'ari's continuous night worship and concealment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extent of al-Ash'ari's dedication to worship, specifically his practice of maintaining ritual purity for the dawn prayer and his humility in concealing his devotional efforts.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's piety was constant and hidden.

In this lesson, we examine a remarkable account from Ibn Asakir that reveals how Imam al-Ash'ari prayed the dawn prayer with the ablution of the night prayer for twenty consecutive years. This practice illustrates not only his devotion but also his humility, as he concealed his spiritual exertions. The following passage, transmitted through a chain of reliable scholars, invites us to reflect on the depth of his worship.

Guided Path
1
Read the transmitted account carefully
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. The account is a chain of narrators leading to a statement about al-Ash'ari's prayer practice.
Notice the isnad begins with shaykhs, showing transmission through multiple trustworthy sources.
2
Identify key details: duration, action, concealment
Look for three elements: how long he did it ('nearly twenty years'), what he did (prayed Fajr with wudu of Isha), and his attitude (he did not disclose his devotional efforts to anyone).
The concealment is important—it shows his humility.
3
Reflect on the significance of this practice
Consider what this tells us about al-Ash'ari's spiritual state and his approach to worship. It indicates constant awareness of Allah, discipline, and sincerity.
This connects to the broader theme of his asceticism and devotion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ذكر ماعرف من أبي الحسن رضى الله عنه من الاجتهاد في العبادة ونقل عنه من التقلل من الدنيا والزهادة
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو المظفر بن أبي العباس الشعيري الصوفي، قال أخبرنا الإمام أبو الفضل محمد بن على بن أحمد بن الحسين البسطامي، جدى لامی قال : سمعت علی بن محمد الطبرى المتكلم قال سمعت ابا الحسين السروى الفاضل في الكلام يقول : كان الشيخ أبو الحسن يعني الأشعري قريبا من عشرين سنة يصلى صلاة الصبح بوضوء العتمة، وكان لا يحكى عن اجتهاده شيئا إلى أحد . كتب إلى الشيخ أبو القاسم نصر بن نصر بن على بن يونس بن العكبرى من بغداد يخبرني عن القاضي أبي المعالي عزيزي بن عبدالملك شيذلة قال : سمعت الشيخ الإمام ابا عبدالله الحسين بن أحمد بن محمد الدامغاني قال : سمعت الامام ابا الحسين محمد بن سمعون قال سمعت ابا عمران موسى بن أحمد بن على الفقيه قال سمعت أبي يقول خدمت الامام أبا الحسن بالبصرة سنين وعاشرته ببغداد إلى ان الله فلم اجد اورع منه ولا اغض طرفا ولم أر شيخا أكثر حياء توفى رحمه منه فى أمور الدنيا ولا انشط منه في أمور الآخرة، قال القاضي أبو المعالي لاظهر الحق ونصره وأدحض الباطل وزجره، وأعلن معالم الدين وأقام دعائم اليقين وصنف كتبا هي في الآفاق مشهورة معروفة، وعند المخالف والمؤالف مثبوتة موصوفة فلم تزل وجوه الدين بجانبه مكشوفة القناع وايدى الشريعة بنصرته مبسوطة الباع، وكلمة البدع منقمعة الأمر وشبه الباطل منقصمة الظهر إلى أن مات رضوان الله عليه .
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور الفقيه بدمشق قال ثنا والشيخ أبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك بن الحسن بن خيرون المقرى ببغداد قال انا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الحافظ قال ثنا القاضي أبو محمد عبد الله بن عبد الرحمن الأصبهانی قال: سمعت ابا بن محمد عبدالله بن دانيال يقول سمعت بندار بن الحسين وكان خادم أبي الحسن علی بن اسماعيل بالبصرة قال كان أبو الحسن يأكل من غلة ضيعة وقفها جده بلال بن أبي بردة بن أبي موسى الأشعرى على عقبه، قال : وكانت نفقته في كل سنة سبعة عشر درهما .
Chapter: Mention of what is known of Abu al-Hasan, may Allah be pleased with him, of diligence in worship and what is transmitted from him of abstaining from the world and asceticism. Al-Shaykh Abu al-Muzafar ibn Abi al-Abbas al-Shu'ayri al-Sufi informed us, saying: Imam Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bistami, my grandfather, informed us, saying: I heard Ali ibn Muhammad al-Tabari al-Mutakallim say: I heard Abu al-Husayn al-Sarawi, the expert in theology, say: The Shaykh Abu al-Hasan—meaning al-Ash'ari—prayed the dawn prayer with the ablution of the night prayer for nearly twenty years, and he used not to mention anything of his devotion to anyone. Written to me by al-Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Nasr ibn Nasr ibn Ali ibn Yunus ibn al-Ukbari from Baghdad, informing me from al-Qadi Abu al-Ma'ali Azizi ibn Abd al-Malik Shaydhala, who said: I heard al-Shaykh al-Imam Abu Abd Allah al-Husayn ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Damghani say: I heard al-Imam Abu al-Husayn Muhammad ibn Sam'un say: I heard Abu Imran Musa ibn Ahmad ibn Ali al-Faqih say: I heard my father say: I served al-Imam Abu al-Hasan in Basra for years and accompanied him in Baghdad until Allah—[and] I did not find anyone more pious than him, nor more modest in gaze, and I did not see a shaykh more shy than him; in worldly matters he was the most abstinent, and in matters of the Hereafter the most active. Al-Qadi Abu al-Ma'ali said: He manifested the truth and supported it, refuted falsehood and restrained it, proclaimed the landmarks of the religion, established the pillars of certainty, and authored books that are famous and well-known in the regions, and with opponent and supporter alike they are established and described. So the faces of the religion continued with him unveiled, the hands of the Shari'a through his support extended, the word of innovation suppressed, and the backbone of falsehood broken, until he died, may Allah's pleasure be upon him. And al-Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Faqih in Damascus informed us, saying: ... and al-Shaykh Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik ibn al-Hasan ibn Khayrun al-Muqri' in Baghdad informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Hafiz informed us, saying: al-Qadi Abu Muhammad Abd Allah ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Isbahani informed us, saying: I heard Abu Muhammad Abd Allah ibn Daniyal say: I heard Bundar ibn al-Husayn, who was the servant of Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Isma'il in Basra, say: Abu al-Hasan used to eat from the revenue of a small estate endowed by his grandfather Bilal ibn Abi Burda ibn Abi Musa al-Ash'ari for his descendants. He said: His expenditure every year was seventeen dirhams.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a collection of biographical traditions (akhbar) about al-Ash'ari's pious practices and ascetic lifestyle. It begins with a chapter heading, then presents a chain of authorities culminating in a report that al-Ash'ari prayed Fajr with the wudu of Isha for twenty years, indicating constant ritual purity and night worship. The report emphasizes his concealment of his efforts. Then another chain adds that his servant observed his extreme piety, modesty, and activity for the afterlife. The qadi's commentary praises his role in defending the truth. A final chain gives details about his sustenance: he lived off the produce of a family waqf and spent only seventeen dirhams yearly, illustrating his extreme asceticism. The passage uses multiple isnads to authenticate these reports.

Key Terms
الوضوء
العبادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How long did al-Ash'ari maintain the practice of praying Fajr with the wudu of Isha?
A) Ten years
B) Nearly twenty years
C) Five years
D) Thirty years

Key Takeaway
This account shows that al-Ash'ari's piety was both intense and concealed, reflecting true devotion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ash'ari maintained his wudu from Isha to Fajr for nearly twenty years. What is one small change you can make tonight to begin a similar discipline? Will you actually do it, or just think about it?
?
He never mentioned his devotion to anyone. Consider your last good deed: did you tell anyone about it? What would it take to completely conceal your next act of worship from everyone, including your closest family? Are you willing to try?
?
The report shows al-Ash'ari as both a great scholar and a hidden saint. Which aspect of your character are you more proud of—your knowledge or your unseen devotion? Honestly, which one do you work on more?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

Al-Ash'ari's Asceticism and Frugality
Ibn Asakir's account of al-Ash'ari's extreme frugality and dependence on a waqf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari's extreme asceticism manifested in his daily life, including his meager expenditure and reliance on a small family endowment.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari lived on seventeen dirhams per year.

The second portion of Ibn Asakir's account focuses on al-Ash'ari's material simplicity. Through the testimony of his servant, we learn that he lived off the revenue of a small endowed estate and spent only seventeen dirhams annually. This lesson explores the depth of his detachment from worldly comforts.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration about his livelihood
Read the section beginning with the servant Bundar ibn al-Husayn's testimony. Note the source of his income and the amount he spent.
The estate was a waqf from his grandfather.
2
Reflect on the significance of his expenditure
Consider what seventeen dirhams could buy at that time. It illustrates his minimal consumption and trust in Allah.
This aligns with the Sufi ideal of tawakkul.
3
Connect to his overall character
How does this practice fit with the earlier reports of his worship? It shows his consistency in prioritizing the afterlife over material goods.
This completes the picture of his piety.

Source Text

According to the narration, how much did al-Ash'ari spend each year?
A) Seventeen dirhams
B) Seventy dirhams
C) One hundred dirhams
D) Seven dirhams

Al-Ash'ari's asceticism was embodied in his minimalist lifestyle, spending only seventeen dirhams yearly from a family endowment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your annual budget were only 17 dirhams (about $10 modern equivalent), what would you have to give up? Would you trust Allah to provide for your needs as al-Ash'ari did?
?
Al-Ash'ari chose to live on a fixed small income from a waqf. Are you willing to simplify your lifestyle to free yourself from attachment to material wealth? What is the first step you can take today?
?
Imagine explaining to a successful friend why you admire a scholar who spent only 17 dirhams a year. How would your own spending habits stand in light of this example? What needs to change?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
Al-Ash'ari's Virtue from the Best Generations
Ibn Asakir cites a hadith to show al-Ash'ari's virtue as belonging to the best generations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir uses a prophetic hadith to demonstrate al-Ash'ari's virtue by placing him among the best generations of the Ummah.

Core Idea
Being from the best generations is a mark of virtue and blessing.

Ibn Asakir begins a chapter by asserting that al-Ash'ari was favored to be from the best generations of this Ummah. To support this, he presents a well-known hadith of the Prophet ﷺ that identifies the best generations as the Prophet's own, then the next two. This lesson explores the hadith and its implication for al-Ash'ari's status.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Begin by reading the chapter heading and the hadith with its chain of narration. Notice the careful transmission from Abu Hurayra through Ahmad ibn Hanbal.
2
Understand the hadith
The hadith states that the best generation is the one in which the Prophet was sent, then the next two. Count them: three generations in total.
The third generation is likely the tabi' al-tabi'in.
3
Connect to al-Ash'ari
Ibn Asakir uses this hadith to show that al-Ash'ari belongs to one of these virtuous generations, thus highlighting his high rank.
Al-Ash'ari lived in the third Islamic century, which corresponds to the third generation.
4
Reflect on the method
This is a common scholarly method: citing a scriptural source to support a biographical point. It shows the author's reverence for al-Ash'ari.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ذكر ما يسر لأبي الحسن رحمه الله من النعمة من كونه من خير قرون هذه الأمة
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم هبة الله بن محمد بن عبدالواحد بن قال أخبرنا أبو على الحسن بن علی بن محمد بن التميمي، قال انا أبو بكر أحمد بن جعفر بن حمدان القطيعي قال ثنا عبد الله بن أحمد ابن حنبل، قال حدثني أبي قال ثنا هشيم قال انا أبو بشر بن عبد الله بن شقيق عن أبي هريرة قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( خير أمتى القرن الذي بعثت فيهم ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم - والله أعلم قال
Chapter: Mention of what was facilitated for Abu al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on him, of grace, from his being from the best generations of this Ummah. Al-Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Hibat Allah ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid informed us, saying: Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Tamimi informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan al-Qati'i informed us, saying: Abd Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal informed us, saying: My father informed me, saying: Hushaym informed us, saying: Abu Bishr Abd Allah ibn Shaqiq informed us from Abu Hurayra, who said: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'The best of my Ummah is the generation in which I was sent, then those who follow them, then those who follow them.' And Allah knows best, he said.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This brief passage presents a chapter heading asserting that al-Ash'ari was favored by being from the best generations, and then provides a hadith via a chain going back to Abu Hurayra. The hadith states that the best generation is that of the Prophet, then the next two. The implication is that al-Ash'ari lived in the third generation (tabi' al-tabi'in) or later, but the author uses this to indicate his virtue. The chain includes Ahmad ibn Hanbal.

Key Terms
القرن
خير أمتي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This hadith proves that al-Ash'ari was a Companion of the Prophet.
Correction: The hadith praises three generations, but al-Ash'ari lived in the third generation (Tabi' al-Tabi'in) or later, not as a Companion. The hadith is used to show his virtue as part of those early generations, not to claim he was a Companion.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, how many best generations are mentioned?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) One

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir uses the hadith of the best generations to affirm al-Ash'ari's high rank among the virtuous early Muslims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you see yourself as part of these 'best generations'? How does your commitment to following the Prophet and his companions measure up against the standards set by the early Muslims?
?
If being from the best generations is a mark of blessing, what steps can you take today to emulate the faith and character of those generations in your own life?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
The Piety and Modesty of Imam al-Ash'ari
First narration describing his wara', lowering gaze, haya', and energy for the akhira.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the personal virtues of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as described by a contemporary who served him.

Core Idea
Imam al-Ash'ari combined profound piety with energetic devotion to the Hereafter.

This passage introduces us to the character of Imam al-Ash'ari through the eyes of someone who served him for years. It highlights four key virtues: scrupulous piety (wara'), modesty (haya'), lowered gaze, and energy for the afterlife. As you read, notice how these qualities are presented as a complete picture of a scholar who lived his faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration about his character
Read the Arabic text once, then the translation. Focus on the description given by the witness who served him in Basra and Baghdad.
The chain includes several narrators, but the core is a firsthand account.
2
Identify the four qualities mentioned
The narrator says he did not find anyone more pious (awra'), more likely to lower his gaze, more modest (haya') in worldly matters, nor more energetic in matters of the Hereafter. List these qualities.
These are not random; they cover both inner piety and outer conduct.
3
Reflect on the integration of these virtues
Consider how these virtues together paint a portrait of a balanced scholar. His modesty in worldly affairs did not dampen his zeal for the afterlife.
This integration is a model for students of knowledge.
4
Note the chain of transmission
The narration comes through a reliable chain: Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Damaghani from Abu al-Husayn from Abu 'Imran from his father. This lends credibility.
Knowing the chain helps assess authenticity.

أحمد بن محمد الدامغاني قال : سمعت الامام ابا الحسين محمد بن سمعون قال سمعت ابا عمران موسى بن أحمد بن على الفقيه قال سمعت أبي يقول خدمت الامام أبا الحسن بالبصرة سنين وعاشرته ببغداد إلى ان الله فلم اجد اورع منه ولا اغض طرفا ولم أر شيخا أكثر حياء توفى رحمه منه فى أمور الدنيا ولا انشط منه في أمور الآخرة، قال القاضي أبو المعالي لاظهر الحق ونصره وأدحض الباطل وزجره، وأعلن معالم الدين وأقام دعائم اليقين وصنف كتبا هي في الآفاق مشهورة معروفة، وعند المخالف والمؤالف مثبوتة موصوفة فلم تزل وجوه الدين بجانبه مكشوفة القناع وايدى الشريعة بنصرته مبسوطة الباع، وكلمة البدع منقمعة الأمر وشبه الباطل منقصمة الظهر إلى أن مات رضوان الله عليه . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور الفقيه بدمشق قال ثنا والشيخ أبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك بن الحسن بن خيرون المقرى ببغداد قال انا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الحافظ قال ثنا القاضي أبو محمد عبد الله بن عبد الرحمن الأصبهانی قال: سمعت ابا بن محمد عبدالله بن دانيال يقول سمعت بندار بن الحسين وكان خادم أبي الحسن علی بن اسماعيل بالبصرة قال كان أبو الحسن يأكل من غلة ضيعة وقفها جده بلال بن أبي بردة بن أبي موسى الأشعرى على عقبه، قال : وكانت نفقته في كل سنة سبعة عشر درهما .
Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Damaghani said: I heard the Imam Abu al-Husayn Muhammad ibn Sam'un say: I heard Abu 'Imran Musa ibn Ahmad ibn 'Ali al-Faqih say: I heard my father say: I served the Imam Abu al-Hasan in Basra for years and accompanied him in Baghdad until Allah [took him?], and I did not find anyone more pious (awra') than him, nor more likely to lower his gaze, nor did I see a shaykh with more modesty (haya') than him in worldly matters, nor more energetic in matters of the Hereafter. The qadi Abu al-Ma'ali said: He manifested the truth and supported it, refuted falsehood and restrained it, proclaimed the landmarks of the religion, established the pillars of certainty, and authored books that are famous and well-known in the horizons, affirmed and described by both opponent and supporter. The faces of the religion remained unveiled by his side, and the hands of the Shari'a were extended by his support. The word of innovation was suppressed, and the spine of falsehood was broken until he died, may Allah be pleased with him. [Another chain:] The shaykh Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Faqih in Damascus informed us, and the shaykh Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Malik ibn al-Hasan ibn Khayrun al-Muqri' in Baghdad said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Ali ibn Thabit al-Hafiz told us: the qadi Abu Muhammad 'Abdullah ibn 'Abd al-Rahman al-Asbahani told us: I heard Aba ibn Muhammad 'Abdullah ibn Daniyal say: I heard Bundar ibn al-Husayn, who was the servant of Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Isma'il in Basra, say: Abu al-Hasan used to eat from the produce of a land that his grandfather Bilal ibn Abi Burda ibn Abi Musa al-Ash'ari had endowed to his descendants. He said: His annual expenditure was seventeen dirhams.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, transmitted through two chains. The first narration, from the son of a companion who served him, emphasizes his personal piety (al-wara'), modesty (al-haya'), and his dedication to the Hereafter over worldly matters. Then the qadi Abu al-Ma'ali describes his public role: he manifested the truth, supported it, refuted falsehood, and authored widely recognized books that were accepted by both opponents and supporters. This shows the impact of his works. The second narration, from his servant Bundar, reveals his simple lifestyle: he ate only from the produce of an endowment left by his grandfather, and his yearly expenses were merely seventeen dirhams. This underscores his asceticism (zuhd) and independence from worldly wealth. Together, these narrations paint a picture of a scholar who combined personal piety, scholarly output, and material simplicity.

Key Terms
الورع
الحياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration, what did the witness find most remarkable about Imam al-Ash'ari's character?
A) His vast knowledge and many books
B) His piety, lowered gaze, and modesty in worldly matters
C) His wealth and generosity
D) His political influence

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari exemplified a balanced piety that combined humility in worldly affairs with energetic devotion to the Hereafter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that Imam al-Ash'ari was 'more energetic in matters of the Hereafter.' When you look at your own daily schedule, is most of your energy going into dunya or akhira? What would it take for you to redirect one hour of your 'worldly energy' towards an act of worship or learning Islam today?
?
The witness said he never saw a shaykh with more modesty (haya‘) than Imam al-Ash'ari in worldly matters. In what situations do you find yourself lacking modesty—perhaps in your speech, dress, or online presence? Will you commit to lowering your gaze or speaking more softly starting now?
?
Imam al-Ash'ari's piety was not passive; it drove him to be active in the Hereafter. What is one doubt or hesitation that prevents you from being more proactive in your faith? How can you use this lesson to overcome it starting this week?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

His Scholarly Works and Simple Lifestyle
Qadi's praise for his works and his servant's account of his minimal expenditure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari's scholarly output and ascetic lifestyle reinforced each other, as described by later authorities.

Core Idea
He wrote widely accepted books while living on an annual expenditure of just seventeen dirhams.

This passage presents two complementary angles: first, the qadi Abu al-Ma'ali's praise for his public role and influential books, and second, an eyewitness account of his frugality through a family endowment. Together, they show that his scholarly authority was matched by personal detachment from worldly comforts.

Guided Path
1
Read the qadi's description of his public role
Read the passage starting from 'قال القاضي أبو المعالي' up to 'إلى أن مات'. Notice the verbs: he manifested truth, refuted falsehood, proclaimed religion, and authored books.
The qadi emphasizes the impact of his works on both supporters and opponents.
2
Note the description of his books
The passage says his books are 'famous in the horizons' and 'affirmed by both opponent and supporter'. This indicates wide acceptance.
His works became standard references in kalam.
3
Read the servant's account of his simple living
From 'سمعت بندار بن الحسين' to the end. His servant says he ate only from a family endowment, and his yearly expenses were 17 dirhams.
17 dirhams was a minimal amount, showing extreme zuhd.
4
Reflect on the contrast and connection
How did a scholar with such influence live so simply? This shows his sincerity and reliance on Allah. His books spread not because of wealth but because of truth.
This aligns with the earlier narration about his piety.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
Evidence that Abu al-Hasan is from the Best Generations
Chapter citing multiple hadith about the best generations to place Abu al-Hasan among them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith about the best generations support the virtue of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and why he belongs to that blessed era.

Core Idea
The Prophet's hadith place the third century among the best generations, and Abu al-Hasan lived in that era.

In this chapter, Imam Ibn 'Asakir gathers multiple hadith narrations that explicitly list the best centuries of the ummah. These narrations, when combined, establish that the third century is included among the best, providing a strong basis for honoring scholars like Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari who lived in that period. Let's examine the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the significance
Recognize that the author is using hadith evidence to establish a biographical virtue for Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.
2
Read the first hadith
Notice the chain from Abu Hurayra and the uncertainty about the third century. The narrator says 'and Allah knows best whether he said the third or not'.
3
Compare with other chains
See how other narrations remove doubt by explicitly mentioning the third century without any uncertainty.
4
Examine the second hadith
This hadith from Ibn Mas'ud lists four best generations: the Prophet's century, then those who follow, then those who follow, then those who follow. Note that Dawud al-Dabbi's version includes the fourth generation.
5
Draw the conclusion
The third century is affirmed as among the best through these multiple narrations, supporting Abu al-Hasan's status as a scholar from the best generations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ذكر ما يسر لأبي الحسن رحمه الله من النعمة من كونه من خير قرون هذه الأمة أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم هبة الله بن محمد بن عبدالواحد بن قال أخبرنا أبو على الحسن بن علی بن محمد بن التميمي، قال انا أبو بكر أحمد بن جعفر بن حمدان القطيعي قال ثنا عبد الله بن أحمد ابن حنبل، قال حدثني أبي قال ثنا هشيم قال انا أبو بشر بن عبد الله بن شقيق عن أبي هريرة قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( خير أمتى القرن الذي بعثت فيهم ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم - والله أعلم قال الثالثة ام لا - ثم يجيء قوم يحبون السمانة يشهدون قبل أن يستشهدوا) رواه مسلم بن الحجاج في صحيحه عن يعقوب بن ابراهيم الدورقي عن هشیم بن بشير الواسطى، وقد جاء هذا الحديث من وجهين آخرين من غير شك في ذكر القرن الثالث بعد ذكر القرنين، أخبرنا به الشيخ أبو بكر محمد بن الحسين بن على بن ابراهيم الفرضى المقرى ببغداد قال ثنا القاضي أبو الحسين محمد بن علی بن محمد بن عبيد الله بن عبد الصمد بن المهتدى بالله ح وأخبرنا به الشيخ أبو القاسم اسمعيل بن أحمد بن عمر بن السمر قندى قال انا أبو الحسين أحمد بن محمد بن أحمد البزاز قالا انا أبو القاسم عيسى بن على بن عيسى الوزير قال انا عبد الله بن محمد بن عبدالعزيز قال ثنا داود بن عمرو الضبي قال ثنا سلام أبو الأحوص قال ثنا منصور عن إبراهيم عن عبيدة السلماني عن عبد الله قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ) خير أمتى قرنى ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم ثم يجيء قوم تسبق شهادة أحدهم يمينه ويمينه شهادته ) قال ابراهیم فكنا ننهی ان نحلف بالعهد والشهادات هذا حديث متفق على ضحته، رواه البخاري في صحيحه عن محمد بن كثير العبدي عن سفيان ابن سعيد الثورى عن منصور ورواه مسلم في صحيحه عن قتيبة بن سعيد وهناد بن السرى عن أبى الأحوص سلام بن سليم الكوفي إلا انهما لم يذكرا ) ثم الذين يلونهم الثالثة ) كما ذكرها داود بن عمرو الضبي في حديثه، وأخبرنا به الشيخ أبو القسم هبة الله بن محمد بن عبد الواحد الشيباني قال انا أبو طالب محمد بن محمد بن ابراهيم بن غيلان الهمذاني قال أنبأ أبو بكر محمد بن عبد الله بن ابراهيم الشافعي قال ثنا الحرث ابن أبي اسامة قال ثنا أبو النضر قال ثنا أبو معاوية شيبان عن عاصم عن خيثمة والشعبي عن النعمان بن بشير عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال (خير الناس قرني ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم ثم يأتي قوم تسبق ايمانهم شهادتهم وتسبق شهادتهم ايمانهم ) أخرجه أبو عبد الله أحمد بن محمد بن حنبل رحمه الله في مسنده عن أبي النضر هاشم بن القسم البغدادى هكذا وذكر فيه القرن الثالث بعد قرن النبي الله عليه وسلم، وفيه اوفى دليل على المعنى الذي اشرت في ترجمة
Chapter on mentioning what was facilitated for Abu al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on him, of blessing from his being from the best centuries of this ummah. The shaykh Abu al-Qasim Hibat Allah ibn Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Wahid ibn informed us: Abu 'Ali al-Hasan ibn 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Tamimi informed us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ja'far ibn Hamdan al-Qati'i told us: 'Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal told us: my father told me: Hushaym told us: Abu Bishr ibn 'Abdullah ibn Shaqiq told us from Abu Hurayra who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'The best of my ummah is the century (qarn) in which I was sent, then those who follow them, then those who follow them—and Allah knows best whether he said the third or not—then there will come a people who love plumpness, who give testimony before being asked to testify.' Muslim ibn al-Hajjaj narrated it in his Sahih from Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim al-Dawraqi from Hushaym ibn Bashir al-Wasiti. And this hadith has come from two other chains without doubt mentioning the third century after mentioning the two centuries. [Another chain:] The shaykh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn 'Ali ibn Ibrahim al-Faradi al-Muqri' in Baghdad informed us: the qadi Abu al-Husayn Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ubayd Allah ibn 'Abd al-Samad ibn al-Muhtadi billah told us, and the shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn 'Umar ibn al-Samarqandi informed us: Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Bazzaz told us: they both said: Abu al-Qasim 'Isa ibn 'Ali ibn 'Isa al-Wazir told us: 'Abdullah ibn Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz told us: Dawud ibn 'Amr al-Dabbi told us: Salam Abu al-Ahwas told us: Mansur told us from Ibrahim from 'Abida al-Salmani from 'Abdullah who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'The best of my ummah is my century, then those who follow them, then those who follow them, then those who follow them. Then there will come a people whose testimony of one of them precedes his oath and his oath precedes his testimony.' Ibrahim said: We used to forbid swearing by covenants and testimonies. This hadith is agreed upon its [؟] (sihha). Al-Bukhari narrated it in his Sahih from Muhammad ibn Kathir al-'Abdi from Sufyan ibn Sa'id al-Thawri from Mansur. Muslim narrated it in his Sahih from Qutayba ibn Sa'id and Hannad ibn al-Sari from Abu al-Ahwas Salam ibn Sulaym al-Kufi, except that they did not mention 'then those who follow them the third' as Dawud ibn 'Amr al-Dabbi mentioned in his hadith. And the shaykh Abu al-Qasim Hibat Allah ibn Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Wahid al-Shaybani informed us: Abu Talib Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Ghaylan al-Hamadhani told us: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn 'Abdullah ibn Ibrahim al-Shafi'i told us: al-Harith ibn Abi Usama told us: Abu al-Nadr told us: Abu Mu'awiya Shayban told us from 'Asim from Khaythama and al-Sha'bi from al-Nu'man ibn Bashir from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, who said: 'The best of people are my century, then those who follow them, then those who follow them, then those who follow them. Then there will come a people whose faith precedes their testimony and their testimony precedes their faith.' Abu 'Abdullah Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hanbal, may Allah have mercy on him, extracted it in his Musnad from Abu al-Nadr Hashim ibn al-Qasim al-Baghdadi in this way, and mentioned in it the third century after the century of the Prophet, peace be upon him. And in it is the fullest evidence for the meaning that I indicated in the biography.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a chapter providing hadith evidence that Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari lived in one of the best centuries of the ummah. The author cites three hadith with multiple chains. The first hadith from Abu Hurayra mentions the best century (the Prophet's), then those who follow (the Companions), then those who follow (the Successors), but the narrator is uncertain about the third. The author then notes that other chains explicitly mention the third century without doubt. The second hadith from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud explicitly lists four best generations: the Prophet's, then those who follow, then those who follow, then those who follow. The author points out that Bukhari and Muslim did not include the third 'those who follow' but Dawud al-Dabbi did. The third hadith from al-Nu'man ibn Bashir also lists four generations. The author concludes by saying that this hadith, as recorded by Ahmad ibn Hanbal, mentions the third century after the Prophet's century, and it provides the fullest evidence for the meaning he indicated in the biography—namely, that Abu al-Hasan belongs to that blessed generation.

Key Terms
القرن
خير القرون
الشهادة
اليمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the third century is not included among the best generations of the ummah.
Correction: The hadith variants cited in this passage explicitly include the third century (or even fourth) among the best, supporting the virtue of those who lived in that time, such as Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud as narrated by Dawud ibn 'Amr al-Dabbi, how many best generations are mentioned before the people who give testimony before their oath?
A) Two generations
B) Three generations
C) Four generations
D) Five generations

Key Takeaway
The third generation after the Prophet is among the best of his ummah, and Abu al-Hasan's life in that era is a mark of divine favor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to be judged by the generation you live in, would it be considered one of the best according to this hadith? What does that imply about your responsibility to adhere to the beliefs and practices of the praised generations?
?
The hadith warns that later generations will have people whose testimony precedes their oath. In your own life, do you rush to form judgments or offer opinions without proper thought? How can you embody the integrity of the early generations?
?
Knowing that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari lived in a generation explicitly praised by the Prophet, how does that affect your confidence in his theological contributions? What one concrete step can you take today to learn from his legacy and align yourself with the best generations?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's Virtue: The Third Generation
Ibn Asakir uses hadith to prove al-Ash'ari's generation is the best.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir uses hadith to prove that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari belongs to the best generation (the third generation) and why this is significant for his scholarly authority.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's birth in the third century places him in the generation the Prophet praised as the best.

Ibn Asakir begins by establishing a key biographical claim: that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari was born in the third generation after the Prophet, which the Prophet himself declared to be among the best generations. This claim, if proven, would elevate al-Ash'ari's status and defend him against detractors. The passage presents multiple hadith chains to support this, along with definitions of a generation as one hundred years.

Guided Path
1
Read the first hadith and its chains
Read the hadith 'The best of my community is my generation...' and note how Ibn Asakir provides multiple chains, emphasizing that some include the third generation explicitly.
Pay attention to the phrase 'then those who follow them the third' in Dawud ibn Amr al-Dabbi's narration.
2
Understand the calculation
Consider how Ibn Asakir calculates the generation from the Prophet's mission or death, and why al-Ash'ari's birth in the third century makes him part of that blessed generation.
Ibn Asakir notes that the duration of a generation is one hundred years.
3
Examine the supporting hadiths
Look at the additional hadiths that define a generation as one hundred years, and see how they reinforce the argument.
The hadiths from Ibn Umar and the boy whose head the Prophet wiped confirm the century definition.

Then comes a people who love fatness, they bear witness before they are asked to bear witness. Allah. Muslim ibn al-Hajjaj narrated it in his Sahih from Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim al-Dawraqi from Hushaym ibn Bashir al-Wasiti. And this hadith has come from two other chains without doubt in mentioning the third generation after mentioning the two generations. [Chain] ... from Abdullah (ibn Mas'ud) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The best of my community is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them, then those who follow them. Then comes a people whose testimony precedes their oath and whose oath precedes their testimony.' Ibrahim said: We used to forbid swearing by covenant and testimonies. This hadith is agreed upon its authenticity. Al-Bukhari narrated it in his Sahih from Muhammad ibn Kathir al-Abdi from Sufyan ibn Sa'id al-Thawri from Mansur. And Muslim narrated it in his Sahih from Qutayba ibn Sa'id and Hannad ibn al-Sari from Abu al-Ahwas Salam ibn Sulaym al-Kufi, except that they did not mention 'then those who follow them the third' as Dawud ibn Amr al-Dabbi mentioned in his hadith. And [another chain] from al-Nu'man ibn Bashir from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) who said: 'The best of people is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them, then those who follow them. Then comes a people whose oaths precede their testimony and whose testimony precedes their oaths.' Ahmad ibn Hanbal narrated it in his Musnad from Abu al-Nadr Hashim ibn al-Qasim al-Baghdadi, and in it he mentioned the third generation after the generation of the Prophet (peace be upon him). And in it is the most complete evidence for the meaning which I pointed to in the title of the chapter, because it is not free from the fact that its time is either the beginning of the generation from his mission, or from the time when Allah (mighty and sublime) took his soul and transferred him to his grave, and the duration of a generation in time is one hundred years. So in the two narrations there is evidence for a merit for Abu al-Hasan al-Hasanah, for he was born in the third generation after the generation of the Chosen One, so he was among those whom Allah chose from the nation of Muhammad (peace be upon him) and selected. So he is without doubt from a generation for which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) testified to goodness, in addition to that he is from the Ash'ari stock which (the Prophet) described this nation with faith and wisdom, as is authentically reported from him. For we do not know any imam from the Ash'aris who dedicated himself to silencing the heretics and slanderers in the past or recent times like the dedication of the imam, the scholar, Abu al-Hasan. So he is deserving of this rank, and singled out from the Ash'aris for the honor of virtue. And evidence for the extent of the generation and its duration, which no one disputes regarding the authenticity of its chain, is what we were informed by [chain] that Abdullah ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) led us in the Isha prayer one night at the end of his life. When he said the salam, he said: 'Do you see this night of yours? For at the head of one hundred years from it, there will not remain anyone on the face of the earth.' He meant by that that that generation would be cut off and no one would remain. It is agreed upon its authenticity. Muslim narrated it from Muhammad ibn Rafi' and Abd ibn Humayd from Abd al-Razzaq. And it is also indicated by [another chain] that a man said: ... The Prophet (peace be upon him) wiped his hand on my head and said: 'This boy will live a generation.' I said: By my father and mother, O Messenger of Allah, how long is a generation? He said: 'One hundred years.'
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and apologetic argument by Ibn Asakir to establish the high rank of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. The author uses two main hadiths to prove that al-Ash'ari belongs to the best generation of Muslims, the third generation after the Prophet. First, he presents multiple chains of the famous hadith 'The best of my community is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them' noting that some narrations explicitly mention the third generation. He then states that this provides 'the most complete evidence' for his point: the time of the Prophet's generation could be calculated from his mission or his death, and the length of a generation is one hundred years. Since al-Ash'ari was born in the third century after the Prophet, he is from that virtuous generation that the Prophet testified to as good. Second, Ibn Asakir adds that al-Ash'ari is from the 'Ash'ari stock' (الجرثومة الأشعرية) which the Prophet described with faith and wisdom. Then he praises al-Ash'ari as uniquely dedicated to refuting heretics and slanderers, unmatched among the Ash'aris. To confirm the definition of a generation as one hundred years, he provides two more hadiths: one from Ibn Umar that after one hundred years none of that generation will remain, and another where the Prophet says a generation is one hundred years. Thus the entire passage defends al-Ash'ari's virtue by placing him in the blessed third century and extolling his scholarly contributions.

Key Terms
القرن الثالث
خير القرون
الجرثومة الأشعرية
أبو الحسن الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith about the best generations only covers the first two generations.
Correction: Ibn Asakir demonstrates that some narrations explicitly mention the third generation, thus including al-Ash'ari's time.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, which generation does Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari belong to, and why is this significant?
A) The first generation, because he was a Companion.
B) The second generation, because he was a Successor.
C) The third generation, which the Prophet testified as good, based on hadith and the calculation of centuries.
D) The fourth generation, because he was born after 300 AH.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir establishes Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's virtue by placing him in the third generation, which the Prophet praised as best, thereby defending his scholarly authority.

The Virtue of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari: Century and Affiliation
Ibn Asakir establishes Abu al-Hasan's virtue from his century and Ash'ari affiliation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir uses historical and hadith-based arguments to establish the virtue of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
Abu al-Hasan's virtue stems from his birth in the praised third century and his Ash'ari lineage.

Ibn Asakir opens his defense of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari by grounding his virtue in two undeniable facts: his birth in the third century after the Prophet, a century testified to be good, and his belonging to the Ash'ari school, which the Prophet himself praised for its faith and wisdom. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the century argument
The passage explains that a century is 100 years, and Abu al-Hasan was born in the third century. The Prophet testified to the goodness of the early centuries, so this is a mark of virtue.
Ibn Asakir mentions two interpretations for the start of the century (from the Prophet's mission or death), but both include the third century.
2
Understand the Ash'ari affiliation
The Prophet described the Ash'ari root as possessing faith and wisdom, as reported in authentic hadith. This adds another layer of virtue to Abu al-Hasan.
The term 'Ash'ari root' refers to the tribe of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, but later applied to the theological school.
3
Recognize Abu al-Hasan's unique role
Ibn Asakir emphasizes that no other Ash'ari imam devoted himself to refuting heretics like Abu al-Hasan did, making him uniquely deserving of this honor.
This connects the general virtue of the Ash'ari school to the specific excellence of Abu al-Hasan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب إليه لأنه لا يخلو ان يكون وقته ابتداء القرن من مبعثه، او من حين توفاه الله عز وجل ونقله إلى جدثه ومدة القرن من الزمان مائة سنة ففى الروايتين مايدل على منقبة لأبي الحسن حسنة فإنه ولد في القرن الثالث بعد قرن المصطفى فكان مما اختاره الله من أمة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم واصطفى فهو لاشك من قرن شهد له رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالخيرية مع ما انضاف إلى ذلك من كونه من الجرثومة الأشعرية التي وصفها هذه الأمة فيما صح عنه بالايمان والحكمة، اذ لا نعلم إمـامـا من الأشعريين تجرد لإفحام الملاحدة والمفترين في سالف أو آنف من الزمن . كتجرد الامام العالم أبى الحسن فهو المستحق لهذه المرتبة، والمخصوص من الأشعريين بشرف المنقبة
The door to it because it cannot be that its time is the beginning of the century from his mission, or from when Allah took him and transferred him to his grave. And the duration of the century from time is one hundred years. So in the two narrations there is an indication of a virtue for Abu al-Hasan, a good virtue, for he was born in the third century after the century of the Chosen One, so he was among those whom Allah chose from the ummah of Muhammad ﷺ and selected. So he is undoubtedly from a century about which the Messenger of Allah ﷺ testified to goodness, along with what is added to that of his being from the Ash'ari root which described this ummah, in what is authentically reported from him, with faith and wisdom, for we do not know any imam from the Ash'aris who devoted himself to silencing the heretics and slanderers in past or recent times like the devotion of the imam, the scholar, Abu al-Hasan. So he is deserving of this rank, and singled out from the Ash'aris with the honor of the virtue.

Commentary
This passage is a eulogy and argument for the virtue of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. Ibn Asakir first establishes that there are two possible interpretations for the start of the Prophet's century (from his mission or from his death), but both agree that a century is one hundred years. He then argues that Abu al-Hasan was born in the third century, which is a century praised by the Prophet as the best of generations. Additionally, he belonged to the Ash'ari school, which the Prophet described as possessing faith and wisdom. Ibn Asakir emphasizes that no other Ash'ari imam dedicated himself to refuting heretics as Abu al-Hasan did, making him uniquely deserving of this honor.

The Birth and Death of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari: Disputed Dates
Ibn Asakir narrates a conflicting report on al-Ash'ari's death date and corrects it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical dispute over the death date of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and the importance of critical scrutiny in biographical reports.

Core Idea
The death date of al-Ash'ari is disputed; critical scholars prefer 320 AH over 330 AH.

In this passage, Ibn 'Asakir examines the biographical reports about Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. While the birth year is widely agreed upon, the death year is subject to debate. By analyzing a narration and offering his own correction, Ibn 'Asakir teaches us how to critically evaluate historical claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the flow of the narration. The passage cuts off, but the main idea is present.
2
Identify the reported dates
Find the birth and death dates mentioned in the narration. The narrator says birth in 260 AH and death around 330 AH.
3
Understand the author's criticism
Ibn 'Asakir rejects the death date of 330 AH and calls the narrator 'reckless'. He suggests the correct date is around 320 AH.
The author uses the phrase 'perhaps he meant year neef wa 'ishrin' (320-something).
4
Recognize the majority opinion
The author states that the majority of scholars hold the death date around 320 AH. This shows how consensus is used in historical scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما معرفة زمان أبى الحسن و تاريخ مولده وذكر وفاته ومبلغ عمره ومنتهى أمده أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم نصر بن أحمد بن مقاتل قال أخبرنا جدى أبو محمد بن أحمد المقرى قال انا أبو على بن ابراهيم الفارسي قال سمعت ابا الحسن محمد بن محمد الوزان بالبصرة يقول سمعت ابا بكر الوزان يقول ولد ابن أبى بشر سنة ستين ومائتين ومات سنة نيف وثلاثين وثلاثمائة، لا أعلم لقائل هذا القول في تاريخ مولده مخالفا ولكن أراه في تاريخ وفاته رحمه الله مجازفا ولعله اراد سنة نيف وعشرين فإن ذلك في وفاته قول الأكثرين فقد ذكر لى الشيخان الفقيه أبو الحسن على بن أحمد ابن قبيس وأبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى ان ابا بكر الخطيب الحافظ ذكر لهما قال ذكر أبو محمد على بن أحمد بن سعيد ان ابا الحسن
As for knowing the time of Abu al-Hasan and the date of his birth and mentioning his death and the extent of his age and the limit of his duration: We were informed by Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Nasr ibn Ahmad ibn Muqatil, he said: my grandfather Abu Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Muqri' narrated to us, he said: Abu Ali ibn Ibrahim al-Farsi narrated to us, he said: I heard Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Wazzan in Basra saying: I heard Abu Bakr al-Wazzan saying: 'Ibn Abi Bishr was born in the year 260 AH and died in the year 330-something AH.' I do not know anyone who disagrees with this saying regarding the date of his birth, but I see that he is being reckless regarding the date of his death, may Allah have mercy on him. Perhaps he meant the year 320-something, for that is the saying of the majority regarding his death. For the two shaykhs, the faqih Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad Ibn Qubays and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri', informed me that Abu Bakr al-Khatib al-Hafiz mentioned to them, saying: Abu Muhammad Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Sa'id mentioned that Abu al-Hasan...
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage addresses the biographical details of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. Ibn Asakir reports a narration that Abu al-Hasan was born in 260 AH and died around 330 AH. However, he critically notes that while the birth date is agreed upon, the death date is likely in error. He suggests that the correct death year is around 320 AH (neef wa 'ishrin), which is the view of the majority. The text then begins to cite another authority confirming this but cuts off.

Key Terms
تاريخ مولده
تاريخ وفاته
أبو الحسن الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may assume that the death year of al-Ash'ari is definitely 330 AH based on the initial narration.
Correction: Ibn Asakir shows that the correct year is likely 320 AH, as held by the majority, and criticizes the narrator for inaccuracy.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the most likely year of Abu al-Hasan's death?
A) 260 AH.
B) 330 AH.
C) 320 AH.
D) 350 AH.

Key Takeaway
The historical date of al-Ash'ari's death is best placed around 320 AH, not 330, as per the majority of scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a historical report that seems to contradict what you've always believed, do you accept it uncritically or do you investigate like Ibn Asakir? Is your faith built on verified knowledge or hearsay?
?
Ibn Asakir did not hesitate to call a narrator 'reckless' when the evidence pointed that way. Are you willing to critique respected sources when the truth demands it, or do you let reputation override facts?
?
The birth date was undisputed, but the death date required scrutiny. In your own life, are you as careful about the foundations of your belief as you are about worldly matters? Or do you treat matters of religion with less rigor?

Chronological Distances Between the Prophets
Ibn Asakir cites two chains narrating ten centuries between Adam, Noah, Abraham, and Moses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the traditional Islamic chronology of the time intervals between the early prophets as transmitted by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Between each major prophet from Adam to Moses lay ten centuries.

This lesson presents historical narrations from Ibn Asakir that preserve the time distances between key prophets. Understanding these intervals gives context to the early prophetic history and shows how scholars transmitted such details through chains of narration.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the two distinct chains of narration. The first chain goes back to Abu Salama, the second to al-Waqidi.
The opening fragment about someone living 95 years is a separate report attached here.
2
Identify the intervals
The passage states that between Adam and Noah were ten centuries, between Noah and Abraham ten centuries, and between Abraham and Moses ten centuries. Note that a century is defined as one hundred years.
3
Reflect on the definition of قرن
The text explicitly defines القرن as مائة عام (one hundred years). This removes ambiguity about the length of a century.
Misconception: some might think 'قرن' means a generation; the text clarifies it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عبد الله فلقد عشت خمسا وتسعين سنة وبقيت خمس سنين إلى أن أتم قول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال محمد فحسبنا بعد ذلك خمس سنين ثم مات وأخبرنا الشيخان أبو غالب أحمد وأبو عبدالله يحيى ابنا الحسن بن أحمد بن البناء ببغداد قالا انا أبو الحسين محمد بن أحمد بن محمد بن علی بن الابنوسى قال انا أبو بكر أحمد بن عبيد بن الفضل بن البيرى اجازة قال انا محمد بن الحسين بن محمد بن سعيد الزعفراني قال ثنا أبو بكر أحمد بن أبي خيثمة زهير بن حرب قال ثنا على بن بحر بن برى ويعقوب بن كعب الأنطاكي قالا حدثنا عيسى بن يونس، قال ثنا الأوزاعي عن يحيى بن أبي كثير عن أبي سلمة قال كان بين آدم ونوح عليهما السلام عشرة قرون القرن مائة عام وكان بين نوح وابراهيم عليهما السلام عشرة قرون، أخبرنا الشيخ أبو بكر محمد بن عبدالباقی بن محمد الفرضى قال أنا أبو محمد الحسن بن علی بن محمد الجوهرى قال انا أبو عمر محمد بن العباس بن محمد الخزاز، قال انا أبو الحسن احمد بن معروف بن بشر الخشاب قال انا أبو محمد حارث بن أبي أسامة قال أنا أبو عبد الله محمد ابن سعد قال أنا محمد بن عمر الواقدى عن غير واحد من أهل العلم قالوا كان بين آدم ونوح عشرة قرون القرن مائة عام، وبين نوح وابراهيم عشرة قرون والقرن ماية سنة وبين ابراهيم وموسى بن عمران عشرة قرون والقرن ماية سنة .
Abdullah: I lived ninety-five years and remained five years until completing the saying of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Muhammad said: So we counted after that five years, then he died. And informed us the two shaykhs Abu Ghalib Ahmad and Abu Abdullah Yahya, the two sons of al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn al-Banna, in Baghdad, they said: informed us Abu al-Husayn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ali ibn al-Abnusi, he said: informed us Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ubayd ibn al-Fadl ibn al-Bayri by permission, he said: informed us Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn Said al-Za'farani, he said: narrated to us Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Abi Khaythama Zuhayr ibn Harb, he said: narrated to us Ali ibn Bahr ibn Barri and Ya'qub ibn Ka'b al-Antaki, they said: narrated to us Isa ibn Yunus, he said: narrated to us al-Awza'i, from Yahya ibn Abi Kathir, from Abi Salama, he said: Between Adam and Noah, peace be upon them, were ten centuries, a century is one hundred years; and between Noah and Abraham, peace be upon them, were ten centuries. And informed us the shaykh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Abd al-Baqi ibn Muhammad al-Faradi, he said: informed us Abu Muhammad al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Jawhari, he said: informed us Abu Umar Muhammad ibn al-Abbas ibn Muhammad al-Khazzaz, he said: informed us Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Ma'ruf ibn Bishr al-Khashshab, he said: informed us Abu Muhammad Harith ibn Abi Usama, he said: informed us Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Sa'd, he said: informed us Muhammad ibn Umar al-Waqidi, from more than one of the people of knowledge, they said: Between Adam and Noah were ten centuries, a century is one hundred years; and between Noah and Abraham were ten centuries, and a century is one hundred years; and between Abraham and Moses ibn Imran were ten centuries, and a century is one hundred years.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a historical report about the time intervals between major prophets, transmitted through two independent chains of narration. The first chain goes back to Abu Salama, who states that between Adam and Noah were ten centuries (each century being one hundred years), and similarly between Noah and Abraham. The second chain, from al-Waqidi and others, confirms the same intervals and adds that between Abraham and Moses were also ten centuries. The opening fragment about a person living ninety-five years and then five more to complete a hadith is likely part of an earlier discussion, but it is included here as the text continues. The multiple chains demonstrate the care of early scholars in preserving prophetic timelines.

Key Terms
قرن
آدم
نوح
ابراهيم
موسى
الأوزاعي
الواقدي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'عشرة قرون' might be misinterpreted as ten generations rather than ten centuries.
Correction: The text explicitly defines a century as one hundred years ('القرن مائة عام' or 'والقرن ماية سنة'), so it refers to ten centuries, not generations.

Checkpoint
According to the narrations, how many centuries were between Adam and Noah?
A) Ten centuries
B) One hundred centuries
C) Five centuries
D) Twenty centuries

Key Takeaway
Traditional reports indicate that ten centuries separated each of the early prophets: Adam to Noah, Noah to Abraham, and Abraham to Moses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the thousand-year intervals between the early prophets. How does this immense span of time between divine messages shape your gratitude for having the final revelation from Allah? What are you doing to truly appreciate this blessing?
?
The knowledge of these intervals was preserved through careful chains of narrators over centuries. What are you actively doing to preserve and transmit the Islamic knowledge you have to others? What is one concrete action you will take this week?
?
If you had lived in the long gap between prophets, how would you have sought guidance? How does reflecting on that make you value the Qur'an and the Sunnah even more? Will you increase your daily engagement with them?

Reports on Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's Birth and Death Dates
Ibn Asakir compiles multiple reports on when al-Ash'ari was born and died.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn 'Asakir compiled and critically evaluated multiple historical reports to establish the most reliable death date of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
Scholars use multiple reports and critical evaluation to establish reliable historical facts.

Historical knowledge of early Islamic figures often comes from carefully transmitted reports that must be weighed for authenticity. In this passage, Ibn 'Asakir presents several narrations about the death of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and uses the principle of majority consensus to resolve disagreements. You will see how scholars combine chains of transmission and internal criticism to arrive at a reliable date.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the reports
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Pay attention to the different death dates mentioned: 33-something, 32-something, 324, after 320 and before 330, etc.
The birth year is unanimously reported as 260 AH.
2
Identify the critic's voice
Notice that the first narrator (Abu Bakr al-Wazzan) gives a death date of '33-something', but the compiler doubts this and suggests the majority say '32-something'. This shows scholarly caution.
The compiler does not blindly accept a single report.
3
List the supporting sources for 324 AH
Find the reports that explicitly mention 324 AH: from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi via two shaykhs, from Abu Ya'qub's history, and from Ibn Furak (a student of al-Ash'ari's student).
Ibn Furak's report is given special weight because of his close connection.
4
Understand the conclusion
The compiler presents multiple lines of evidence pointing to 324 AH, and the final note adds that al-Ash'ari died before 330 and was called 'Nasir al-Din' at his funeral.
This illustrates how scholars resolve conflicting reports through accumulation and preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما معرفة زمان أبى الحسن و تاريخ مولده وذكر وفاته ومبلغ عمره ومنتهى أمده أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم نصر بن أحمد بن مقاتل قال أخبرنا جدى أبو محمد بن أحمد المقرى قال انا أبو على بن ابراهيم الفارسي قال سمعت ابا الحسن محمد بن محمد الوزان بالبصرة يقول سمعت ابا بكر الوزان يقول ولد ابن أبى بشر سنة ستين ومائتين ومات سنة نيف وثلاثين وثلاثمائة، لا أعلم لقائل هذا القول في تاريخ مولده مخالفا ولكن أراه في تاريخ وفاته رحمه الله مجازفا ولعله اراد سنة نيف وعشرين فإن ذلك في وفاته قول الأكثرين فقد ذكر لى الشيخان الفقيه أبو الحسن على بن أحمد ابن قبيس وأبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى ان ابا بكر الخطيب الحافظ ذكر لهما قال ذكر أبو محمد على بن أحمد بن سعيد ان ابا الحسن مات فى سنة أربع وعشرين وثلاثمائة قال الخطيب أبو بكر وذكر لي أبو القسم عبد الواحد بن على الأسدى انه مات ببغداد بعد سنة عشرين، وقبل سنة ثلاثين وثلاثمائة وقرأت في تاريخ أبي يعقوب إسحق بن ابراهيم بن عبد الرحمن الهدوى بخط بعض أهل المعرفة قال سنة أربع وعشرين وثلاثمائة فيها مات أبو الحسن على بن اسماعيل الأشعرى وكذا ذكر الأستاذ أبو بكر محمد بن الحسن بن فورك الأصبهاني تلميذ تلميذه أبي الحسن الباهلى وهو أعلم بامره وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم نصر بن نصر بن على العكبرى في كتابه عن القاضى أبى المعالى عزيزى بن عبدالملك قال قيل ان ابا الحسن مات قبل الثلاثين ونودى على جنازته بناصر الدین
As for knowing the time of Abu al-Hasan and his date of birth, and mentioning his death, the length of his life, and the end of his term: informed us the shaykh Abu al-Qasim Nasr ibn Ahmad ibn Muqatil, he said: informed us my grandfather Abu Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Muqri, he said: informed us Abu Ali ibn Ibrahim al-Farisi, he said: I heard Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Wazzan in Basra say: I heard Abu Bakr al-Wazzan say: Ibn Abi Bishr was born in the year 260 (H) and died in the year 33-something (H). I do not know of anyone who disagrees with this statement regarding his date of birth, but I see that he took liberties with his date of death, may Allah have mercy on him, and perhaps he intended the year 32-something (H), for that is the majority opinion regarding his death. For the two shaykhs, the jurist Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Qubays and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri, mentioned to me that Abu Bakr al-Khatib al-Hafiz mentioned to them: Abu Muhammad Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Sa'id mentioned that Abu al-Hasan died in the year 324 (H). Al-Khatib Abu Bakr said: And Abu al-Qasim Abd al-Wahid ibn Ali al-Asadi mentioned to me that he died in Baghdad after the year 320 (H) and before the year 330 (H). And I read in the History of Abu Ya'qub Ishaq ibn Ibrahim ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Hadawi, in the handwriting of one of the people of knowledge, he said: In the year 324 (H) died Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Isma'il al-Ash'ari. And likewise mentioned the master Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak al-Isbahani, the student of his student Abu al-Hasan al-Bahili, and he is most knowledgeable of his affair. And informed us the shaykh Abu al-Qasim Nasr ibn Nasr ibn Ali al-Ukburi in his book, from the judge Abu al-Ma'ali Azizi ibn Abd al-Malik, he said: It was said that Abu al-Hasan died before thirty (330 H) and it was proclaimed at his funeral: 'Helper of the religion' (Nasir al-Din).
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of reports concerning the birth and death dates of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. It begins with a chain that states he was born in 260 H and died around 33-something H, but the narrator doubts the accuracy of the death year and suggests the majority say 32-something H. Then several specific reports are cited: al-Khatib al-Baghdadi reports that al-Ash'ari died in 324 H; another report from al-Asadi says he died after 320 H and before 330 H; Abu Ya'qub's history also states 324 H; Ibn Furak, a student of al-Ash'ari's student, also supports 324 H; finally, it is said he died before 330 H and was proclaimed 'Nasir al-Din' at his funeral. The passage shows that while there is some variation, the majority of reliable sources place his death in 324 H.

Key Terms
أبو الحسن الأشعري
تاريخ المولد
تاريخ الوفاة
سنة 324
ابن فورك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might assume that a single unanimous date exists for al-Ash'ari's death without any disagreement.
Correction: The passage shows that there were multiple reports with slight variation, but the majority of reliable sources converge on 324 AH, and scholars used critical evaluation to reach this conclusion.

Checkpoint
According to the majority of reports cited by Ibn 'Asakir, in which year did Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari die?
A) 330 AH
B) 324 AH
C) 310 AH
D) 333 AH

Key Takeaway
The most reliable reports place al-Ash'ari's death in 324 AH, as supported by multiple chains and the authority of Ibn Furak.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How do you ensure that the knowledge you hold about your faith is based on reliable sources, not just hearsay? Are there any beliefs you hold that might be based on a single weak report? Commit to verifying one belief this week.
?
When faced with conflicting opinions among scholars, do you tend to follow the majority or the most convincing proof? This lesson shows Ibn 'Asakir weighing reports. What does that teach you about your own approach to learning?
?
The funeral proclamation called al-Ash'ari 'Nasir al-Din' (Helper of the Religion). What legacy will you leave? Are you actively helping the religion of Allah, or are you passive in your faith? Write one concrete action you will take this month to be a true 'nasir' of the deen.

The Dream of Ibn Sam'un: Al-Ash'ari's Intercession
Ibn Sam'un narrates a dream showing al-Ash'ari's high status and intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a dream narrative was used to assert the high spiritual status and intercessory role of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
Dreams can reveal spiritual truths about the status of righteous scholars.

This lesson presents a famous dream vision narrated by the pious scholar Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un. In it, a deceased companion appears punished due to his bad opinion of a shaykh, while al-Ash'ari appears in glory, forgiven and interceding for his followers. The dream serves as a powerful affirmation of al-Ash'ari's place among the awliya' and defenders of Sunni orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the dream narrative
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the vivid descriptions: the companion's disfigurement, the dialogue, and the majestic appearance of al-Ash'ari.
The dream uses contrasting imagery to convey spiritual states.
2
Identify the key figures and their roles
Identify Ibn Sam'un (the narrator), his deceased companion (punished), and Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari (forgiven and interceding). Understand why each figure is significant.
The companion's bad opinion of a shaykh caused his punishment.
3
Reflect on the moral lesson
Consider why having a bad opinion of a scholar of Ahl al-Sunna can be spiritually harmful. The dream warns against such attitudes and elevates the status of al-Ash'ari.
This dream is not legal evidence but a spiritual lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروى الشيخ أبو الحسين بن سمعون قال كان لي صاحب يلازم مجلسی متصاون جميل الظاهر كثير المجاهدة فمات فحسنت تجهیزه و دفنته بباب حرب فلما كان بعد ايام رأيته في النوم عريانا مشوه الخلق على صورة قبيحة فقلت له يا ابا عبد الله ما فعل الله بك فقال انا مطرود كما ترى فقلت اما كنت حسن الظن بالله تعالى فقال نعم ولكنى كنت مسيء الظن بهذا الشيخ فنظرت فإذا أنا بشيخ طوال بهى المنظر حسن الهيئة طيب الرائحة جميل المحاسن وهو يقرأ بصوت جهوری :طيب قد وجدنا ما وعدنا ربنا حقا فهل وجدتم ماوعد ربكم حقا، وينظر إلى ذلك المسكين صاحبي وكان معه خلق عظيم فوق الاحصاء فسألت عنه فقيل لي هذا أبو الحسن الأشعري قد غفر الله له قال الشيخ أبو الحسين وأظنهم قالوا وشفعه في أصحابه رضى الله عنهم أجمعين وقد كان الشيخ أبو الحسن كجده أبي موسى الأشعرى موصوفا بحسن الصوت فيما بلغنى من بعض الوجوه كما آه أبو الحسين بن سمعون فى منامه بعد الموت . باب ما وصف من مجانبته لأهل البدع وجهاده وذكر ما عرف من نصيحته للأمة وصحة اعتقاده أخبرنا الشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن الفضل الفراوي بنيسابور قال سمعت الاستاذ ابا القسم عبد الملك بن هوازن القشيري يقول سمعت
And the shaykh Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un narrated: I had a companion who frequented my gathering, dignified in appearance, beautiful in outward form, given much to struggle (mujahada). He died, so I prepared him well and buried him at Bab Harb. Then after some days I saw him in a dream, naked, disfigured in form, in an ugly image. I said to him: O Abu Abdullah, what has Allah done with you? He said: I am expelled as you see. I said: Were you not having good opinion of Allah? He said: Yes, but I used to have bad opinion of this shaykh. So I looked, and behold, I saw a tall shaykh, beautiful in appearance, good in form, pleasant in fragrance, handsome in features, reciting with a loud voice: 'Tayyib, we have found what our Lord promised us true, so have you found what your Lord promised you true?' And he was looking at that poor companion of mine, and with him was a great multitude beyond counting. I asked about him, and it was said to me: This is Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, Allah has forgiven him. The shaykh Abu al-Husayn said: And I think they said: And he interceded for his companions, may Allah be pleased with them all. And the shaykh Abu al-Hasan, like his grandfather Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, was described as having a beautiful voice, as was reported to me from some sources, as Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un saw him in his dream after death. Chapter: What was described of his avoidance of the people of innovation and his struggle, and mention of what was known of his sincere advice to the community and the soundness of his belief. Informed us the shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Farawi in Nishapur, he said: I heard the master Abu al-Qasim Abd al-Malik ibn Hawazin al-Qushayri say: I heard...
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage contains a dream vision narrated by Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un. He describes a pious companion who died and appeared in a dream punished, explaining that his suffering was due to his bad opinion of a shaykh (presumably al-Ash'ari). Then a tall, beautiful shaykh appears reciting a verse, and is identified as Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, who has been forgiven and even intercedes for his followers. The passage concludes with a note that al-Ash'ari was known for his beautiful voice, as confirmed by the dream. After the dream, a new section begins with a chapter heading stating that the following material will describe al-Ash'ari's avoidance of heretics, his struggle, his sincere advice to the community, and the soundness of his creed. The first chain of this section starts with al-Qushayri but is cut off.

Key Terms
المنام
الشفاعة
أبو الحسن الأشعري
أبو الحسين بن سمعون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dreams can be used as legal evidence in matters of theology.
Correction: Dreams are not sources of Islamic law or creed; they may indicate spiritual realities but are not authoritative for establishing doctrine.

Checkpoint
What did the dream reveal about Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari?
A) He was being punished
B) He was forgiven and interceded for his companions
C) He had a bad opinion of others
D) He refused to intercede

Key Takeaway
The dream narrative elevates al-Ash'ari's status by showing his forgiveness and intercession, highlighting the importance of holding good opinion of scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you hold any secret bad opinion about a scholar or imam of Ahl al-Sunna? The companion's punishment came from his bad opinion despite his piety. What is one step you will take today to uproot such hidden resentment from your heart?
?
Al-Ash'ari intercedes for his companions. Do you truly consider yourself among his followers in spirit and conviction? If so, what does this intercession demand from you in terms of loyalty to the Ash'ari creed and love for its scholars?
?
The dream shows that our outward piety can be worthless if our heart harbors ill will. Think of one specific person—scholar or layman—toward whom you have negative feelings. Will you now commit to make du'a for them and remove that from your heart starting now?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

Reports on al-Ash'ari's Death
Reports on al-Ash'ari's death year and place from multiple sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars transmitted and verified reports of al-Ash'ari's death, including the year and place.

Core Idea
Multiple chains of transmission converge on al-Ash'ari's death in 324 AH.

This passage presents a series of reports about the death of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, collected by Ibn 'Asakir. It demonstrates the careful scholarly method of citing multiple authorities and written records to establish a historical fact. You will see how different sources agree on the year 324 AH, though with some variation.

مات فى سنة أربع وعشرين وثلاثمائة قال الخطيب أبو بكر وذكر لي أبو القسم عبد الواحد بن على الأسدى انه مات ببغداد بعد سنة عشرين، وقبل سنة ثلاثين وثلاثمائة وقرأت في تاريخ أبي يعقوب إسحق بن ابراهيم بن عبد الرحمن الهدوى بخط بعض أهل المعرفة قال سنة أربع وعشرين وثلاثمائة فيها مات أبو الحسن على بن اسماعيل الأشعرى وكذا ذكر الأستاذ أبو بكر محمد بن الحسن بن فورك الأصبهاني تلميذ تلميذه أبي الحسن الباهلى وهو أعلم بامره وأخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم نصر بن نصر بن على العكبرى في كتابه عن القاضى أبى المعالى عزيزى بن عبدالملك قال قيل ان ابا الحسن مات قبل الثلاثين ونودى على جنازته بناصر الدین
He died in the year 324. Al-Khatib Abu Bakr said, and Abu al-Qasim Abd al-Wahid ibn Ali al-Asadi mentioned to me that he died in Baghdad after the year 320 and before the year 330. And I read in the history of Abu Ya'qub Ishaq ibn Ibrahim ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Hadawi in the handwriting of some knowledgeable people, he said: In the year 324, Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Isma'il al-Ash'ari died. Similarly mentioned by the master Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Furak al-Isbahani, the student of his student Abu al-Hasan al-Bahili, and he is more knowledgeable about his affair. And Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Nasr ibn Nasr ibn Ali al-Ukbari informed us in his book from Qadi Abu al-Ma'ali Azizi ibn Abd al-Malik, he said: It was said that Abu al-Hasan died before the thirtieth, and it was proclaimed over his funeral as Nasir al-Din.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a collection of reports about the death of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. The author presents multiple narrations: first, that he died in the year 324 AH, as stated by al-Khatib Abu Bakr and corroborated by others. Then a report from the history of Abu Ya'qub al-Hadawi also places his death in 324. The master Ibn Furak is cited as a reliable source for this. Finally, a report from Abu al-Qasim al-Ukbari quotes Qadi Abu al-Ma'ali saying that al-Ash'ari died before the year 330 and that his funeral was announced under the title 'Nasir al-Din'. The passage shows the scholarly effort to establish the correct date and includes chains of transmission to support each report.

Misconception: There is no consensus on al-Ash'ari's death year.
Correction: Multiple reports agree on 324 AH, with some variation in range.
