Dream of al-Ash'ari and the Danger of Bad Opinion
A dream vision of al-Ash'ari forgiving a man who doubted him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the dream vision of al-Ash'ari reported by Ibn Sam'un, and the lesson about holding good opinion of scholars.

Core Idea
A dream reveals that ill opinion of a righteous scholar can lead to punishment.

This lesson presents a remarkable dream narrative from the biography of Imam al-Ash'ari. A pious man who harbored suspicion towards al-Ash'ari is seen in a dream suffering punishment, while al-Ash'ari appears gloriously forgiven and interceding. The story underscores the importance of holding good opinion of scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the dream narrative
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to understand the story.
Pay attention to the details of the dream: the state of the deceased companion and the appearance of al-Ash'ari.
2
Identify key figures and their states
Notice the contrast between the companion's punishment and al-Ash'ari's forgiveness. The companion is described as naked and deformed, while al-Ash'ari is tall, brilliant, and reciting Quran.
3
Reflect on the lesson about opinion of scholars
The companion's bad opinion of al-Ash'ari caused his punishment. Consider how this teaches the importance of holding good opinion of righteous scholars.
This connects to the broader Islamic principle of respecting scholars.
4
Consider the significance of al-Ash'ari's forgiveness and intercession
The dream states that al-Ash'ari was forgiven and interceded for his companions. Reflect on the high status of al-Ash'ari in this vision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروى الشيخ أبو الحسين بن سمعون قال كان لي صاحب يلازم مجلسی متصاون جميل الظاهر كثير المجاهدة فمات فحسنت تجهیزه و دفنته بباب حرب فلما كان بعد ايام رأيته في النوم عريانا مشوه الخلق على صورة قبيحة فقلت له يا ابا عبد الله ما فعل الله بك فقال انا مطرود كما ترى فقلت اما كنت حسن الظن بالله تعالى فقال نعم ولكنى كنت مسيء الظن بهذا الشيخ فنظرت فإذا أنا بشيخ طوال بهى المنظر حسن الهيئة طيب الرائحة جميل المحاسن وهو يقرأ بصوت جهوری :طيب قد وجدنا ما وعدنا ربنا حقا فهل وجدتم ماوعد ربكم حقا، وينظر إلى ذلك المسكين صاحبي وكان معه خلق عظيم فوق الاحصاء فسألت عنه فقيل لي هذا أبو الحسن الأشعري قد غفر الله له قال الشيخ أبو الحسين وأظنهم قالوا وشفعه في أصحابه رضى الله عنهم أجمعين وقد كان الشيخ أبو الحسن كجده أبي موسى الأشعرى موصوفا بحسن الصوت فيما بلغنى من بعض الوجوه كما آه أبو الحسين بن سمعون فى منامه بعد الموت.
And Shaykh Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un narrated: I had a companion who attended my sessions, dignified, handsome in appearance, of great spiritual struggle. He died, so I prepared his funeral well and buried him at Bab Harb. After some days, I saw him in a dream naked, deformed in form, in an ugly image. I said to him, 'O Abu Abd Allah, what did Allah do with you?' He said, 'I am repelled as you see.' I said, 'Were you not of good opinion of Allah?' He said, 'Yes, but I was of bad opinion of this shaykh.' So I looked, and there was a tall shaykh, brilliant in appearance, good of form, pleasant of scent, beautiful of countenance, reciting in a loud voice: 'Good, we have found what our Lord promised us true; so have you found what your Lord promised you true?' And he was looking at that poor companion of mine, and with him was a great creation beyond count. I asked about him, and it was said to me: 'This is Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, Allah has forgiven him.' Shaykh Abu al-Husayn said: I think they said, 'And he interceded for his companions, may Allah be pleased with them all.' And Shaykh Abu al-Hasan was, like his grandfather Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, described as having a beautiful voice, as I heard from some sources, as Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un saw him in his dream after death.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a dream narrative reported by Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un. It describes a man who was a regular attendee of Ibn Sam'un's gatherings, known for his piety, but who had harbored suspicion towards al-Ash'ari. After the man's death, Ibn Sam'un sees him in a dream in a miserable state, and the man confesses that his bad opinion of al-Ash'ari caused his punishment. Then al-Ash'ari appears in a glorious form, reciting a verse from the Quran, and is identified as forgiven by Allah. The dream serves to affirm al-Ash'ari's lofty station and forgiveness, and even suggests his intercession for his followers. The author also notes al-Ash'ari's beautiful voice, likening him to his grandfather the Companion Abu Musa al-Ash'ari.

Al-Ash'ari's Deathbed Principle on Takfir
Narrates al-Ash'ari's deathbed words: he does not declare takfir of any ahl al-qibla.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-Ash'ari, on his deathbed, established the principle of not declaring takfir of anyone who prays toward the qibla, while still condemning the Mu'tazila for their errors.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari refused to excommunicate any Muslim who prays toward Mecca.

This lesson presents a famous biographical report about Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's final moments. The report, transmitted through a chain of reliable scholars, captures al-Ash'ari's two most important statements: his curse of the Mu'tazila and his refusal to declare takfir of any person of the qibla. Together, they illustrate the Sunni theological balance between opposing innovation and preserving communal unity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the transmission chain
Notice the chain of narrators and the context of the deathbed report.
The report is transmitted through multiple reliable scholars, emphasizing its authenticity.
2
Identify al-Ash'ari's two statements
First, he curses the Mu'tazila. Then, he says he does not declare takfir of any ahl al-qibla.
3
Reflect on the doctrinal principle
Why does al-Ash'ari say he does not declare takfir? Because all focus on the same worshipped being; differences are only linguistic.
The phrase 'ikhtilāf al-ʻibārāt' is key.
4
Address the apparent tension
Al-Ash'ari curses the Mu'tazila yet does not declare them kafir. This shows takfir is about the fundamental commonality of the qibla, not about agreement on every point.
Cursing is not the same as declaring kufr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاستاذ الشهيد ابا على الحسن بن على الدقاق رحمه الله يقول : سمعت ابا على زاهر بن أحمد الفقيه رحمه الله يقول مات أبو الحسن الأشعري رحمه الله ورأسه في حجرى وكان يقول شيئا في حال نزعه من داخل حلقه فادنيت إليه رأسى وأصغيت إلى ما كان يقرع سمعى فكان يقول : لعن الله المعتزلة موهوا ومخرقوا، سمعت الشيخين ابا محمد عبد الجبار بن أحمد بن. محمد البيهقى الفقيه وابا القسم زاهر بن طاهر المعدل بنيسابور يقولان سمعنا الشيخ ابا بكر أحمد بن الحسين بن على البيهقى يقول سمعت ابا حازم عمر بن أحمد العبدوى الحافظ يقول سمعت ابا على زاهر بن أحمد السرخسي، يقول لما قرب حضور أجل أبي الحسن الأشعري رحمه الله في داری ببغداد دعانى فأتيته فقال اشهد على انى لا أكفر أحدا من أهل هذه القبلة لأن الكل يشيرون إلى معبود واحد وإنما هذا كله اختلاف العبارات.
The teacher, the martyr, Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Daqqaq, may God have mercy on him, said: I heard Abu Ali Zahir ibn Ahmad al-Faqih, may God have mercy on him, say: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may God have mercy on him, died with his head in my lap, and he was saying something during his death rattle from inside his throat. So I brought my ear close to him and listened to what my hearing could grasp, and he was saying: 'May God curse the Mu'tazila—they deceived and deceived.' I heard the two shaykhs, Abu Muhammad Abd al-Jabbar ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Bayhaqi al-Faqih and Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir al-Mu'addal in Nishapur, say: We heard the shaykh Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn ibn Ali al-Bayhaqi say: I heard Abu Hazim Umar ibn Ahmad al-Abdawi al-Hafiz say: I heard Abu Ali Zahir ibn Ahmad al-Sarakhsi say: When the time of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's death drew near in my house in Baghdad, he called me and I came to him. He said: 'Bear witness that I do not declare any person of this qibla to be an unbeliever, because all direct themselves to one worshipped being, and all this is merely variation of expressions.'
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narration about Imam al-Ash'ari's deathbed. It begins with a chain of transmission descending from al-Daqqaq to al-Sarakhsi. The core of the report is al-Ash'ari's final two statements. First, he cursed the Mu'tazila for their deceit. Second, he insisted that he does not declare takfir of any 'ahl al-qibla' (people who pray toward Mecca) because they all worship the same God; differences among them are only variations of expressions ('ikhtilāf al-ʻibārāt'). This is a foundational principle for Sunni theology: theological disagreements do not negate the commonality of the qibla.

Key Terms
تكفير (takfīr)
أهل القبلة (ahl al-qibla)
المعتزلة (al-Muʻtazila)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari forbade all takfir of any Muslim, including those who commit clear kufr.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari only forbade takfir of those who affirm the qibla and worship the same God; he himself cursed the Mu'tazila, showing he distinguished between error and apostasy.

Checkpoint
What was al-Ash'ari's deathbed position regarding takfir of ahl al-qibla?
A) He declared all ahl al-qibla to be kafir.
B) He refused to declare any ahl al-qibla kafir because of their common focus on the same worshipped being.
C) He said only the Mu'tazila are kafir.
D) He said everyone is a kafir except his followers.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's deathbed statement establishes the Sunni principle that theological disagreement does not warrant takfir as long as the opponent affirms the qibla and oneness of the worshipped being.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been tempted to judge another Muslim's faith because of a theological difference? How does al-Ash'ari's final testimony challenge that impulse in you? Before you answer, consider: if even an imam of Ahl al-Sunna, who cursed the Mu'tazila, still refused to call them unbelievers, can you afford to be harsher?
?
Al-Ash'ari's last words were about unity in worship despite intellectual disagreements. When you disagree with a fellow believer on a non-essential matter, is your heart more concerned with being right or with preserving the bond of the qibla? Ask Allah to purify your intention.
?
Imagine your own deathbed. What principle would you want to be remembered for upholding? Al-Ash'ari's was mercy and restraint in takfir. What is yours? This lesson demands you think about what legacy you are building now.

Ibn Asakir's Justification for Transmitting al-Ash'ari's Creed
Ibn Asakir explains why he must quote al-Ash'ari's creed exactly as written.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ibn Asakir insists on quoting al-Ash'ari's creed verbatim and the scholarly rationale behind faithful transmission.

Core Idea
Faithful transmission of creed requires both trustworthiness and necessity.

Before presenting al-Ash'ari's creed, Ibn Asakir establishes the credibility of the source and the obligation to transmit accurately. This short introduction shows the careful method of Sunni scholars in preserving orthodox doctrine. You will see how he builds a case for exact quotation.

Guided Path
1
Read Ibn Asakir's argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting how Ibn Asakir establishes al-Ash'ari's scholarly status and the consensus of the righteous.
2
Identify the logical structure
Recognize the three parts: (1) al-Ash'ari's renowned orthodoxy, (2) the need to avoid addition or subtraction, (3) the announcement of the quotation.
This is a basic argument: premise → conclusion → action.
3
Reflect on the principle
Consider why exact transmission matters in theological disputes. What would be lost if Ibn Asakir paraphrased?
This connects to the broader Islamic commitment to textual fidelity (amanah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا كان أبو الحسن رضى الله عنه كما ذكر عنه من حسن مستوصب المذهب عند أهل المعرفة بالعلم والانتقاد يوافقه في أكثر ما يذهب إليه أكابر العباد ولا يقدح في معتقده غير أهل الجهل والعناد فلابد ان نحكى عنه معتقده على وجهه بالامانة ونجتنب ان نريد فيه أو ننقص منه تركا للخيانة ليعلم حقيقة حاله في صحة عقيدته في أصول الديانة فاسمع ماذكره في أول كتابه الذي سماه بالابانة فإنه قال الحمد لله الأحد الواحد العزيز الماجد المتفرد بالتوحيد المتمجد بالتمجيد، الذي لا تبلغه صفات العبيد وليس له مثل ولانديد وهو المبدى المعيد، جل عن الصاحية والأبناء وتقدس عن ملامسة النساء فليست له عرة تنال ولاحد تضرب له فيه الأمثال لم يزل بصفاته أولا قديرا ولا يزال عالما خبيرا، سبق الأشياء علمه ونفذت فيها إرادته فلم تعزب عنه خفيات الأمور، ولم تغيره سوالف صروف الدهور، ولم يلحقه في خلق شيء مما خلق كلال ولا تعب ولامسه لغوب ولانصب خلق الأشياء بقدرته ودبرها بمشيئته وقهرها بجبروته، وذللها بعزته فذل لعظمته المتكبرون، واستكان لعظم ربوبيته المتعظمون وانقطع دون الرسوخ في علمه الممترون وذلت له الرقاب وتارت فى ملكوته فطن ذوى الألباب، وقامت بكلمته السموات السبع واستقرت الأرض المهاد وثبتت الجبال الرواسي وجرت الرياح اللواقع، وسار في جو السماء السحاب وقامت على حدودها البحار وهو إله قاهر يخضع له المعززون ويخشع له المترفعون ويدين طوعا وكرها له العالمون، نحمده كما حمد نفسه وكما ربنا له أهل ونستعينه استعانة من فوض أمره إليه وأقر أنه لا ملجأ ولا منجى منه إلا إليه ونستغفره استغفار مقر بذنبه معترف بخطيئته ونشهد ان لا إله إلا الله وحده لاشريك له، اقرارا بواحدانيته وإخلاصا لربوبيته وانه العالم بما تبطنه الضمائر وتنطوي عليه السرائر، وما تخفيه النفوس وماتختزن البحار وماتوارى الأسرار وماتغيض الأرحام وما تزداد وكل شيء عنده بمقدار لا توارى منه كلمة ولاتغيب غائبة، وما تسقط من ورقة من شجرة ولاحبة فى ظلمات الأرض ولا رطب ولا يابس إلا في كتاب مبين.
If Abu al-Hasan (may Allah be pleased with him) is as described regarding his excellent, sound doctrine among those knowledgeable in scholarship and criticism, and the great worshippers agree with him in most of his positions, and none disparage his creed except the ignorant and obstinate, then we must relate his creed exactly as it is, faithfully, and avoid adding or subtracting anything, leaving treachery aside, so that the true state of his correct creed in the fundamentals of religion may be known. So listen to what he mentioned at the beginning of his book which he named "al-Ibanah". He said: Praise be to Allah, the One, the Unique, the Almighty, the Glorious, unique in Oneness, glorified in glorification, whom the attributes of servants cannot reach, who has no like or equal, the Originator and Repeater, exalted above the [desert?] and children, sanctified from touching women; He has no intimacy to be attained, and no peer by whom examples are set for Him. He has never ceased to be described as eternal and powerful, and He continues to be All-Knowing, All-Aware. His knowledge preceded all things, and His will penetrated them, so the hidden things of matters do not escape Him, nor do the vicissitudes of time change Him, nor does any fatigue or weariness or exhaustion or hardship befall Him in creating anything He created. He created all things by His power, arranged them by His will, subdued them by His omnipotence, and humbled them by His might. So the arrogant are humbled by His greatness, and the haughty submit to the greatness of His lordship, and those who test [Him] are cut off from penetrating His knowledge. Necks are humbled, and the intellects of the intelligent fly in His dominion. The seven heavens stand by His word, the earth the bed is settled, the firm mountains are fixed, the blustering winds blow, the clouds travel in the sky, and the seas stand at their boundaries. He is a subjugating God, to whom the honored submit and the exalted humble themselves, and the worlds submit willingly or unwillingly to Him. We praise Him as He praised Himself, and as He is worthy, our Lord. We seek His aid as one who entrusts his affair to Him and acknowledges that there is no refuge or sanctuary from Him except to Him. We seek His forgiveness as one who confesses his sin and acknowledges his mistake. And we bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, with no partner, acknowledging His Oneness and devoting worship to His Lordship; and that He knows what innermost consciences hide, what secrets contain, what souls conceal, what the seas treasure, what the hidden things hold, what wombs diminish and what they increase, and everything with Him is in measure. Not a word is hidden from Him, and no absent thing is absent [from Him]. Not a leaf falls from a tree, nor a seed in the darkness of the earth, nor anything moist or dry, except it is in a clear Book.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage serves as Ibn Asakir's justification for quoting al-Ash'ari's creed verbatim. He first establishes al-Ash'ari's reliability and orthodoxy. Since he is universally recognized by scholars and worshippers, his creed must be transmitted faithfully without alteration. Then Ibn Asakir begins quoting al-Ash'ari's book "al-Ibanah". The quotation starts with a standard Islamic doxology praising Allah's uniqueness, transcendence, and power. Allah is described as one, unique, almighty, glorious, unique in oneness. He is beyond the attributes of His creatures, having no likeness. He is exalted above having offspring or being associated with women. He has no peer. He is eternally powerful and knowing. His knowledge encompasses all things, His will executes, nothing escapes Him. He is not affected by time or fatigue. He creates all things by His power and manages them by His will and subjugates them. All creation, from the heavens to the earth, is under His command. He controls winds, clouds, seas. All creatures submit to Him. Then the doxology turns to praise, seeking aid, and forgiveness, and witnessing to tawhid. It then describes Allah's comprehensive knowledge of all hidden and manifest things, down to the falling of a leaf. Everything is recorded in a clear book.

الابانة
معتقده

According to Ibn Asakir, why must al-Ash'ari's creed be transmitted exactly as it is?
A) Because al-Ash'ari was a famous scholar.
B) Because only the ignorant oppose him, and his creed is sound.
C) Because it is from al-Ibanah.
D) Because he is the founder of the Ash'ari school.

Ibn Asakir insists on verbatim transmission of al-Ash'ari's creed because scholarly consensus confirms its orthodoxy, and any alteration would be a betrayal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you share Islamic knowledge, especially about Allah's attributes, do you ensure you are transmitting exactly what the scholars have said, or do you paraphrase in ways that might subtly distort the meaning? What specific step will you take this week to be more precise in your transmission?

Ibn Asakir says only the ignorant and obstinate disparage al-Ash'ari's creed. Is there any area of aqeedah you have dismissed without proper investigation? What will you do to seek the truth about that belief?

Al-Ash'ari's Opening Doxology from al-Ibanah
Al-Ash'ari begins his book al-Ibanah with a doxology praising Allah's transcendence and attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key themes of al-Ash'ari's statement of creed: divine oneness, transcendence, eternal attributes, creative power, and comprehensive knowledge.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's creed begins with a powerful affirmation of Allah's absolute uniqueness and transcendence.

Ibn Asakir now presents the actual text of al-Ash'ari's creed from the beginning of al-Ibanah. This passage is a rich theological doxology that covers the core tenets of Sunni Islam: tawhid, divine attributes, and Allah's sovereignty over all creation. As you read, notice how every phrase emphasizes that Allah is beyond all human limitations.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic doxology aloud
Read the Arabic passage slowly, appreciating its rhythm and repetition. Then read the translation.
This is a statement of praise (hamd) that sets the tone for the entire creed.
2
Identify the main themes
List the attributes of Allah that are mentioned: Oneness, uniqueness, transcendence, power, knowledge, will, etc. Group them into categories.
Look for phrases like 'جل عن' (exalted above) and 'لم يزل' (has not ceased).
3
Analyze the structure
Notice the flow from praise to negation of defects, to affirmation of attributes, to descriptions of creation, to testimony of faith.
The passage moves from Allah's essence to His actions to human response.
4
Connect to later Ash'ari theology
Consider how this passage lays the foundation for discussions on divine attributes and anthropomorphism. Why does al-Ash'ari stress that Allah is unlike creation?
This is a key point in refuting anthropomorphism (tashbih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا كان أبو الحسن رضى الله عنه كما ذكر عنه من حسن مستوصب المذهب عند أهل المعرفة بالعلم والانتقاد يوافقه في أكثر ما يذهب إليه أكابر العباد ولا يقدح في معتقده غير أهل الجهل والعناد فلابد ان نحكى عنه معتقده على وجهه بالامانة ونجتنب ان نريد فيه أو ننقص منه تركا للخيانة ليعلم حقيقة حاله في صحة عقيدته في أصول الديانة فاسمع ماذكره في أول كتابه الذي سماه بالابانة فإنه قال الحمد لله الأحد الواحد العزيز الماجد المتفرد بالتوحيد المتمجد بالتمجيد، الذي لا تبلغه صفات العبيد وليس له مثل ولانديد وهو المبدى المعيد، جل عن الصاحية والأبناء وتقدس عن ملامسة النساء فليست له عرة تنال ولاحد تضرب له فيه الأمثال لم يزل بصفاته أولا قديرا ولا يزال عالما خبيرا، سبق الأشياء علمه ونفذت فيها إرادته فلم تعزب عنه خفيات الأمور، ولم تغيره سوالف صروف الدهور، ولم يلحقه في خلق شيء مما خلق كلال ولا تعب ولامسه لغوب ولانصب خلق الأشياء بقدرته ودبرها بمشيئته وقهرها بجبروته، وذللها بعزته فذل لعظمته المتكبرون، واستكان لعظم ربوبيته المتعظمون وانقطع دون الرسوخ في علمه الممترون وذلت له الرقاب وتارت فى ملكوته فطن ذوى الألباب، وقامت بكلمته السموات السبع واستقرت الأرض المهاد وثبتت الجبال الرواسي وجرت الرياح اللواقع، وسار في جو السماء السحاب وقامت على حدودها البحار وهو إله قاهر يخضع له المعززون ويخشع له المترفعون ويدين طوعا وكرها له العالمون، نحمده كما حمد نفسه وكما ربنا له أهل ونستعينه استعانة من فوض أمره إليه وأقر أنه لا ملجأ ولا منجى منه إلا إليه ونستغفره استغفار مقر بذنبه معترف بخطيئته ونشهد ان لا إله إلا الله وحده لاشريك له، اقرارا بواحدانيته وإخلاصا لربوبيته وانه العالم بما تبطنه الضمائر وتنطوي عليه السرائر، وما تخفيه النفوس وماتختزن البحار وماتوارى الأسرار وماتغيض الأرحام وما تزداد وكل شيء عنده بمقدار لا توارى منه كلمة ولاتغيب غائبة، وما تسقط من ورقة من شجرة ولاحبة فى ظلمات الأرض ولا رطب ولا يابس إلا في كتاب مبين.
If Abu al-Hasan (may Allah be pleased with him) is as described regarding his excellent, sound doctrine among those knowledgeable in scholarship and criticism, and the great worshippers agree with him in most of his positions, and none disparage his creed except the ignorant and obstinate, then we must relate his creed exactly as it is, faithfully, and avoid adding or subtracting anything, leaving treachery aside, so that the true state of his correct creed in the fundamentals of religion may be known. So listen to what he mentioned at the beginning of his book which he named "al-Ibanah". He said: Praise be to Allah, the One, the Unique, the Almighty, the Glorious, unique in Oneness, glorified in glorification, whom the attributes of servants cannot reach, who has no like or equal, the Originator and Repeater, exalted above the [desert?] and children, sanctified from touching women; He has no intimacy to be attained, and no peer by whom examples are set for Him. He has never ceased to be described as eternal and powerful, and He continues to be All-Knowing, All-Aware. His knowledge preceded all things, and His will penetrated them, so the hidden things of matters do not escape Him, nor do the vicissitudes of time change Him, nor does any fatigue or weariness or exhaustion or hardship befall Him in creating anything He created. He created all things by His power, arranged them by His will, subdued them by His omnipotence, and humbled them by His might. So the arrogant are humbled by His greatness, and the haughty submit to the greatness of His lordship, and those who test [Him] are cut off from penetrating His knowledge. Necks are humbled, and the intellects of the intelligent fly in His dominion. The seven heavens stand by His word, the earth the bed is settled, the firm mountains are fixed, the blustering winds blow, the clouds travel in the sky, and the seas stand at their boundaries. He is a subjugating God, to whom the honored submit and the exalted humble themselves, and the worlds submit willingly or unwillingly to Him. We praise Him as He praised Himself, and as He is worthy, our Lord. We seek His aid as one who entrusts his affair to Him and acknowledges that there is no refuge or sanctuary from Him except to Him. We seek His forgiveness as one who confesses his sin and acknowledges his mistake. And we bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, with no partner, acknowledging His Oneness and devoting worship to His Lordship; and that He knows what innermost consciences hide, what secrets contain, what souls conceal, what the seas treasure, what the hidden things hold, what wombs diminish and what they increase, and everything with Him is in measure. Not a word is hidden from Him, and no absent thing is absent [from Him]. Not a leaf falls from a tree, nor a seed in the darkness of the earth, nor anything moist or dry, except it is in a clear Book.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage serves as Ibn Asakir's justification for quoting al-Ash'ari's creed verbatim. He first establishes al-Ash'ari's reliability and orthodoxy. Since he is universally recognized by scholars and worshippers, his creed must be transmitted faithfully without alteration. Then Ibn Asakir begins quoting al-Ash'ari's book "al-Ibanah". The quotation starts with a standard Islamic doxology praising Allah's uniqueness, transcendence, and power. Allah is described as one, unique, almighty, glorious, unique in oneness. He is beyond the attributes of His creatures, having no likeness. He is exalted above having offspring or being associated with women. He has no peer. He is eternally powerful and knowing. His knowledge encompasses all things, His will executes, nothing escapes Him. He is not affected by time or fatigue. He creates all things by His power and manages them by His will and subjugates them. All creation, from the heavens to the earth, is under His command. He controls winds, clouds, seas. All creatures submit to Him. Then the doxology turns to praise, seeking aid, and forgiveness, and witnessing to tawhid. It then describes Allah's comprehensive knowledge of all hidden and manifest things, down to the falling of a leaf. Everything is recorded in a clear book.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Ash'ari's creed contains anthropomorphic elements, but the passage repeatedly emphasizes transcendence and denies any likeness.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari explicitly states that Allah is 'exalted above children and touching women' and 'has no like or equal', affirming absolute transcendence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does al-Ash'ari describe Allah's relationship to women and children?

C) He is similar to human fathers.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's opening doxology affirms Allah's absolute uniqueness, transcendence, eternal attributes, creative power, and comprehensive knowledge, forming the basis of Sunni creed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'Praise be to Allah', do you truly feel that your praise is adequate for a God whose attributes are beyond all comparison? Or do you slip into thinking of Him as a powerful human? This passage shatters that image. What specific phrase from this doxology will you repeat daily to correct your concept of God?
?
The text says that the arrogant are humbled and the haughty submit to His greatness. Where in your life do you still hold onto pride, resisting the reality that you are completely dependent on Him? Write down one area of your life you haven't submitted and commit to surrendering it today.
?
You just read that not a leaf falls without His knowledge, and everything is recorded. Does this fill you with awe or anxiety? If you live as if your smallest acts are observed, how would your next hour change? Commit to one act of obedience now, knowing it is recorded.

The Sunni Methodology: Adherence to Revelation and the Salaf
Ibn Asakir responds to a question by stating the Sunni methodological commitment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni methodological principle of adhering to the Qur'an, Sunnah, and the way of the righteous predecessors, with special emphasis on Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal.

Core Idea
The Sunni creed is defined by submission to revelation and the path of the Salaf.

The passage opens with a hypothetical questioner challenging the rejection of various heretical sects and asking for a clear statement of the Sunni position. The response begins by laying out the foundational methodology: absolute adherence to the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Prophet, and the transmissions of the Companions, Successors, and hadith imams. This sets the stage for the creed that follows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
Read the opening question: a challenge to 'deny the sayings of the heretical sects' and then 'inform us of your saying and religion.' Understand the polemical setting.
The questioner is not necessarily hostile but represents a request for clear doctrine.
2
Analyze the answer's structure
Notice the answer begins with methodology before listing beliefs. The method is 'adherence to the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of His Prophet and what has been transmitted from the early generations.'
This is a statement of hermeneutical principle: revelation and tradition are the sources.
3
Examine the role of Ahmad ibn Hanbal
The passage singles out Ahmad ibn Hanbal as the exemplary imam who upheld the truth amid widespread deviation. Note the praise and the claim that his way is the Sunni way.
This highlights the Ash'ari/Maturidi-Salafi overlap at this point in history.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself: why is it important for Ibn Asakir to begin with methodology? The creed itself will be built on these sources; the methodology justifies the content.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل قد أنكرتم قول المعتزلة والقدرية والجهمية والحرورية والرافضة والمرجئة فعرفونا قولكم الذي به تقولون وديانتكم التي بها تدينون قيل له قولنا الذي به نقول وديانتنا التي ندين بها التمسك بكتاب الله وسنة نبيه صلى الله عليه وسلم وما روي عن الصحابة والتابعين وأئمة الحديث ونحن بذلك معتصمون وبما كان عليه أحمد بن حنبل نضر الله وجهه ورفع درجته وأجزل مثوبته قائلون ولمن خالف قوله قوله مجانبون لأنه الإمام الفاضل والرئيس الكامل، الذي أبان به الحق عند ظهور الضلال وأوضح به المنهاج وقمع به بدع المبتدعين وزيّغ الزائغين وشكّ الشاكين فرحمة الله عليه من إمام مقدم وكبير مفهم وعلى جميع أئمة المسلمين. وجملة قولنا أن نقر بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله وما جاء من عند الله وما رواه الثقات عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا نرد من ذلك شيئًا وأن إله واحد فرد صمد لا إله غيره ولم يتخذ صاحبة ولا ولدًا وأن محمدًا عبده ورسوله وأن الجنة والنار حق وأن الساعة آتية لا ريب فيها وأن الله يبعث من في القبور وأن الله استوى على عرشه كما قال (الرحمن على العرش استوى) وأن له وجهًا كما قال (ويبقى وجه ربك ذو الجلال والإكرام) وأن له يدا كما قال (بل يداه مبسوطتان) وقال (لما خلقت بيدي) وأن له عينًا بلا كيف كما قال (تجري بأعيننا) وأن من زعم أن الله غيره كان ضالا وأن الله علمًا كما قال (أنزله بعلمه) وقوله (وما تحمل من أنثى ولا تضع إلا بعلمه) ونثبت أن الله قدرة كما قال (أولم يروا أن الله)
If a questioner says: 'You have denied the sayings of the Mu'tazila, the Qadariyya, the Jahmiyya, the Haruriyya, the Rafida, and the Murji'a; so inform us of your saying by which you speak and your religion by which you practice.' It is said to him: 'Our saying by which we speak and our religion by which we practice is adherence to the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of His Prophet (peace be upon him) and what has been transmitted from the Companions, the Successors, and the imams of hadith. We cling to that, and we follow what was followed by Ahmad ibn Hanbal—may Allah brighten his face, raise his rank, and multiply his reward—and we dissociate from whoever contradicts his statement, because he is the virtuous imam and the perfect leader, through whom Allah made the truth manifest at the time of the spread of misguidance, clarified the path, suppressed the innovations of the innovators, scattered the deviants, and confounded the doubters. So the mercy of Allah be upon him as a leading imam and a great teacher, and upon all the imams of the Muslims. The summary of our say is: we affirm Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, and what has come from Allah and what the trustworthy have transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him); we reject none of that. And that He is one God, unique, self-sufficient, no god but Him; He has not taken a companion nor a son. And that Muhammad is His servant and messenger. And that Paradise and Hell are true, and that the Hour is coming, no doubt in it, and that Allah will resurrect those in the graves. And that Allah is established over His Throne as He said: "The Most Merciful is established over the Throne" (Q 20:5). And that He has a face, as He said: "And the face of your Lord will remain, full of majesty and honor" (Q 55:27). And that He has a hand, as He said: "But both His hands are outstretched" (Q 5:64) and He said: "When I created with My hands" (Q 38:75). And that He has an eye without modality, as He said: "Sailing under Our eyes" (Q 54:14). And that whoever claims that Allah is other than that is misguided. And that Allah has knowledge, as He said: "He sent it down with His knowledge" (Q 4:166) and His saying: "No female conceives nor gives birth except with His knowledge" (Q 35:11). And we affirm that Allah has power, as He said: "Do they not see that Allah..."
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. A hypothetical questioner asks: 'You have rejected the views of the various heretical sects; now tell us your own position and religion.' The answer presents the Sunni creed, beginning with the statement that their religion is adherence to the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Prophet, and the transmissions of the early generations and the hadith scholars. They particularly follow the way of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, whom they praise extravagantly. The creed then enumerates specific articles: belief in Allah, angels, books, messengers, and all authentic transmissions; affirmation of the oneness of Allah, that He is unique and has no partner or child; belief in Muhammad as servant and messenger; belief in Paradise, Hell, the Hour, and resurrection; and affirmation of divine attributes including istiwa' (establishment over the Throne), face, hands, eyes, knowledge, and power—all without modality (bila kayf). The passage concludes with a warning that whoever claims Allah is 'other than that' is misguided. The last sentence is cut off, but it would likely reaffirm Allah's power.

Key Terms
أهل السنة
أحمد بن حنبل
التمسك بكتاب الله وسنة نبيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first thing the answer emphasizes in response to the questioner?
A) The names of the heretical sects
B) The importance of reason in theology
C) Adherence to the Book, Sunnah, and early transmissions
D) The superiority of Ahmad ibn Hanbal over all other imams

Key Takeaway
The Sunni creed is rooted in exclusive reliance on revelation and the authentic tradition of the early Muslim community, epitomized by Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are faced with a difficult decision, do you instinctively turn to the Qur'an and authentic Sunnah, or do you rely more on your own reasoning or the opinion of a popular scholar? What does that reveal about your true methodology?
?
If someone asked you to define your creed, would you immediately point to the sources mentioned in this passage (Qur'an, Sunnah, and the way of the Salaf), or would you describe a set of beliefs you've picked up without checking their foundation?
?
Are there any areas of your life where you have prioritized cultural norms or personal desires over clear revelation? What is one concrete step you can take today to align yourself more closely with the methodology of the Salaf?

The Sunni Creed: Fundamental Articles of Faith
Ibn Asakir enumerates the fundamental articles of the Sunni creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the core articles of the Sunni creed as presented by Ibn Asakir: belief in Allah, angels, books, messengers, the afterlife, and resurrection.

Core Idea
Faith in the unseen includes angels, scriptures, prophets, the Last Day, and bodily resurrection.

After establishing the methodological commitment to revelation and the way of the Salaf, Ibn Asakir now summarizes the essential beliefs of the Sunni creed. These are not presented as theological proofs but as affirmations of what has been revealed and authentically transmitted. The list begins with belief in Allah, then expands to encompass all the major articles of Islamic faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage aloud
Read the Arabic passage slowly, noticing each article of faith introduced with 'أن' (that...). This is a creedal declaration.
The repetition of 'وأن' creates a rhythmic enumeration of beliefs.
2
List the articles
Identify each distinct article: belief in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, whatever comes from Allah, whatever is authentically transmitted from the Prophet, rejection of none, affirmation of Tawhid (oneness), denial of partner and son, Muhammad as servant and messenger, Paradise and Hell as true, the Hour as coming, and resurrection.
Some might combine 'belief in Allah' with 'Tawhid' which is mentioned separately.
3
Understand the sequence
Notice the logical flow: from the broadest belief in Allah and His messengers to specific eschatological events. The sequence moves from the divine to the prophetic to the afterlife.
4
Ponder the rejection clause
The passage includes 'لا نرد من ذلك شيئًا' – we reject none of it. This emphasizes the Sunni commitment to accepting all revealed truths without selective rejection.
This contrasts with the sects mentioned earlier who reject parts of revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل قد أنكرتم قول المعتزلة والقدرية والجهمية والحرورية والرافضة والمرجئة فعرفونا قولكم الذي به تقولون وديانتكم التي بها تدينون قيل له قولنا الذي به نقول وديانتنا التي ندين بها التمسك بكتاب الله وسنة نبيه صلى الله عليه وسلم وما روي عن الصحابة والتابعين وأئمة الحديث ونحن بذلك معتصمون وبما كان عليه أحمد بن حنبل نضر الله وجهه ورفع درجته وأجزل مثوبته قائلون ولمن خالف قوله قوله مجانبون لأنه الإمام الفاضل والرئيس الكامل، الذي أبان به الحق عند ظهور الضلال وأوضح به المنهاج وقمع به بدع المبتدعين وزيّغ الزائغين وشكّ الشاكين فرحمة الله عليه من إمام مقدم وكبير مفهم وعلى جميع أئمة المسلمين. وجملة قولنا أن نقر بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله وما جاء من عند الله وما رواه الثقات عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا نرد من ذلك شيئًا وأن إله واحد فرد صمد لا إله غيره ولم يتخذ صاحبة ولا ولدًا وأن محمدًا عبده ورسوله وأن الجنة والنار حق وأن الساعة آتية لا ريب فيها وأن الله يبعث من في القبور وأن الله استوى على عرشه كما قال (الرحمن على العرش استوى) وأن له وجهًا كما قال (ويبقى وجه ربك ذو الجلال والإكرام) وأن له يدا كما قال (بل يداه مبسوطتان) وقال (لما خلقت بيدي) وأن له عينًا بلا كيف كما قال (تجري بأعيننا) وأن من زعم أن الله غيره كان ضالا وأن الله علمًا كما قال (أنزله بعلمه) وقوله (وما تحمل من أنثى ولا تضع إلا بعلمه) ونثبت أن الله قدرة كما قال (أولم يروا أن الله)
If a questioner says: 'You have denied the sayings of the Mu'tazila, the Qadariyya, the Jahmiyya, the Haruriyya, the Rafida, and the Murji'a; so inform us of your saying by which you speak and your religion by which you practice.' It is said to him: 'Our saying by which we speak and our religion by which we practice is adherence to the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of His Prophet (peace be upon him) and what has been transmitted from the Companions, the Successors, and the imams of hadith. We cling to that, and we follow what was followed by Ahmad ibn Hanbal—may Allah brighten his face, raise his rank, and multiply his reward—and we dissociate from whoever contradicts his statement, because he is the virtuous imam and the perfect leader, through whom Allah made the truth manifest at the time of the spread of misguidance, clarified the path, suppressed the innovations of the innovators, scattered the deviants, and confounded the doubters. So the mercy of Allah be upon him as a leading imam and a great teacher, and upon all the imams of the Muslims. The summary of our say is: we affirm Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, and what has come from Allah and what the trustworthy have transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him); we reject none of that. And that He is one God, unique, self-sufficient, no god but Him; He has not taken a companion nor a son. And that Muhammad is His servant and messenger. And that Paradise and Hell are true, and that the Hour is coming, no doubt in it, and that Allah will resurrect those in the graves. And that Allah is established over His Throne as He said: "The Most Merciful is established over the Throne" (Q 20:5). And that He has a face, as He said: "And the face of your Lord will remain, full of majesty and honor" (Q 55:27). And that He has a hand, as He said: "But both His hands are outstretched" (Q 5:64) and He said: "When I created with My hands" (Q 38:75). And that He has an eye without modality, as He said: "Sailing under Our eyes" (Q 54:14). And that whoever claims that Allah is other than that is misguided. And that Allah has knowledge, as He said: "He sent it down with His knowledge" (Q 4:166) and His saying: "No female conceives nor gives birth except with His knowledge" (Q 35:11). And we affirm that Allah has power, as He said: "Do they not see that Allah..."
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. A hypothetical questioner asks: 'You have rejected the views of the various heretical sects; now tell us your own position and religion.' The answer presents the Sunni creed, beginning with the statement that their religion is adherence to the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Prophet, and the transmissions of the early generations and the hadith scholars. They particularly follow the way of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, whom they praise extravagantly. The creed then enumerates specific articles: belief in Allah, angels, books, messengers, and all authentic transmissions; affirmation of the oneness of Allah, that He is unique and has no partner or child; belief in Muhammad as servant and messenger; belief in Paradise, Hell, the Hour, and resurrection; and affirmation of divine attributes including istiwa' (establishment over the Throne), face, hands, eyes, knowledge, and power—all without modality (bila kayf). The passage concludes with a warning that whoever claims Allah is 'other than that' is misguided. The last sentence is cut off, but it would likely reaffirm Allah's power.

The Sunni Creed: Affirming Divine Attributes without Modality
Ibn Asakir affirms specific divine attributes from the Qur'an with the qualification 'bila kayf'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on divine attributes: affirming the attributes mentioned in the Qur'an (istīwā', face, hands, eyes, knowledge, power) without asking how (bila kayf).

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are affirmed as He described them, without modality or resemblance.

Following the general articles of faith, Ibn Asakir now addresses a critical point of contention in early Islamic theology: the nature of divine attributes. He affirms specific attributes mentioned in the Qur'an—such as istīwā' (establishment over the Throne), face, hands, eyes, knowledge, and power—but explicitly states that they are 'without modality' (bila kayf). This passage defends the Sunni approach of affirming what Allah has said about Himself without delving into how or likening Him to creation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the attributes
Read through the passage and list each attribute that is mentioned: istīwā', face, hands, eyes, knowledge, power. Notice that each is supported by a Qur'anic verse.
The passage is cut off but the pattern is clear.
2
Note the phrase 'bila kayf'
The passage explicitly says 'بلا كيف' (without modality) for the eye, and the same principle applies to the other attributes. This is the key phrase that distinguishes Sunni theology from anthropomorphism.
Ibn Asakir is part of the Ash'ari tradition which affirms attributes but denies modality.
3
Examine the warning
The passage states that 'whoever claims that Allah is other than that is misguided.' This indicates that denying or misrepresenting these attributes is a deviation from the creed.
4
Reflect on the proof texts
Each attribute is anchored in a specific Qur'anic verse (e.g., 'الرحمن على العرش استوى'). Notice that the passage does not interpret the verses metaphorically but affirms them as they are.
The Sunni approach is to accept the literal wording while affirming that Allah is unlike creation.

Love of the Salaf and the Rightly-Guided Caliphs
Ibn Asakir states Sunni creed on the Salaf, caliphate, and Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position regarding love for the Salaf, the order and status of the four caliphs, and the proper attitude toward the Companions.

Core Idea
Loving the Salaf and affirming the caliphate of prophethood are core Sunni beliefs.

Ibn Asakir, in his defense of Sunni orthodoxy, sets forth the creed concerning the Companions. This passage establishes the duty to love the early Muslims, the correct order of the caliphs, and the principle of refraining from disputes among the Companions. It is a concise summary of Sunni belief on these matters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice the author's direct style and the sequence of beliefs.
The passage is a creedal statement, not an argument.
2
Identify the three main sections
The passage covers: 1) love for the Salaf, 2) the four caliphs in order, 3) testimony for the ten promised Paradise and refraining from disputes.
Each section is introduced with specific Arabic phrases.
3
Understand the phrase 'caliphate of prophethood'
Ibn Asakir explicitly states that the caliphate of the four imams is 'khilafat al-nubuwwa' (caliphate of prophethood). This means their rule is a continuation of the prophetic mission, not mere political power.
This phrase is a key Sunni doctrine.
4
Reflect on refraining from disputes
The passage advises silence on conflicts among the Companions. Consider why this is important for maintaining unity and respect for the Salaf.
This is a practical application of love for the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وندين بحب السلف الذين اختارهم لصحبة نبيه ونثنى عليهم بما اثنى الله عليهم ونتولاهم ونقول ان الامام بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أبو بكر رضى الله عنه وأن الله تعالى أعزّ به الدين وأظهره على المرتدين، وقدمه المسلمون للإمامة كما قدمه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم للصلاة ثم عمر ابن الخطاب رضى الله عنه، ثم عثمان نضر الله وجهه قتله قاتلوه ظلماً وعدواناً، ثم على بن أبي طالب رضي الله عنه . فهؤلاء الأئمة بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وخلافتهم خلافة النبوة، ونشهد للعشرة بالجنة الذين شهد لهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ونتولى سائر أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ونكف عما شجر بينهم، وندين الله أن الأئمة الأربعة راشدون مهديون فضلاء لايوازيهم في الفضل غيرهم
And we hold by love of the predecessors whom He chose for the companionship of His Prophet, and we praise them with what Allah praised them, and we love them. And we say that the Imam after the Messenger of Allah ﷺ is Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, and that Allah Almighty strengthened religion through him and made him prevail over the apostates, and the Muslims put him forward for the imamate just as the Messenger of Allah ﷺ put him forward for prayer. Then Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him. Then Uthman, may Allah brighten his face; his killers killed him wrongfully and aggressively. Then Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him. So these are the imams after the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, and their caliphate is the caliphate of prophethood. And we testify for the ten (Companions) of Paradise, whom the Messenger of Allah ﷺ testified for. And we love the rest of the Companions of the Prophet ﷺ, and we refrain from (discussing) what happened between them. And we declare before Allah that the four imams are rightly-guided, guided, virtuous; none equals them in virtue.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a statement of Sunni belief regarding the Companions and the caliphate. It begins by affirming love for the Salaf (the early Muslims) and praising them as Allah praised them. Then it states the order of the caliphs after the Prophet: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali, emphasizing that their caliphate is a continuation of prophethood. It mentions that Abu Bakr was put forward for prayer by the Prophet, and the Muslims followed suit. For Uthman, it notes his unjust killing. For Ali, it simply states his name. The passage then affirms testifying that the ten Companions promised Paradise will enter it, and it adopts a position of refraining from discussing disputes among the Companions. Finally, it declares that the four rightly-guided caliphs are unparalleled in virtue.

Correction: The text asserts it is 'the caliphate of prophethood', indicating a religious and spiritual continuity from the Prophet.

The Early Alliance and Split Between Hanbalis and Ash'aris
Ibn 'Asakir recounts the early cooperation of Hanbalis and Ash'aris against innovation and later divergence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical relationship between the Hanbali and Ash'ari schools, including their early cooperation against innovation and the eventual split.

Core Idea
Hanbalis and Ash'aris were once united against innovation; the split was caused by extremists.

Ibn 'Asakir, a renowned Shafi'i scholar, presents a nuanced historical account of the relationship between the Hanbali and Ash'ari schools. He begins by affirming their early alliance in Baghdad, where the Hanbalis relied on Ash'ari theological expertise. This lesson traces that cooperation and the factors leading to its breakdown.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the tone of Ibn 'Asakir as he describes the alliance.
The passage uses a historical narrative style.
2
Identify the nature of the alliance
Identify how the Hanbalis supported themselves with the Ash'aris. What did they learn from them? How did they speak?
3
Understand the split and its cause
Locate where the text mentions the split. Who was involved? What was the result?
The split is attributed to extremists on both sides.
4
Reflect on the defense of Ahmad
Notice how Ibn 'Asakir defends Imam Ahmad from the actions of extremists. He quotes Ibn Shahin's saying about two righteous men being plagued by evil companions.
This shows the author's desire to protect the reputation of the Hanbali founder.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم تزل الحنابلة ببغداد في قديم الدهر على ممر الأوقات تعتضد بالأشعرية على أصحاب البدع لأنهم المتكلمون من أهل الاثبات فمن تكلم منهم فى الرد على مبتدع فبلسان الأشعرية يتكلم ومن حقق منهم في الأصول في مسألة فمنهم يتعلم، فلم يزالوا كذلك حتى حدث الاختلاف في زمن أبى نصر القشيرى ووزارة النظام ووقع بينهم الانحراف من بعضهم عن بعض، لانحلال النظام وعلي الجملة فلم يزل في الحنابلة طائفة تغلو في السنة وتدخل فيما لا يعنيها حبا للخفوف في الفتنة . ولا عار على أحمد رحمه الله من صنيعهم، وليس يتفق على ذلك رأى جميعهم ولهذا قال أبو حفص عمر بن أحمد بن عثمان بن شاهين وهو من أقران الدارقطني ومن أصحاب الحديث المتسننين ماقرأت على الشيخ أبي محمد عبد الكريم بن حمزة بن الخضر بدمشق، عن أبي محمد عبدالعزيز ابن أحمد قال حدثني أبو النجيب عبد الغفار بن عبد الواحد الأرموى، قال ثنا أبو ذر عبد بن أحمد الهروى قال سمعت ابن شاهين يقول رجلان صالحان بليا بأصحاب سوء جعفر بن محمد وأحمد بن حنبل، كتب إلى أبو القسم العكبرى يخبرني عن أبي المعالى عزيزى بن عبد الملك قال لما تم للهجرة مايتان وستون سنة رفعت أنواع البدع رؤسها وتسقت عوام الخلائق كؤوسها، حتى أصبحت آيات الدين منطمسة الآثار وأعلام الحق مندرسة لأخبار فاظهر الله سبحانه وتعالى ناصر الحق وناصر الخلق محيى السنن مرضى السنن الإمام الرضى الزكي أبا الحسن، سقى الله بماء الرحمة تربته وأعلى في غرفات الجنان درجته من أصل باذخ الذرى وشرف شامخ القوى وهو أبو موسى عبدالله بن قيس الأشعري صاحب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقاضيه والمستخلف من قبل الخلفاء الراشدين والأئمة المهديين أبى بكر وعمر وعثمان وعلى رضوان الله عليهم أجمعين على القضاء والصلوات والجيوش والامارة على المؤمنين وتعليم الشريعة للمسلمين، وكان زوج أم کلثوم بنت الفضل بن العباس بن عبد المطلب وهي أم أبي بردة بن أبى ) ۹ - تبيين كدب المفترى ) ۱۲۹
And the Hanbalis in Baghdad in ancient times, throughout the ages, continued to support themselves with the Ash'aris against the people of innovation, because they (the Ash'aris) were the theologians from among the people of affirmation. So whoever among them spoke in refutation of an innovator, he spoke with the tongue of the Ash'aris, and whoever among them verified an issue in the foundations, learned from them. They continued thus until disagreement occurred in the time of Abu Nasr al-Qushayri and the vizier Nizam al-Mulk, and deviation occurred among them, some from others, due to the dissolution of the system. And in general, there remained among the Hanbalis a faction that exaggerated in the Sunnah and intruded into what does not concern them, out of love for rushing into strife. And there is no shame on Ahmad (may Allah have mercy on him) from their doing, and not all of them agree on that opinion. For this reason, Abu Hafs 'Umar ibn Ahmad ibn 'Uthman ibn Shahin—who is of the peers of al-Daraqutni and one of the traditionists adhering to the Sunnah—said: I read to Sheikh Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-Karim ibn Hamza ibn al-Khudr in Damascus, from Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad, he said: Abu al-Najib 'Abd al-Ghaffar ibn 'Abd al-Wahid al-Armani informed me, he said: Abu Dharr 'Abd ibn Ahmad al-Harawi narrated to us, he said: I heard Ibn Shahin say: Two righteous men were plagued by evil companions: Ja'far ibn Muhammad and Ahmad ibn Hanbal. Abu al-Qasim al-'Ukbari wrote to me informing me from Abu al-Ma'ali 'Azizi ibn 'Abd al-Malik, he said: When two hundred and sixty years of the Hijra had passed, the types of innovation raised their heads and gave the common masses their cups to drink, until the signs of the religion became obliterated and the landmarks of truth became erased. Then Allah, Exalted and High, manifested the supporter of truth and the helper of creation, the reviver of the Sunnah, the one pleasing to the Sunnah, the Imam, the contented, the pure, Abu al-Hasan. May Allah water his grave with the rain of mercy and elevate his ranks in the gardens of Paradise, from an origin of lofty status and high honor, and he is Abu Musa 'Abdullah ibn Qays al-Ash'ari, the companion of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), his judge, and the deputy appointed by the Rightly Guided Caliphs and the guided Imams—Abu Bakr, 'Umar, 'Uthman, and 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with them all—over judgment, prayers, armies, leadership of the believers, and teaching the Shari'a to the Muslims. And he was the husband of Umm Kulthum bint al-Fadl ibn al-'Abbas ibn 'Abd al-Muttalib, who was the mother of Abu Burda ibn Abi ( ) 9 - Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari 129
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative that describes the relationship between the Hanbali and Ash'ari schools. Ibn 'Asakir begins by stating that the Hanbalis of Baghdad had long relied on the Ash'aris for theological defense against innovators, because the Ash'aris were the skilled theologians among the people of affirmation (ahl al-ithbat). The Hanbalis would use the language of the Ash'aris when refuting innovators and learned the principles of theology from them. This cooperation continued until a split occurred in the time of Abu Nasr al-Qushayri and the vizier Nizam al-Mulk, leading to deviation among some. After this, a faction of Hanbalis became extreme in their adherence to the Sunnah, meddling in matters that did not concern them out of love for rushing into fitna. Ibn 'Asakir defends Ahmad ibn Hanbal from any blame for the actions of these extremists, noting that not all Hanbalis agreed with that faction. He supports this by quoting Ibn Shahin, who said that two righteous men, Ja'far al-Sadiq and Ahmad ibn Hanbal, were plagued by evil companions. Then, through another chain, he reports that around 260 AH, innovations became rampant until Allah raised Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as a defender of the truth and reviver of the Sunnah. The passage ends with a laudatory account of al-Ash'ari's lineage, tracing it to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, the companion of the Prophet, and notes his marriage to Umm Kulthum bint al-Fadl ibn al-'Abbas.

Key Terms
حنابلة
أشعرية
أبو نصر القشيري
النظام
ابن شاهين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume Hanbalis and Ash'aris were always opposed to each other.
Correction: This passage shows they were allies against innovation for centuries before a later split caused by extremists on both sides.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn 'Asakir, when did the split between the Hanbalis and Ash'aris occur?
A) In the time of Abu Nasr al-Qushayri and Nizam al-Mulk
B) After the death of Ahmad ibn Hanbal
C) During the Abbasid caliphate of al-Ma'mun
D) In the 4th century AH

Key Takeaway
The Hanbali-Ash'ari relationship was initially cooperative, and the later division was due to extremists on both sides, not the founders themselves.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see division among Muslims today, do you immediately blame one group's founder, or do you reflect on the extremists on both sides that may have caused it? What lesson from this passage would you apply to your own attitude towards different Muslim groups?
?
Have you ever exaggerated in following the Sunnah to the point of intruding into what does not concern you, out of love for rushing into fitna? How can you guard against becoming the 'evil companion' that plagues a righteous scholar?
?
Ibn 'Asakir says the Hanbalis learned from the Ash'aris in theological matters. Are you willing to learn from those of different schools when they have truth? What pride or prejudice holds you back from seeking knowledge wherever it is found?

The Rise of Imam al-Ash'ari as a Reviver of the Sunnah
Ibn 'Asakir recounts the historical context and emergence of Imam al-Ash'ari as a reviver.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical context of Imam al-Ash'ari's emergence as a reviver of the Sunnah in the face of widespread innovation.

Core Idea
Imam al-Ash'ari was raised by Allah to revive the Sunnah when innovations had spread.

In this second part of the passage, Ibn 'Asakir reports that around 260 AH, innovations had become rampant, obscuring the signs of religion. It was at this critical juncture that Allah manifested Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as a defender of truth and reviver of the Sunnah. This lesson explores that background and the noble lineage of al-Ash'ari.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the rise of innovations
Read the Arabic and translation describing the state of affairs in 260 AH. Notice the vivid language: 'innovations raised their heads' and 'gave the common masses their cups to drink.'
This sets the stage for the emergence of al-Ash'ari.
2
Identify the role of Imam al-Ash'ari
Find the description of al-Ash'ari as the 'supporter of truth,' 'helper of creation,' and 'reviver of the Sunnah.' Understand how he is presented as a divinely appointed figure.
3
Trace his noble lineage
Examine the lineage of al-Ash'ari as traced back to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, a companion of the Prophet. Note the mention of his marriage to Umm Kulthum bint al-Fadl ibn al-'Abbas.
This lineage elevates his status.
4
Reflect on the significance of this narrative
Consider why Ibn 'Asakir includes this detailed account. How does it serve to defend the Ash'ari school and establish its credentials?
It counters claims that Ash'ari theology is an innovation.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم تزل الحنابلة ببغداد في قديم الدهر على ممر الأوقات تعتضد بالأشعرية على أصحاب البدع لأنهم المتكلمون من أهل الاثبات فمن تكلم منهم فى الرد على مبتدع فبلسان الأشعرية يتكلم ومن حقق منهم في الأصول في مسألة فمنهم يتعلم، فلم يزالوا كذلك حتى حدث الاختلاف في زمن أبى نصر القشيرى ووزارة النظام ووقع بينهم الانحراف من بعضهم عن بعض، لانحلال النظام وعلي الجملة فلم يزل في الحنابلة طائفة تغلو في السنة وتدخل فيما لا يعنيها حبا للخفوف في الفتنة . ولا عار على أحمد رحمه الله من صنيعهم، وليس يتفق على ذلك رأى جميعهم ولهذا قال أبو حفص عمر بن أحمد بن عثمان بن شاهين وهو من أقران الدارقطني ومن أصحاب الحديث المتسننين ماقرأت على الشيخ أبي محمد عبد الكريم بن حمزة بن الخضر بدمشق، عن أبي محمد عبدالعزيز ابن أحمد قال حدثني أبو النجيب عبد الغفار بن عبد الواحد الأرموى، قال ثنا أبو ذر عبد بن أحمد الهروى قال سمعت ابن شاهين يقول رجلان صالحان بليا بأصحاب سوء جعفر بن محمد وأحمد بن حنبل، كتب إلى أبو القسم العكبرى يخبرني عن أبي المعالى عزيزى بن عبد الملك قال لما تم للهجرة مايتان وستون سنة رفعت أنواع البدع رؤسها وتسقت عوام الخلائق كؤوسها، حتى أصبحت آيات الدين منطمسة الآثار وأعلام الحق مندرسة لأخبار فاظهر الله سبحانه وتعالى ناصر الحق وناصر الخلق محيى السنن مرضى السنن الإمام الرضى الزكي أبا الحسن، سقى الله بماء الرحمة تربته وأعلى في غرفات الجنان درجته من أصل باذخ الذرى وشرف شامخ القوى وهو أبو موسى عبدالله بن قيس الأشعري صاحب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقاضيه والمستخلف من قبل الخلفاء الراشدين والأئمة المهديين أبى بكر وعمر وعثمان وعلى رضوان الله عليهم أجمعين على القضاء والصلوات والجيوش والامارة على المؤمنين وتعليم الشريعة للمسلمين، وكان زوج أم کلثوم بنت الفضل بن العباس بن عبد المطلب وهي أم أبي بردة بن أبى ) ۹ - تبيين كدب المفترى ) ۱۲۹
And the Hanbalis in Baghdad in ancient times, throughout the ages, continued to support themselves with the Ash'aris against the people of innovation, because they (the Ash'aris) were the theologians from among the people of affirmation. So whoever among them spoke in refutation of an innovator, he spoke with the tongue of the Ash'aris, and whoever among them verified an issue in the foundations, learned from them. They continued thus until disagreement occurred in the time of Abu Nasr al-Qushayri and the vizier Nizam al-Mulk, and deviation occurred among them, some from others, due to the dissolution of the system. And in general, there remained among the Hanbalis a faction that exaggerated in the Sunnah and intruded into what does not concern them, out of love for rushing into strife. And there is no shame on Ahmad (may Allah have mercy on him) from their doing, and not all of them agree on that opinion. For this reason, Abu Hafs 'Umar ibn Ahmad ibn 'Uthman ibn Shahin—who is of the peers of al-Daraqutni and one of the traditionists adhering to the Sunnah—said: I read to Sheikh Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-Karim ibn Hamza ibn al-Khudr in Damascus, from Abu Muhammad 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad, he said: Abu al-Najib 'Abd al-Ghaffar ibn 'Abd al-Wahid al-Armani informed me, he said: Abu Dharr 'Abd ibn Ahmad al-Harawi narrated to us, he said: I heard Ibn Shahin say: Two righteous men were plagued by evil companions: Ja'far ibn Muhammad and Ahmad ibn Hanbal. Abu al-Qasim al-'Ukbari wrote to me informing me from Abu al-Ma'ali 'Azizi ibn 'Abd al-Malik, he said: When two hundred and sixty years of the Hijra had passed, the types of innovation raised their heads and gave the common masses their cups to drink, until the signs of the religion became obliterated and the landmarks of truth became erased. Then Allah, Exalted and High, manifested the supporter of truth and the helper of creation, the reviver of the Sunnah, the one pleasing to the Sunnah, the Imam, the contented, the pure, Abu al-Hasan. May Allah water his grave with the rain of mercy and elevate his ranks in the gardens of Paradise, from an origin of lofty status and high honor, and he is Abu Musa 'Abdullah ibn Qays al-Ash'ari, the companion of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), his judge, and the deputy appointed by the Rightly Guided Caliphs and the guided Imams—Abu Bakr, 'Umar, 'Uthman, and 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with them all—over judgment, prayers, armies, leadership of the believers, and teaching the Shari'a to the Muslims. And he was the husband of Umm Kulthum bint al-Fadl ibn al-'Abbas ibn 'Abd al-Muttalib, who was the mother of Abu Burda ibn Abi ( ) 9 - Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari 129

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative that describes the relationship between the Hanbali and Ash'ari schools. Ibn 'Asakir begins by stating that the Hanbalis of Baghdad had long relied on the Ash'aris for theological defense against innovators, because the Ash'aris were the skilled theologians among the people of affirmation (ahl al-ithbat). The Hanbalis would use the language of the Ash'aris when refuting innovators and learned the principles of theology from them. This cooperation continued until a split occurred in the time of Abu Nasr al-Qushayri and the vizier Nizam al-Mulk, leading to deviation among some. After this, a faction of Hanbalis became extreme in their adherence to the Sunnah, meddling in matters that did not concern them out of love for rushing into fitna. Ibn 'Asakir defends Ahmad ibn Hanbal from any blame for the actions of these extremists, noting that not all Hanbalis agreed with that faction. He supports this by quoting Ibn Shahin, who said that two righteous men, Ja'far al-Sadiq and Ahmad ibn Hanbal, were plagued by evil companions. Then, through another chain, he reports that around 260 AH, innovations became rampant until Allah raised Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as a defender of the truth and reviver of the Sunnah. The passage ends with a laudatory account of al-Ash'ari's lineage, tracing it to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, the companion of the Prophet, and notes his marriage to Umm Kulthum bint al-Fadl ibn al-'Abbas.

?

Will you let that truth liberate you from excuses of inadequacy?

The Virtue of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari
Ibn Asakir cites lineage and hadith to assert al-Ash'ari's virtue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir uses a hadith and rational reasoning to establish the unique virtue of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
The hadith of Abu Musa points to virtue, but al-Ash'ari's deeds prove his unique station.

Ibn Asakir presents a biographical argument linking the Prophet's praise of the Yemenis to a specific descendant who fulfilled that praise. He combines a hadith with a rational deduction to assert that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari alone among Abu Musa's descendants refuted innovators. This lesson examines that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translations. Notice the chain of transmission and the key claim about al-Ash'ari's unique role.
The passage begins with a hadith and then makes a rational deduction.
2
Understand the hadith
The Prophet applies the Quranic verse to the Yemenis, who are the people of Abu Musa. See how this establishes the virtue of the lineage.
The hadith is from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari himself.
3
Grasp the rational deduction
Ibn Asakir asserts that by rational proofs, only al-Ash'ari among Abu Musa's descendants refuted heretics. Why is this significant?
This connects the general praise to a specific individual.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends by describing al-Ash'ari's success with rational and transmitted proofs. How does this support the earlier claim?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن موسى الأشعرى جد الإمام أبى الحسن الأشعرى، وروى دعلج بن أحمد عن عبد الله بن أحمد بن حنبل نبأ أبو معمر قال ثنا عبد الله بن ادريس عن أبيه سماك بن حرب عن عياض الأشعرى عن أبي موسى الأشعري قال قرئت عنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ( فسوف يأتى الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه ) فقال صلوات الله علیه وسلامه ( هم قومك يا أبا موسى أهل (اليمن) ومعلوم بأدلة العقول وبراهين الأصول أن أحدا من أولاد أبي موسى لم يرد على أصحاب الأباطيل ولم يبطل شبه أهل البدع والأضاليل، بحجج قاهرة من الكتاب والسنة ودلائل باهرة من الإجماع والقياس، إلا الإمام أبو الحسن الأشعرى وحديث أبي موسى دليل واضح على فضيلة الإمام أبي الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه فجاهد أعداء الحق وقمعهم وفرق كلمتهم وبدد جمعهم بالحجج القاهرة العقلية والأدلة الباهرة السمعية .
From Musa al-Ash'ari, the grandfather of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Da'laj ibn Ahmad narrated from 'Abd Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal: Abu Mu'ammar informed us: 'Abd Allah ibn Idris narrated to us from his father Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari who said: The Prophet recited upon us (then Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him) and said: They are your people, O Abu Musa, the people of Yemen. And it is known by rational proofs and fundamental evidences that none of the descendants of Abu Musa refuted the people of falsehood and invalidated the doubts of the people of innovation and misguidance with overwhelming proofs from the Book and Sunnah and clear evidences from consensus and analogy except Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. And the hadith of Abu Musa is a clear proof of the virtue of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him. He waged war against the enemies of truth and suppressed them, scattered their word and dispersed their assembly with overwhelming rational proofs and clear transmitted evidences.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a biographical statement establishing the lineage and virtue of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. It begins by mentioning his lineage from Musa al-Ash'ari, a companion, then quotes a hadith in which the Prophet identifies Musa al-Ash'ari's people (the Yemenis) as those whom Allah loves. The author then asserts that it is a known fact by rational proofs and fundamental evidences that among the descendants of Abu Musa, only Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari refuted the people of falsehood and invalidated the doubts of heretics using overwhelming proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, consensus (ijma'), and analogy (qiyas). The hadith itself is presented as a clear proof of al-Ash'ari's virtue. The passage concludes by describing how al-Ash'ari fought the enemies of truth, suppressed them, and scattered their gatherings with both rational proofs and transmitted evidences.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the hadith of Abu Musa directly praises al-Ash'ari by name.
Correction: The hadith praises the Yemenis generally; the passage uses it as a general proof of the virtue of his lineage, then deduces al-Ash'ari's unique merit from his actual achievements.

Key Takeaway

?

?
What concrete proof can you offer that you are among those whom Allah loves and who love Him—is it merely a claim, or do you actively wage jihad against falsehood as al-Ash'ari did?

Dream of Abu al-Qasim: Al-Ash'ari Proclaims His Madhhab True
A man sees al-Ash'ari in a dream who three times says his madhhab is true.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a dream narrative was used to affirm the truth of the Ash'ari school and the reasoning behind accepting such dreams as reliable.

Core Idea
Dreams of the righteous can convey truth, especially from a truthful person in the abode of truth.

This passage presents a vivid dream account in which Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari himself declares his madhhab true. It not only recounts the dream but also explicitly justifies why such a dream should be accepted: because al-Ash'ari was truthful in life and now resides in Paradise, where only truth is spoken. This reasoning reflects a broader theological principle about the reliability of dreams of the deceased righteous.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the dialogue and the triple repetition of the statement.
The repetition emphasizes the importance of the message.
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the dreamer (Abu al-Qasim), the setting (Damascus mosque), and the content of the dream (al-Ash'ari appears and says his madhhab is true three times).
3
Examine the narrator's justification
The narrator adds a verification: 'What he said to you is true, for he was truthful in speech, and he is in the abode of truth, so he only says the truth.' Note the two reasons given.
The 'abode of truth' (دار حق) refers to Paradise.
4
Reflect on the principle
Consider how this reasoning establishes a principle: the truthful deceased in Paradise only speak truth. How does this support accepting dream testimonies?
This is a specific form of hujjah (proof) for the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحكى لي بعض اصحابنا عن أبي القـسـم بن ابراهيم بن حسين الدقاق المعروف بالزبير رؤيا رآها فلقيته في الجامع بدمشق فسألته عن رؤياه وقلت له : بلغنى أنك رأيت الفقيه أبا الحسن رحمه في المنام فقال أى والذى قبض روحه لقد رأيته فى المنام كأنه ههنا وأشار إلى مكان من الجامع بقرب باب البرادة وخلفته وهو داخل إلى صدر المسجد فقال لي يا أبا القسم مذهب الأشعرى حق مذهب الأشعري حق مذهب الأشعرى حق ثم استيقظت فقلت له ما قال لك حق فانه كان صادق اللهجة وهو في دار حق فلا يقول إلا الحق .
And some of our companions narrated to me from Abu al-Qasim ibn Ibrahim ibn Husayn al-Daqqaq known as al-Zubayr a dream he saw. I met him in the mosque in Damascus and asked him about his dream, saying: 'It has reached me that you saw the jurist Abu al-Hasan (i.e., al-Ash'ari), may Allah have mercy on him, in a dream.' He said: 'Yes, by Him who took his soul, I saw him in a dream as if he was here' – and he pointed to a place in the mosque near Bab al-Barada – 'and I followed him and he entered the prayer hall, and he said to me: O Abu al-Qasim, the madhhab of al-Ash'ari is the truth, the madhhab of al-Ash'ari is the truth, the madhhab of al-Ash'ari is the truth. Then I woke up.' I said to him: 'What he said to you is true, for he was truthful in speech, and he is in the abode of truth, so he only says the truth.'
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is another dream testimony affirming the truth of the Ash'ari school. The narrator hears from a companion that Abu al-Qasim had seen Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari in a dream. He meets Abu al-Qasim in the Damascus mosque and asks him about it. Abu al-Qasim confirms the dream, describing how al-Ash'ari appeared in the mosque and three times declared: 'The madhhab of al-Ash'ari is the truth.' The narrator then adds his own verification: 'What he said to you is true, for he was truthful in speech, and he is in the abode of truth (i.e., Paradise), so he only says the truth.' This reasoning treats the dream as reliable because al-Ash'ari was truthful in life and now resides in the realm of truth, where lying is impossible.

Key Terms
مذهب الأشعري
حق
دار حق
صدق اللهجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dreams are not valid evidence for truth claims.
Correction: The passage argues that dreams of the deceased righteous can be accepted because they are truthful in life and reside in the abode of truth where lying is impossible.

Checkpoint

A) Once
B) Twice
C) Three times
D) Four times

Key Takeaway
The dream of al-Ash'ari affirming his madhhab is accepted as true because he was truthful in life and resides in the abode of truth, where only truth is spoken.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ash'ari's truthfulness in life made his dream testimony credible. How does your own truthfulness now affect what your words will mean in the next life? What are you saying today that you would be ashamed to repeat in Dar al-Haqq?
?
If you were to die and be asked about the truth of your beliefs, would your answer carry the same certainty as al-Ash'ari's? What foundation does your certainty stand on?
?
The dream confirms a school of thought. Is there a truth in your life that you have been avoiding, despite clear signs from the truthful ones? When will you stop and listen?

Al-Qushayri's Poem on Love for Abu Bakr and the Ash'ari Creed
Al-Qushayri's poem affirming love for Abu Bakr and Ash'ari creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Qushayri expressed his theological allegiance through poetry, affirming love for Abu Bakr and adherence to the Ash'ari school.

Core Idea
Two loves define the believer: love of Abu Bakr and love of Ash'ari theology.

This brief poem by the great scholar Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri captures the essence of his spiritual and theological commitments. In just two lines, he declares his unwavering love for Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and his adherence to the Ash'ari creed, distancing himself from anyone who criticizes these.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation

The poem is only two lines but carries deep meaning.

This reflects the importance of scholarly chains.

Why does al-Qushayri pair love for Abu Bakr with belief in the Ash'ari school? Consider how both represent foundational Sunni principles.
Love of the Companions and correct theology are inseparable.
4
Connect to the context
Al-Qushayri was a leading Ash'ari theologian and a Shafi'i jurist. This poem aligns his personal devotion with his scholarly identity.

Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a poem citation. Ibn Asakir records a chain of transmission leading to Imam al-Qushayri, who recites his own poem. The poem declares that two matters are fundamental to the speaker: love for Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (the first caliph) and adherence to the theological school of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. Anyone who criticizes these is disassociated from him. The poem thus asserts that true guidance combines devotion to the rightly-guided caliph and Ash'ari theology.
