ومنهم أبو بكر الجرجاني المعروف بالاسماعیلی رحمه أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم بن أبي بكر الكتبي قال انا أبو القسم اسماعيل بن مسعدة بن اسماعيل الجرجاني قال انا أبو القسم حمزة بن يوسف السهمى الجرجاني في تاريخ جرجان قال : أحمد بن إبراهيم بن اسماعيل بن العباس أبو بكر الاسماعيلي، الامام رحمه الله وبيض وجهه والحقه بعباده الصالحين توفى يوم السبت غرة رجب سنة احدى وسبعين وثلاثمائة وكان له اربع وتسعون سنة سمعت والدى أبا يعقوب يوسف ابن إبراهيم بن موسى يقول كان أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم الاسماعيلي بارا بوالديه لحقته بركة دعائهما، قال حمزة وسألني الوزير أبو الفضل جعفر بن الفضل بن الفرات بمصر عن أبي بكر الاسماعيلى وما صنف وجمع وعن سيرته فكنت اخبره بما صنف من الكتب وجمع من المسانيد والمقلين وتخريجه على كتاب محمد بن اسماعيل البخارى، وجميع سيرة فتعجب ذلك وقال لقد كان رزق من العلم والجاه وكان له صيت حسن، وقال حمزة سمعت أبا الحسن الدارقطنى الحافظ يقول كنت قد عزمت غير مرة أن أرحل إلى أبي بكر الاسماعيلى فلم ارزق، قال حمزة وكنت اذا حضرت مجلس الامام أبي بكر الاسماعيلى ورأيته لم يتفوه بشيء من تقسير خبر أو ضرب مثل أو حكاية أو بيت شعر أو نادرة أو غير ذلك من سائر العلوم إلا وتبادر جماعة من الغرباء وأهل البلد علقوا وكتبوا خصوصا أبو بكر البرقاني فإنه قلما كان يترك شيئا يجرى إلا وهو يكتب وكذلك أبو القسم الورثانى وأبو جعفر محمد بن علی بن دلان الجرجاني، والفضل بن أبي سعد الهدوى وأبو الفضل المخزومي البصرى وأبو سعد الماليني وأبو القسم عیسی بن عباد الدينوري ويحيى الابهرى وأحمد بن عبدالرحمن الشيرازي وأبو بكر الجرجاني، وعبدالرحمن السجزى وغيرهم رحمهم الله لا أحصى عددهم وما من يوم إلا وكان بحضرته من الغرباء الجوالين ممن يفهم ويحفظ مقدار اربعين أو خمسين نفسا وكنت اعلق عنه مقدار فهمى وحفظى وأنسخ مما علق عنه أبو بكر البرقاني وأبو جعفر بن دلان الجرجانی، أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم اسماعيل بن أحمد السمرقندي قال ثنا أبو اسحق إبراهيم بن على الفقيه قال : أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم بن اسماعيل بن العباس الاسماعيلي مات سنة نيف وسبعين وثلاثمائة وجمع بين الفقه والحديث ورياسة الدين والدنيا وصنف الصحيح واخذ عنه ابنه أبو سعد وفقهاء جرجان، وقال شيخنا القاضى الامام أبو الطيب الطبري رحمه الله دخلت جرجان قاصدا إليه وهو حى فمات قبل أن ألقاه، جمع بين الأصول والفقه والحديث وصنف صحيحا على شرط البخارى رحمه الله، يدل على فضل كثير لمن وقف عليه أخبرنا الشريف أبو بكر أحمد بن عبدالرحمن ابن أحمد المروزى الواعظ بدمشق قال قال لنا الشيخ الحافظ أبو نصر هبة الله ابن عبد الجبار بن فاخر بن معاذ بن أحمد بن محمد السجزي بسجستان : أبو بكر الاسماعيلى شيخ كبير جليل ثقة من الفقهاء والمحدثين في عصره يرجع إلى علم وافر ومعرفة بالحديث صادقة ومروءة ظاهرة وكانت إليه الرحلة في زمانه وهو أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم بن اسماعيل بن العباس الإسماعيلى الجرجاني روى عن أبي خليفة والمشايخ ولد سنة سبع وسبعين ومائتين ومات سنة احدى وسبعين وثلاثمائة
Among them is Abu Bakr al-Jurjani, known as al-Isma'ili, may Allah have mercy on him. We were informed by the Shaykh Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Bakr al-Katibi, who said: we were told by Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Mas'ada ibn Isma'il al-Jurjani, who said: we were told by Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf al-Sahmi al-Jurjani in the History of Jurjan, who said: Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-'Abbas Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, the Imam, may Allah have mercy on him, brighten his face, and join him with His righteous servants. He died on Saturday, the first of Rajab, in the year 371 AH, and he was ninety-four years old. I heard my father Abu Ya'qub Yusuf ibn Ibrahim ibn Musa say: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Isma'ili was dutiful to his parents and was blessed by their supplication. Hamza said: The vizier Abu al-Fadl Ja'far ibn al-Fadl ibn al-Furat asked me in Egypt about Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, what he authored, compiled, and his biography. So I informed him of the books he authored, the musnads and the 'less narrators' he compiled, his commentary on the book of Muhammad ibn Isma'il al-Bukhari, and all of his biography. He was amazed and said: He was indeed granted knowledge and status, and he had a good reputation. Hamza said: I heard Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni, the hafiz, say: I resolved more than once to travel to Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili but was not enabled. Hamza said: Whenever I attended the assembly of Imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili and saw him, he did not utter anything in explanation of a tradition, giving an example, a story, a line of poetry, a rare anecdote, or anything else from the various sciences, but a group of strangers and locals would immediately take notes and write, especially Abu Bakr al-Barqani, who hardly ever left anything spoken without writing it down, as well as Abu al-Qasim al-Warthani, Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn Dilan al-Jurjani, al-Fadl ibn Abi Sa'd al-Hadawi, Abu al-Fadl al-Makhzumi al-Basri, Abu Sa'd al-Malini, Abu al-Qasim 'Isa ibn 'Abbad al-Dinawari, Yahya al-Abhari, Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman al-Shirazi, Abu Bakr al-Jurjani, 'Abd al-Rahman al-Sijizi, and others—may Allah have mercy on them—I cannot count their number. And not a day passed but there were present with him about forty or fifty traveling strangers who understood and memorized. And I would take down notes according to my understanding and memory, and I copied from what Abu Bakr al-Barqani and Abu Ja'far ibn Dilan al-Jurjani had taken down. We were informed by the Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi, who said: Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn 'Ali al-Faqih narrated to us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-'Abbas al-Isma'ili died around 370 AH. He combined fiqh, hadith, and leadership in religion and world, and authored the Sahih. His son Abu Sa'd and the jurists of Jurjan studied under him. Our teacher, the Qadi Imam Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari, may Allah have mercy on him, said: I entered Jurjan intending to visit him, but he died before I met him. He combined the principles, fiqh, and hadith, and authored a Sahih according to the conditions of al-Bukhari, may Allah have mercy on him, which indicates great excellence to whoever examines it. The noble Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ahmad al-Marwazi al-Wa'iz informed us in Damascus, saying: The hafiz, the Shaykh Abu Nasr Hibat Allah ibn 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn Fakhr ibn Mu'adh ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sijzi told us in Sijistan: Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili is a great, venerable shaykh, trustworthy among the jurists and hadith scholars of his time, possessing abundant knowledge, sincere knowledge of hadith, and manifest manliness. People traveled to him in his time. He is Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-'Abbas al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani. He narrated from Abu Khalifa and other shaykhs. He was born in the year 277 AH and died in the year 371 AH.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, presented through multiple chains of narration. It begins with a chain from Hamza al-Sahmi, who quotes his father about al-Isma'ili's filial piety and the blessing he received from his parents' supplication. Then Hamza reports the vizier's inquiry about al-Isma'ili's works, noting his compilation of musnads and his commentary on Bukhari. Al-Daraqutni's testimony shows the high regard for al-Isma'ili, as he wished to travel to him. The passage then describes al-Isma'ili's teaching sessions, where many scholars and students would write down everything he said, listing several of his attendees. The following chain from Abu al-Qasim al-Samarqandi emphasizes that al-Isma'ili combined fiqh and hadith and held leadership in both religious and worldly affairs. Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari's comment highlights his scholarship in usul, fiqh, and hadith, and his Sahih on the conditions of Bukhari. Finally, the chain from al-Sijzi gives his birth and death dates and confirms his status as a trustworthy scholar. The biography demonstrates the reverence for this early Ash'ari scholar who was a major figure in hadith and fiqh.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The text shows he also excelled in fiqh and principles (usul), and held leadership in both religious and worldly affairs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili was blessed because of his filial piety—his parents' dua brought him barakah. When was the last time you sincerely asked your parents to pray for your deen and dunya, or if they are not alive, what are you doing to earn their dua from their graves?
?
Al-Daraqutni, a great hafiz, resolved to travel to al-Isma'ili but never made it. What opportunities to sit with people of knowledge have you let slip, thinking you could always do it later? Is there a scholar or teacher you have been meaning to learn from? Write down one concrete step you will take this week to seek that knowledge before it is too late.
?
Al-Isma'ili's sessions were filled with scholars writing every word. When you attend a lesson or read a book, do you exert effort to preserve what you learn, or do you let it pass? What does your level of care reveal about your longing for knowledge?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

Biography of Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari
Ibn Asakir introduces Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari as a student and propagator of Ash'ari school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari as a student of Imam al-Ash'ari and his contributions to spreading the Ash'ari school in Syria.

Core Idea
Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari: a devoted student of al-Ash'ari who carried his teachings to Syria.

Ibn Asakir's biographical dictionary introduces us to a key figure in the transmission of Ash'ari theology. Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Tabari was not just a student of al-Ash'ari but an active propagator of his school in Syria. He also authored a foundational work on usul. Let's explore his life and contribution.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical passage
Read the Arabic passage once without translation, then read the literal translation. Notice the key details about al-Tabari's life and teachers.
Pay attention to his kunya 'Abu al-Hasan' which matches his teacher's.
2
Identify his relationship with al-Ash'ari
The passage states he was 'among the notable companions of Abu al-Hasan (al-Ash'ari)' and 'studied under him'. Note that he traveled to Syria to spread the Ash'ari school.
3
Reflect on his scholarly work
He wrote from Abu Ja'far al-Tabari the famous Tafsir. He also authored a book on usul titled 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi wa Basirat al-Mustahdi'. Think about the significance of this title.
The title suggests it was designed to train beginners in theology.

ومنهم أبو الحسن عبد العزيز بن محمد بن اسحق الطبري المعروف بالدمل رحمه الله كان من اعيان اصحاب أبى الحسن وممن تخرج به وخرج إلى الشام ونشربها مذهبه وكتب عن أبي جعفر محمد بن جرير الطبري كتابه في التفسير وسمعه منه ووقفت له قديما على تأليف فى الأصول يدل على فضل كثير وعلم غزير سماه كتاب رياضة المبتدى وبصيرة المستهدى
Among them is Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Tabari, known as al-Damal, may Allah have mercy on him. He was among the notable companions of Abu al-Hasan (al-Ash'ari) and among those who studied under him. He traveled to Syria and spread his (al-Ash'ari's) school there. He wrote from Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari his book of Tafsir and heard it from him. I came across an earlier work of his on the principles (usul) that indicates great excellence and abundant knowledge, which he titled 'The Training of the Beginner and the Insight of the Seeker.'
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a brief biographical notice for Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Tabari, known as al-Damal. It states that he was one of the distinguished companions of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and studied under him. He traveled to Syria and propagated the Ash'ari school there. He also wrote from Abu Ja'far al-Tabari (the famous historian and exegete) his Tafsir and listened to it directly from him. The author (Ibn Asakir) mentions that he saw an earlier composition by al-Tabari on usul (principles of jurisprudence or theology) that demonstrated his extensive knowledge, titled 'The Training of the Beginner and the Insight of the Seeker.' This highlights his role in spreading Ash'ari theology and his scholarly output.

Correction: The Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari in this passage is a different person. He was a student of al-Ash'ari and studied under Abu Ja'far al-Tabari, not the same as his teacher.

Abu al-Hasan al-Tabari: Student of al-Ash'ari and Author on Divine Attributes
Ibn 'Asakir introduces a key student of al-Ash'ari and his famous work on attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly profile of Abu al-Hasan 'Ali al-Tabari, his relationship with al-Ash'ari, and his contribution to interpreting hadiths on God's attributes.

Core Idea
Al-Tabari authored the key Ash'ari work on interpreting problematic attribute hadiths.

This lesson introduces Abu al-Hasan 'Ali al-Tabari, a direct student of Imam al-Ash'ari who became a distinguished scholar and author. His most famous work addresses a critical theological issue: how to understand hadiths that seem to describe God in human-like terms. This passage from Ibn 'Asakir gives us a brief but important glimpse into his life and legacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical entry
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the isnad at the end connecting Ibn 'Asakir to his source.
The isnad shows the chain of transmission for this information.
2
Identify al-Tabari's relationship to al-Ash'ari
The passage uses words like 'sahiba' (accompanied), 'akhadha 'anhu' (took from him), and 'takharraja bihi' (graduated under him). Understand the strong student-teacher bond.
3
Focus on his famous book
Al-Tabari wrote a famous book on the interpretation of problematic hadiths about God's attributes. This is a key Ash'ari text dealing with tanzih (transcendence).
The book's title is often given as 'Kitab Ta'wil al-Ahadith al-Mushkilat'.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Be careful not to confuse this al-Tabari with other scholars named al-Tabari, such as the historian or the mufassir. This one is specifically the Ash'ari theologian.
The common misunderstanding is addressed in the misconception section.

Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a short biographical entry for Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Tabari. It states that he accompanied Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari in Basra, learned from him, and became a distinguished scholar. He authored multiple works demonstrating his vast knowledge. Crucially, he is the author of a famous book that interprets problematic hadiths concerning the divine attributes (sifat), a key topic in Ash'ari theology where anthropomorphic expressions are interpreted metaphorically to preserve God's transcendence. The passage ends with an isnad showing Ibn Asakir's source for this information.

Correction: This al-Tabari is a different person: he was a student of al-Ash'ari, lived in Basra, and authored a work on the interpretation of attribute hadiths. He is known as a mutakallim (theologian) of the Ash'ari school, not a historian or universal commentator.

The Scholar Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili: A Model of Integrated Knowledge
Ibn Asakir narrates the biography of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili through multiple chains, emphasizing his scholarly breadth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the profile of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili as a Shafi'i jurist, hadith master, and author of a Sahih collection on al-Bukhari's conditions, as recorded by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili united jurisprudence, hadith, and leadership.

In this lesson, we explore the biography of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili as transmitted by Ibn Asakir. The passage uses multiple chains to convey his scholarly stature, emphasizing his combination of fiqh and hadith, his authorship of a Sahih, and the high esteem in which he was held. It also corrects the misconception that he was merely a hadith specialist.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage from Ibn Asakir, then its literal translation. Notice the two different chains of transmission (isnads) and how they present complementary information.
2
Identify key biographical details
List the key facts: his full name, birth and death dates, his scholarly contributions (especially the Sahih), and his teachers and students.
Pay attention to the phrase 'جمع بين الفقه والحديث' which sums up his dual expertise.
3
Reflect on the significance of his Sahih
The passage states his Sahih is 'on the conditions of al-Bukhari'. Consider what this implies about his methodology and the value of his work.
This shows he was a leading hadith scholar who followed al-Bukhari's rigorous standards.
4
Examine the misconception
The common misunderstanding is that al-Isma'ili was only a hadith scholar. The text explicitly states he combined fiqh, hadith, and leadership. Note how both chains highlight this.
This lesson guards against reducing his legacy to a single field.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم اسماعيل بن أحمد السمرقندي قال ثنا أبو اسحق إبراهيم بن على الفقيه قال : أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم بن اسماعيل بن العباس الاسماعيلي مات سنة نيف وسبعين وثلاثمائة وجمع بين الفقه والحديث ورياسة الدين والدنيا وصنف الصحيح واخذ عنه ابنه أبو سعد وفقهاء جرجان، وقال شيخنا القاضى الامام أبو الطيب الطبري رحمه الله دخلت جرجان قاصدا إليه وهو حى فمات قبل أن ألقاه، جمع بين الأصول والفقه والحديث وصنف صحيحا على شرط البخارى رحمه الله، يدل على فضل كثير لمن وقف عليه أخبرنا الشريف أبو بكر أحمد بن عبدالرحمن ابن أحمد المروزى الواعظ بدمشق قال قال لنا الشيخ الحافظ أبو نصر هبة الله ابن عبد الجبار بن فاخر بن معاذ بن أحمد بن محمد السجزي بسجستان : أبو بكر الاسماعيلى شيخ كبير جليل ثقة من الفقهاء والمحدثين في عصره يرجع إلى علم وافر ومعرفة بالحديث صادقة ومروءة ظاهرة وكانت إليه الرحلة في زمانه وهو أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم بن اسماعيل بن العباس الإسماعيلى الجرجاني روى عن أبي خليفة والمشايخ ولد سنة سبع وسبعين ومائتين ومات سنة احدى وسبعين وثلاثمائة .
Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi informed us, saying: Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn 'Ali al-Faqih narrated to us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-'Abbas al-Isma'ili died in the year around seventy and three hundred [371 AH]. He combined jurisprudence and hadith and the leadership of religion and the world, and he authored the Sahih. His son Abu Sa'd and the jurists of Jurjan studied with him. Our shaykh, the judge imam Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari, may Allah have mercy on him, said: I entered Jurjan intending to visit him while he was alive, but he died before I met him. He combined the foundations, jurisprudence, and hadith, and authored a Sahih according to the conditions of al-Bukhari, may Allah have mercy on him. It indicates great excellence for whoever examines it. Al-Sharif Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ahmad al-Marwazi al-Wa'iz informed us in Damascus, saying: Shaykh al-Hafiz Abu Nasr Hibat Allah ibn 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn Fakhr ibn Mu'adh ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sijzi told us in Sijistan: Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili is a great, venerable shaykh, trustworthy among the jurists and hadith specialists of his time. He possessed abundant knowledge, sincere knowledge of hadith, and manifest chivalry. People traveled to him in his time. He is Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-'Abbas al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani. He narrated from Abu Khalifa and the shaykhs. He was born in the year seven and seventy and two hundred [277 AH] and died in the year one and seventy and three hundred [371 AH].
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili (d. 371 AH), a prominent Shafi'i scholar, hadith master, and jurist from Jurjan. The text first provides his death date and highlights that he combined fiqh, hadith, and leadership in both religious and worldly affairs. He authored a Sahih collection, and many scholars, including his son Abu Sa'd and the jurists of Jurjan, studied under him. The judge Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari notes that he traveled to Jurjan to meet him but al-Isma'ili died before the meeting. Another chain adds that al-Isma'ili was a great, reliable shaykh, possessing abundant knowledge and sincere expertise in hadith, and people undertook journeys to him. His birth is given as 277 AH and death as 371 AH.

The Chain of Ash'ari Learning: Al-Dumali
Ibn Asakir introduces a student of al-Ash'ari and his usul book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of Abu al-Hasan al-Dumali in transmitting Ash'ari doctrine and the significance of his book 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi' wa Basirat al-Mustahdi'.

Core Idea
Al-Dumali was a key student of al-Ash'ari who spread his school in Syria and wrote an influential usul work.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari introduces us to a lesser-known but important figure: Abu al-Hasan al-Dumali al-Tabari. A direct student of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, he was instrumental in spreading the Ash'ari school in Syria. Ibn Asakir also mentions a manuscript he saw—a book on usul (principles of religion) that reflects deep knowledge. Let's explore this brief biography.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage from Ibn Asakir once, then the English translation. Notice the concise style of biographical entries in classical works.
2
Identify key figures and their roles
Note that al-Dumali is a companion (sahib) of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and also studied tafsir under Abu Ja'far al-Tabari. Distinguish his primary affiliation with al-Ash'ari.
He is not a student of al-Tabari in theology, only in tafsir.
3
Focus on the book title
Examine the title 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi' wa Basirat al-Mustahdi.' Consider what it tells us about the content: it is a guide for beginners and seekers of guidance in usul al-din.
The title suggests pedagogical intent.
4
Reflect on the transmission chain
Think about how knowledge was passed: al-Ash'ari taught al-Dumali, who then traveled to Syria to spread the school. This illustrates the importance of teacher-student networks in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو الحسن عبد العزيز بن محمد بن اسحق الطبري ) المعروف بالدمل رحمه الله كان من اعيان اصحاب أبى الحسن وممن تخرج به وخرج إلى الشام ونشربها مذهبه وكتب عن أبي جعفر محمد بن جرير الطبري كتابه في التفسير وسمعه منه ووقفت له قديما على تأليف فى الأصول يدل على فضل كثير وعلم غزير سماه كتاب ) رياضة المبتدى وبصيرة المستهدى .
Among them is Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Tabari, known as al-Dumali, may Allah have mercy on him. He was among the notable companions of Abu al-Hasan [al-Ash'ari] and among those who graduated under him. He went out to Syria and spread his [al-Ash'ari's] school there. He wrote from Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari his book of tafsir and heard it from him. I came across an old work of his on principles (usul) that indicates great excellence and abundant knowledge; he named it 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi' wa Basirat al-Mustahdi.'
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Tabari, known as al-Dumali (perhaps derived from 'daml' meaning 'grease' or a place name). He was a prominent companion and student of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and he traveled to Syria to propagate the Ash'ari school. He also studied under Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari, the famous historian and mufassir, and copied or heard his tafsir directly from him. Ibn 'Asakir mentions that he saw a work by al-Dumali on usul al-din (principles of religion) which demonstrated great learning; its title is 'Riyadat al-Mubtadi' wa Basirat al-Mustahdi' (The Training of the Beginner and the Insight of the Seeker of Guidance).

Correction: He studied tafsir from al-Tabari, but his primary affiliation and doctrinal training were under Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Biography of Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari: An Ash'ari Disciple and His Poetry
Ibn Asakir records the biography of Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari, another Ash'ari disciple, including his poetry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly lineage of Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari as a student of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and the content of his poetry reflecting on companionship and the plight of the times.

Core Idea
Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari wrote a key work on hadith attributes and his poetry shows a wise outlook on life.

This lesson introduces another important figure from the Ash'ari school: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari. He was a direct student of al-Ash'ari in Basra and authored a famous book on the interpretation of problematic hadiths about God's attributes. We will also look at two poems he composed, which offer moral and reflective insights.

Among them is Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Mahdi al-Tabari. The faqih Abu al-Fath Nasr Allah ibn Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Qawi al-Misisi informed us in Damascus, saying: Abu al-Qasim 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn Abi al-'Ala' al-Misisi told us in Damascus, saying: Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Fariqi known as Ibn al-Darrab told us there, saying: Abu Sa'd Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Khalili al-Malini told us, saying: Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari recited to me his own poetry: 'I heard: He who has a companion who can improve his affairs is not lost. For the world [is sustained] by its inhabitants, and man [is sustained] by his brothers.' He said: And Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari recited to me his own poetry: 'Indeed time is a time of evil, and all these people are [?]. The noble ones have all gone, and I remain in [wishing] 'if only' and 'would that.' And if you ask about generosity, their answer about that is [?]'
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage introduces Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Mahdi al-Tabari, another disciple of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, who studied under him in Basra and authored several works. Most notably, he wrote a famous book on the interpretation (ta'wil) of problematic hadiths concerning the divine attributes, indicating his involvement in defending Ash'ari theology. Then the author (Ibn 'Asakir) provides a chain of transmission to verses of poetry composed by al-Tabari himself. The first poem emphasizes the value of having a good companion who can improve one's state, and that a person is known by his brothers. The second poem laments the passing of noble people and the speaker's remaining in a state of regret ('if only' and 'would that'), with a fragment about generosity that is partially corrupt.

Key Terms
علي بن مهدي الطبري
تأويل الأحاديث المشكلات
الصفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the famous book on problematic hadiths about the attributes was authored by al-Ash'ari himself.
Correction: The passage clearly states that it was composed by his student Ali ibn Mahdi al-Tabari.

Ibn 'Asakir transmits the biography of Abu Ja'far al-Naqqash, an Ash'ari theologian and hadith scholar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, scholarly credentials, and theological affiliation of Abu Ja'far al-Naqqash as recorded by Ibn 'Asakir.

Core Idea
A trustworthy Ash'ari theologian who taught kalam to his students.

This biographical passage introduces us to Abu Ja'far al-Naqqash, a scholar of both hadith and kalam. Through the testimony of his contemporaries, we see his reliability as a transmitter and his role in spreading the Ash'ari school. The details of his birth and death help place him in the timeline of Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the full Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, focusing on the names and key phrases. Notice the chain of transmission: Ibn 'Asakir reports from al-Azhari, who reports from al-Naqqash's students.
2
Trace his name and lineage
Identify his full name and epithet 'al-Naqqash', meaning 'the engraver'. Note his lineage back several generations to establish his identity.
His name includes 'al-Sulami' (related to the tribe of Sulaym) and 'al-Baghdadi' (from Baghdad).
3
List his teachers and students
From the passage, identify the scholars he narrated from (teachers) and those who narrated from him (students). This shows his place in the scholarly network.
Teachers include al-Baghawi and Ibn Abi Dawud; students include Abu 'Ali ibn Shadhan and al-Azhari.
4
Understand his theological affiliation
Al-Azhari states that al-Naqqash was a theologian (mutakallim) following the Ash'ari school, and that he taught kalam to Abu 'Ali ibn Shadhan. Note the significance of this for Ash'ari history.
5
Confirm his trustworthiness and dates
Al-Azhari explicitly calls him 'thiqah' (trustworthy). The passage also gives his birth (294 AH) and death (379 AH), placing him in the 3rd-4th centuries AH.
The death date is given as Sunday/Monday, 6 Muharram 379 AH.

ومنهم أبو جعفر السلمى البغدادي النقاش رحمه الله ) محمد بن أحمد بن العباس بن أحمد ابن خلاد بن أسلم بن سهل بن مرداس أبو جعفر السلمي نقاش الفضة بن سليمان الباغندى، والحسن بن محمى المحرمي وعبد الله ابن محمد البغوى وأبا بكر بن أبى داود السجستاني ويحيى بن صاعد وابابكر بن مجاهد المقرى، حدثنا عنه أبو على بن شاذان وأبو القسم الأزهرى وعلى بن المحسن التنوخي، سألت الأزهرى عن أبي جعفر النقاش فقال ثقة، قال وكان احد المتكلمين على مذهب الأشعرى ومنه تعلم أبو على بن شاذان الكلام، قال لنا على بن المحسن التنوخي مولد أبي جعفر النقاش للنصف من جمادى الأولى سنة اربع وتسعين ومائتين وقال أبو بكر أحمد بن محمد العتيقى قال سنة تسع وسبعين وثلاثمائة فيها توفى أبو جعفر الأشعرى النقاش يوم الأحد أو الاثنين لست خلون من المحرم وكان ثقة .
Among them is Abu Ja'far al-Sulami al-Baghdadi al-Naqqash, may Allah have mercy on him. [He is] Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-'Abbas ibn Ahmad ibn Khallad ibn Aslam ibn Sahl ibn Mirdas, Abu Ja'far al-Sulami, the silver engraver. [He narrated from] ibn Sulayman al-Baghindi, al-Hasan ibn Muhanna al-Muharrami, 'Abd Allah ibn Muhammad al-Baghawi, Abu Bakr ibn Abi Dawud al-Sijistani, Yahya ibn Sa'id, and Abu Bakr ibn Mujahid al-Muqri'. Abu 'Ali ibn Shadhan, Abu al-Qasim al-Azhari, and 'Ali ibn al-Muhsin al-Tanukhi narrated from us [from him]. I asked al-Azhari about Abu Ja'far al-Naqqash, and he said: 'Trustworthy.' He said: 'He was one of the theologians upon the madhhab of al-Ash'ari, and from him Abu 'Ali ibn Shadhan learned kalam.' 'Ali ibn al-Muhsin al-Tanukhi told us: The birth of Abu Ja'far al-Naqqash was at the middle of Jumada al-Ula in the year four and ninety and two hundred [294 AH]. And Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-'Atiqi said: In the year nine and seventy and three hundred [379 AH], Abu Ja'far al-Ash'ari al-Naqqash died on Sunday or Monday, six days into al-Muharram, and he was trustworthy.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is the biography of Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Sulami al-Baghdadi al-Naqqash (d. 379 AH). His lineage is traced back through several generations, and his epithet 'al-Naqqash' means 'the engraver' or 'the one who works with silver' (naqqash al-fidda). The text lists his teachers, including Ibn Sulayman al-Baghindi, al-Hasan al-Muharrami, al-Baghawi, Ibn Abi Dawud, Yahya ibn Sa'id, and Ibn Mujahid al-Muqri'. His students include Abu 'Ali ibn Shadhan, Abu al-Qasim al-Azhari, and 'Ali ibn al-Muhsin al-Tanukhi. Ibn 'Asakir asked al-Azhari about him and was told he was trustworthy (thiqah) and that he was one of the mutakallimun (theologians) following the Ash'ari school; indeed, Abu 'Ali ibn Shadhan learned kalam from him. His birth is given as mid-Jumada al-Ula 294 AH, and his death as early Muharram 379 AH, with a note that he was reliable.

أبو علي بن شاذان

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'al-Naqqash' refers to a critic of hadith (naqd) rather than an engraver.
Correction: The passage explicitly says 'naqqash al-fidda' (silver engraver), so it is a profession, not a reference to criticism.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry (tarjama) for Abu Ja‘far al-Sulami al-Baghdadi al-Naqqash, introduced by the phrase 'Among them' (minhum). It provides a chain of transmission (isnad) that leads to the author, listing multiple teachers who transmitted the biography. The biography gives his full name and lineage, noting his craft as a silver engraver (naqqash al-fidda). It lists his teachers (shuyukh) including well-known scholars such as al-Baghawi and Ibn Abi Dawud, and his students such as Abu ‘Ali ibn Shadhan, Abu al-Qasim al-Azhari, and ‘Ali ibn al-Muhsin al-Tanukhi. Al-Azhari is quoted attesting to his trustworthiness (thiqa). Importantly, it states that he was one of the mutakallimun on the Ash‘ari school, and that Abu ‘Ali ibn Shadhan learned kalam from him, highlighting his role as a teacher of Ash‘ari theology. The passage concludes with his birth (mid-Jumada al-Ula 294 AH) and death (early Muharram 379 AH), both dates given on different authorities, and reaffirms his reliability.

Abu Abdullah al-Isbahani: An Ash'ari Theologian
Biographical entry for the Ash'ari theologian Abu Abdullah al-Isbahani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the profile of Abu Abdullah al-Isbahani as an Ash'ari theologian and his scholarly contributions.

Core Idea
A Shafi'i jurist was also a mutakallim who professed the school of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

This passage introduces us to a scholar who combined Ash'ari theology with Shafi'i jurisprudence. Through a reliable chain, we learn about his return to Isfahan, his death, and his many works. This helps us see how Ash'arism spread among scholars of different legal schools.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical entry
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the chain of transmission that vouches for the information.
The chain shows the care with which biographies were preserved.
2
Identify his theological affiliation
Look for the phrase 'ينتحل مذهب أبي الحسن الأشعرى'. This tells us he was an Ash'ari theologian.
The term 'ينتحل' indicates he adopted or professed this school.
3

The text mentions he authored works in usul, fiqh, and ahkam. Consider the range of his scholarship.
4
Reflect on the significance
Think about what this tells us about the spread of Ash'arism among Shafi'i scholars in the 4th century AH.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حدثني أبو مسعود عبدالرحيم بن على بن أحمد المعدل باصبهان قال انا أبو على الحسن بن أحمد بن الحسن المقرى واجازه الى أبو على الحداد قال انا أبو نعيم أحمد بن عبدالله بن أحمد الحافظ الأصبهاني قال: محمد بن القسم أبو عبد الله الشافعي متكلم على مذهب اهل السنة ينتحل مذهب أبي الحسن الأشعرى، عاد الى أصبهان سنة ثلاث وخمسين وثلاثمائة وتوفى بها في ربيع الأول يوم الجمعة لاثنتى عشرة خلت منه سنة احدى وثمانين وثلاثمائة سمع الكثير بالعراق كثير المصنفات في الأصول والفقه والأحكام.
Abu Mas‘ud ‘Abd al-Rahim ibn ‘Ali ibn Ahmad al-Mu‘addal narrated to me in Isfahan, he said: Abu ‘Ali al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn al-Hasan al-Muqri’ narrated to us, and he granted permission to Abu ‘Ali al-Haddad, he said: Abu Nu‘aym Ahmad ibn ‘Abd Allah ibn Ahmad al-Hafiz al-Isbahani narrated to us, he said: Muhammad ibn al-Qasim, Abu ‘Abd Allah al-Shafi‘i, a theologian (mutakallim) upon the school of the people of the Sunnah, who professed the school of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari. He returned to Isfahan in the year 353 and died there in Rabi‘ al-Awwal, on Friday, the twelfth night of the month, in the year 381. He heard much (hadith) in Iraq, and he produced many works on usul, fiqh, and ahkam.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu ‘Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Qasim al-Shafi‘i, known as al-Isbahani. The biography is transmitted through a chain: the author hears from Abu Mas‘ud, who heard from Abu ‘Ali al-Muqri’ with authorization from Abu ‘Ali al-Haddad, who heard from Abu Nu‘aym al-Isbahani. The core description states that he was a mutakallim (theologian) on the school of the People of the Sunnah (Ahl al-Sunna) and that he professed (yantaḥilu) the school of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari, marking him as an Ash‘ari. It records his return to Isfahan in 353 AH and his death there in Rabi‘ al-Awwal 381 AH. It notes that he studied extensively in Iraq and authored many works in usul (principles of religion), fiqh (jurisprudence), and ahkam (legal rulings), indicating his broad scholarship in both theology and law.

Correction: The title 'al-Shafi'i' indicates his legal school (fiqh), but the passage explicitly states his theological school was Ash'ari.

Abu Muhammad al-Zuhri embodied scholarship and asceticism, fasting daily and completing the Quran every two days.

This passage from Ibn ‘Asakir's biographical dictionary introduces us to a lesser-known but remarkable figure: Abu Muhammad al-Zuhri, a theologian of the Ash‘ari school and a devoted ascetic. The biography not only traces his scholarly lineage and teachers but also highlights his extraordinary devotional practices. As you read, pay attention to the details that reveal both his intellectual pedigree and his spiritual discipline.

The imam, the shaykh Abu Nasr ‘Abd al-Rahim ibn ‘Abd al-Karim wrote to me, informing me, he said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn ibn ‘Ali ibn Musa al-Hafiz narrated to us, he said: Abu ‘Abd Allah Muhammad ibn ‘Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us, he said: ‘Abd al-Wahid ibn Ahmad ibn al-Qasim ibn Muhammad ibn ‘Abd al-Rahman al-Zuhri, Abu Muhammad al-Mudhakkir, from the descendants of ‘Abd al-Rahman ibn ‘Awf, and he is the son of Abu al-Fadl, the Ash‘ari theologian (al-mutakallim al-Ash‘ari). He heard (hadith) from Abu Hamid ibn Bilal, Abu Bakr al-Qattan, and their peers. Then he accompanied me (the transmitter) with Abu al-Nadr in Tus, and with al-Mahbubi and al-Sayyari in Marw, and he heard much with us. He used to fast perpetually and complete the Quran every two days. Al-Zuhri, may God have mercy on him, died in Nishapur on the morning of Thursday, the eighteenth of Rabi‘ al-Awwal of the year 382. I visited him early on the day of his death, and he wept much and said: 'I entrust you to God, O governor, for I am departing.'
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Muhammad ‘Abd al-Wahid ibn Ahmad al-Zuhri, known as Ibn Abi al-Fadl, an Ash‘ari theologian. The chain includes a letter from Abu Nasr to the author, then through Abu Bakr al-Hafiz and Abu ‘Abd Allah al-Hafiz. The biography notes his descent from ‘Abd al-Rahman ibn ‘Awf, a famous Companion. It states that his father was also an Ash‘ari mutakallim. It lists his teachers (Abu Hamid ibn Bilal, Abu Bakr al-Qattan, and others) and mentions that he accompanied the chains transmitters in Tus and Marw. A notable practice is recorded: he fasted every day (perpetual fasting) and completed the Quran every two days, highlighting his asceticism. The death date is given precisely: morning of Thursday, 18 Rabi‘ al-Awwal 382 AH in Nishapur. The final anecdote relates the transmitter's visit on his deathbed, where al-Zuhri wept and bid farewell to a governor (al-hakim), saying 'I entrust you to God, for I am departing.' This adds a personal, emotional touch to the biography.

Key Terms
المتكلم الأشعرى
المذكر
يصوم الدهر
يختم القرآن
الزهرى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Abu Muhammad al-Zuhri was an Ash‘ari theologian and ascetic who fasted daily, completed the Quran every two days, and was part of a scholarly family tracing back to a Companion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Zuhri fasted every day and completed the Quran every two days. When was the last time you fasted a voluntary fast or completed the Quran? Does your daily schedule reflect that same urgency to worship, or have you become comfortable with minimal effort?
?
On his deathbed, al-Zuhri wept and entrusted the governor to Allah. If you knew you were dying tomorrow, what would you say to those you love? Are you living in a way that your final words would be a testament to faith, or would they be filled with regret?
?
Al-Zuhri came from a noble lineage of the Companion 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf, yet his piety was his own. Do you rely on your family background, reputation, or past good deeds to feel secure about your standing with Allah, or are you actively striving to build a personal relationship with Him through consistent worship?

Biography of Abu Abdullah al-Asbahani al-Shafi'i
Biographical entry for Abu Abdullah al-Asbahani al-Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the biographical details and scholarly credentials of Abu Abdullah al-Asbahani al-Shafi'i, an early Ash'ari theologian.

Core Idea
A chain-narrated biography reveals the scholarly lineage and Ash'ari affiliation of a 4th-century Sunni theologian.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari presents a biographical entry for Abu Abdullah al-Asbahani al-Shafi'i. It begins with a chain of transmission, then provides key details about his theology, travel, death, and scholarly output. This lesson explores the content and significance of this biography.

Guided Path
1
Follow the chain of narration
Identify the narrators from Ibn Asakir back to Abu Nu'aym. Notice how the chain establishes authenticity.
2
Study the biographical details
Read the description: his title, his theological school (Ash'ari), his return to Isfahan, and his death date.
3
Reflect on his scholarly contributions
Note that he authored works in usul, fiqh, and ahkam. Consider how this reflects his expertise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو عبدالله الأصبهاني المعروف بالشافعي
حدثني أبو مسعود عبدالرحيم بن على بن أحمد المعدل باصبهان قال انا أبو على الحسن بن أحمد بن الحسن المقرى واجازه الى أبو على الحداد قال انا أبو نعيم أحمد بن عبدالله بن أحمد الحافظ الأصبهاني قال : محمد بن القسم أبو عبد الله الشافعي متكلم على مذهب اهل السنة ينتحل مذهب أبي الحسن الأشعرى، عاد الى أصبهان سنة ثلاث وخمسين وثلاثمائة وتوفى بها في ربيع الأول يوم الجمعة لاثنتى عشرة خلت منه سنة احدى وثمانين وثلاثمائة سمع الكثير بالعراق كثير المصنفات في الأصول والفقه والأحكام.
Among them is Abu Abdullah al-Asbahani, known as al-Shafi'i. Abu Mas'ud Abd al-Rahim ibn Ali ibn Ahmad al-Mu'addil narrated to me in Isfahan, saying: Abu Ali al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn al-Hasan al-Muqri' narrated to us with permission to Abu Ali al-Haddad, saying: Abu Nu'aym Ahmad ibn Abdullah ibn Ahmad al-Hafiz al-Asbahani narrated to us, saying: Muhammad ibn al-Qasim Abu Abdullah al-Shafi'i, a mutakallim (theologian) on the way of the People of the Sunna, adopting the school of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. He returned to Isfahan in the year 353 AH and died there in Rabi' al-Awwal on Friday, the twelfth of that month, in the year 381 AH. He heard much in Iraq and authored many works on usul (foundations), fiqh (jurisprudence), and legal rulings.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Abdullah al-Asbahani al-Shafi'i. It begins with a chain of narration: the author (Ibn Asakir) received the report from Abu Mas'ud in Isfahan, who heard from Abu Ali al-Muqri', who had permission from Abu Ali al-Haddad, who heard from Abu Nu'aym al-Asbahani. Abu Nu'aym states that Muhammad ibn al-Qasim, known as Abu Abdullah al-Shafi'i, was a mutakallim (theologian) adhering to the Sunni school and adopting the school of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. The entry gives his travel: he returned to Isfahan in 353 AH and died there in 381 AH. He heard many hadith in Iraq and produced numerous writings in usul (principles of religion), fiqh, and legal rulings. The chain shows the reliability of the report, and the details highlight his scholarship and affiliation with Ash'arism.

Correction: They are transmitted through a reliable chain of narrators, as indicated by the opening narration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This scholar adhered to the 'way of the People of the Sunna' through the Ash'ari school. What would change if you took that responsibility seriously?
?

Are you certain of their reliability, and are you actively seeking knowledge from living scholars, or do you only consume content from the internet without verifying?

Abu Bakr al-Bukhari al-Awdani: A Model of Piety
Biographical entry for Abu Bakr al-Bukhari al-Awdani, a pious Shafi'i jurist.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and character of the Shafi'i imam Abu Bakr al-Bukhari al-Awdani as recorded by Imam Ibn 'Asakir.

Core Idea
True knowledge is accompanied by deep piety and humility.

This brief biography of Abu Bakr al-Bukhari al-Awdani offers a window into the character of a great scholar. It is not just a list of dates but a portrait of a man who combined legal authority with profound spiritual humility. Let's explore his life through the eyes of his contemporaries.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the chain of narration and the key details about his life.
2
Identify his scholarly status
Look for phrases that indicate his position: 'imam of the Shafi'is in Transoxiana' and 'without dispute'. How does this show his authority?
3
Reflect on his personal qualities
The biography highlights his asceticism, scrupulousness, diligence in worship, weeping, and humility. Think about why these are mentioned alongside his scholarship.
Note the common misunderstanding: his weeping is not despair but sincere piety.
4
Consider his travels and teachers
He studied in Bukhara, al-Nasaf, and visited Nishapur. This shows the importance of traveling for knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو بكر البخارى المعروف بالأودنى الفقيه رحمه الله كتب إلى الشيخ الامام أبو نصر بن الأستاذ أبي القسم القشيري قال انا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين ،الحافظ، قال انا أبو عبدالله محمد بن عبدالله الحافظ قال محمد بن عبدالله بن محمد الفقيه أبو بكر البخاري ثم الأودني امام الشافعيين بما وراء النهر في عصره بلا مدافعة قدم نيسابور سنة خمس وستين وحج ثم انصرف، فأقام عندنا مدة فى سنة ست وستين وكان من ازهد الفقهاء وأورعهم واكثرهم اجتهادا في العبادة، وأبكاهم على تقصيره وأشدهم تواضعا وإخباتا وانابة، سمع ببخارى أبا الفضل يعقوب بن يوسف العاصمي وأقرانه وخرج إلى أبي يعلى بالنسف فاكثر عنه وعن الهيثم بن كليب وأقرانهما وتوفى الفقيه أبو بكر الاودنی رحمه الله ببخاری سنة خمس وثمانين وثلاثمائة .
Among them is Abu Bakr al-Bukhari, known as al-Awdani, the jurist, may Allah have mercy on him. The imam Abu Nasr ibn al-Ustadh Abi al-Qasim al-Qushayri wrote to me, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Hafiz narrated to us, saying: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Hafiz informed us, saying: Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Muhammad, the jurist Abu Bakr al-Bukhari, then al-Awdani, the imam of the Shafi'is in Transoxiana in his time without dispute. He came to Nishapur in 365 AH and performed Hajj, then returned. He stayed with us for a while in 366 AH. He was among the most ascetic of the jurists, the most scrupulous, the most diligent in worship, the most weeping over his shortcomings, the most humble, submissive, and repentant. He heard in Bukhara from Abu al-Fadl Ya'qub ibn Yusuf al-Asimi and his peers, and went out to Abu Ya'la in al-Nasaf and heard much from him and from al-Haytham ibn Kulayb and their peers. The jurist Abu Bakr al-Awdani, may Allah have mercy on him, died in Bukhara in the year 385 AH.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Bakr al-Bukhari al-Awdani, a Shafi'i jurist. The chain begins with Abu Nasr al-Qushayri reporting to the author, who heard from Abu Bakr al-Hafiz, who heard from Abu Abdullah al-Hafiz. The core report states that Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Muhammad was known as Abu Bakr al-Bukhari then al-Awdani, and he was the undisputed imam of the Shafi'is in Transoxiana in his time. He visited Nishapur in 365 AH, performed Hajj, and returned, staying with the narrator in 366 AH. The entry describes his piety: he was extremely ascetic, scrupulous, diligent in worship, wept much over his shortcomings, and was profoundly humble and repentant. His scholarly travels included hearing hadith in Bukhara and al-Nasaf, where he studied under Abu Ya'la and al-Haytham ibn Kulayb. He died in Bukhara in 385 AH.

Key Terms
أبو بكر البخاري الأودني
امام الشافعيين
ازهد الفقهاء
أبكاهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that weeping over one's shortcomings indicates despair or lack of trust in Allah's mercy.
Correction: The biography presents his weeping as a virtue, showing deep self-reproach and sincere piety, not hopelessness.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

?

Abu Bakr al-Awdani: A Model of Asceticism and Learning
Biography of Abu Bakr al-Awdani with chain, virtues, teachers, and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, virtues, and scholarly journey of Abu Bakr al-Awdani, a leading Shafi'i jurist of Transoxiana.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr al-Awdani combined deep learning with exceptional piety and humility.

Imam Ibn 'Asakir presents a chain of transmission leading to a brief yet rich biography of Abu Bakr al-Awdani. This passage not only records his scholarly status as the undisputed head of the Shafi'is in his region but also paints a vivid picture of his character through a series of virtues. As you read, notice how the biography balances scholarly achievements with spiritual excellence.

Guided Path
1
Read and trace the chain
The passage begins with a chain of authorities from Ibn 'Asakir back to al-Hakim al-Naysaburi. Notice how traditional biographical works preserve the transmission.
This chain ensures the reliability of the biography.
2
Identify the biographical highlights
Look for key events: his arrival in Nishapur in 365 AH, his Hajj, his stay, and his death year (385 AH).
3
Analyze the list of virtues
The author lists several qualities: asceticism, piety, diligence, weeping, and humility. Consider why these are emphasized and how they reflect his character.
The virtues are presented as superlatives.
4
Note his teachers and regions
He studied in Bukhara and Nasaf with specific scholars. This shows his broad learning and connections.
His teachers include Abu al-Fadl al-Asimi, Abu Ya'la, and al-Haytham ibn Kulayb.
5
Reflect on the lesson for today
How does this biography inspire a balance between knowledge and character? What can we learn from his humility and devotion?

And among them is Abu Bakr al-Bukhari known as al-Awdani, the faqih, may Allah have mercy on him. He wrote to the imam Abu Nasr ibn al-Ustadh Abi al-Qasim al-Qushayri saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Hafiz told us, saying: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Hafiz told us, saying: Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Muhammad al-Faqih, Abu Bakr al-Bukhari then al-Awdani, the undisputed imam of the Shafi'is in Transoxiana in his time, came to Nishapur in the year 365 AH, performed Hajj, then returned. The faqih Abu Bakr al-Awdani, may Allah have mercy on him, died in Bukhara in the year 385 AH.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Abu Bakr al-Bukhari al-Awdani, a prominent Shafi'i jurist in Transoxiana. The author, Ibn 'Asakir, transmits the biography through a chain that reaches al-Qushayri, then al-Hafiz al-Bayhaqi, then al-Hakim al-Naysaburi. The biography emphasizes al-Awdani's undisputed leadership of the Shafi'is, his journey to Nishapur and pilgrimage, his exceptional asceticism, piety, diligence in worship, and humility. It also notes his teachers: he studied in Bukhara with Abu al-Fadl al-Asimi and in Nasaf with Abu Ya'la and al-Haytham ibn Kulayb. He died in Bukhara in 385 AH. The teacher-like explanation follows the sequence: transmission chain, arrival, virtues, teachers, death.

The Scholarly Ascetic: Abu Mansur ibn Hamshad
Biography of the ascetic scholar Abu Mansur ibn Hamshad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and character of Abu Mansur ibn Hamshad al-Naysaburi as a model of combined scholarship, asceticism, and answered supplication.

Core Idea
A scholar of three hundred books who lived on a day's ration.

This biography from Ibn Asakir's Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari presents a vivid portrait of a scholar who mastered multiple disciplines while living an ascetic life. The passage not only details his extensive travels and teachers but also reveals his profound piety and the miraculous acceptance of his prayers. Let's explore how his life exemplifies the ideal of knowledge coupled with detachment.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the extensive listing of teachers and subjects.
Pay attention to the chain of transmission at the beginning.
2
Analyze his education
Identify the different fields he studied: literature, fiqh, kalam, ma'ani, and hadith. Note the regions he traveled to.
He studied in Khurasan, Iraq, Hijaz, and Yemen.
3
Reflect on his piety
Observe the descriptions of his asceticism: avoiding rulers, living on minimal sustenance, and devotion to the mosque and school.
4
Note his achievements
He authored over 300 books and his prayers were answered. This shows his high rank with Allah.
He was known as 'mujab al-da'wah' (one whose supplication is answered).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو منصور بن حمشاد النيسابوري رحمه الله كمه كتب إلى الأستاذ أبو نصر بن الأستاذ أبى القسم القشيري يخبرني قال انا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين الحافظ قال انا أبو عبدالله محمد بن عبدالله الحافظ قال : محمد بن عبد الله بن حمشاد أبو منصور الأديب الزاهد من العباد العلماء المجتهدين، درس الأدب على أبي عمر الزردي وابي حامد الخارزنجى وأبى عمر الزاهد وأقرانهم والفقه بخراسان على أبي الوليد وبالعراق على أبي على بن أبى هريرة والكلام على أبي سهل الخليطي والمعانى على أبي بكر بن عبدوس ونظرائه وسمع بخراسان أبا حامد بن بلال البزاز وأبا بكر محمد بن الحسين القطان وأقرانهما وبالعراق على الصفار وأبا جعفر الرزاز وأقرانهما وبالحجاز أبا سعيد بن الأعرابي وأقرانه ودخل اليمن فأدرك بها الاسانيد العالية وكان من المجتهدين في العبادة الزاهدين فى الدنيا تجنب مخالطة السلاطين وأولياءهم إلى أن خرج من دار الدنيا وهو ملازم لمسجدهم ومدرسته، قد اقتصر من بقية أوقاف السلفه عليه على قوت يوم بيوم تخرج به جماعة من العلماء الواعظين وظهر له من مصنفاته أكثر من ثلاثمائة كتاب مصنف وقد ظهر لنا في غير شيء أنه كان مجاب الدعوة ، توفي رحمه الله وقت الصبح يوم الجمعة الرابع والعشرين من رجب سنة ثمان وثمانين وثلاثمائة وسمعته في مرضه الذي مات فيه يذكر مولده سنة ست عشرة وثلاثماية فمات وهو ابن اثنتين وسبعين سنة .
And among them is Abu Mansur ibn Hamshad al-Naysaburi, may Allah have mercy on him. He wrote to al-Ustadh Abu Nasr ibn al-Ustadh Abi al-Qasim al-Qushayri informing me, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Hafiz told us, saying: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Hafiz told us, saying: Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Hamshad, Abu Mansur, the literary scholar, the ascetic, among the devout, the learned, the diligent. He studied literature under Abu 'Amr al-Zirdi, Abu Hamid al-Kharzanji, Abu 'Amr al-Zahid, and their peers; fiqh in Khurasan under Abu al-Walid and in Iraq under Abu 'Ali ibn Abi Hurayra; kalam under Abu Sahl al-Khaliti; and meanings (al-ma'ani) under Abu Bakr ibn 'Abdus and his peers. He heard hadith in Khurasan from Abu Hamid ibn Bilal al-Bazzaz, Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Qattan, and their peers; in Iraq from al-Saffar, Abu Ja'far al-Razzaz, and their peers; in the Hijaz from Abu Sa'id ibn al-A'rabi and his peers. He entered Yemen and obtained there high chains of transmission. He was among the diligent in worship, ascetic in this world, avoiding association with rulers and their allies until he left the world, while being devoted to their mosque and school. He restricted himself from the remaining endowments left to him to a day's sustenance. A group of scholars and preachers graduated from him. He produced more than three hundred authored books. It became evident to us in more than one matter that his supplications were answered. He died, may Allah have mercy on him, at dawn on Friday, the 24th of Rajab, year 388 AH. I heard him during his final illness mention his birth in the year 316 AH, so he died at the age of seventy-two years.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Abu Mansur ibn Hamshad al-Naysaburi, a prolific scholar and ascetic. The transmission chain goes through al-Qushayri, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Hakim. The biography details his extensive studies: literature under several teachers in Nishapur, fiqh in Khurasan and Iraq under notable jurists, kalam with Abu Sahl al-Khaliti, and 'ma'ani' with Abu Bakr ibn 'Abdus. He traveled widely for hadith, hearing in Khurasan, Iraq, and the Hijaz, and even went to Yemen for high chains. His piety is highlighted: he avoided rulers, lived on minimal means, and spent his time in the mosque and school. He authored over 300 books and was known for answered prayers. He died in 388 AH at age 72. The passage follows a pattern: chain, education, travels, piety, writings, death.

Correction: The biography shows he studied literature, fiqh, kalam, ma'ani, and hadith, and traveled to multiple regions for each.

The Noble Shaykh Who Speaks with Wisdom: Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un
Biography of the eloquent preacher and mystic Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the character and scholarly stature of Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un as portrayed through the chains of transmission in Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari.

Core Idea
Ibn Sam'un united Sufi wisdom with theological expertise, earning the title 'tongue of the age.'

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's work introduces us to a remarkable figure from Baghdad: Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un. Through two chains of narration, we learn of his eloquence, his mastery of both outward etiquettes and inner sciences, and his unparalleled status as a preacher and theologian. As you read, pay attention to the titles bestowed upon him and the way his contemporaries spoke of him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic text carefully, then follow with the English translation. Notice the flow of the isnads and the descriptions.
The passage contains two separate transmission chains.
2
Identify the two chains
The first chain goes through al-Farsi, al-Muzakki, and al-Sulami; the second through al-Husayni, al-Ghassani, and Ibn Khayrun from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. Note how they corroborate each other.
3
Examine the titles given to Ibn Sam'un
Look for phrases like 'لسان الوقت' (tongue of the age), 'إمام المتكلمين' (imam of the speakers), and 'الشيخ الجليل المنطق بالحكمة' (the noble shaykh who speaks with wisdom). Consider what these reveal about his reputation.
He is praised for both outward adab and inner wisdom.
4
Understand his dual role
The text emphasizes that he was both a master of Sufi sciences (علم الخواطر والاشارات) and an imam of the mutakallimun (theologians). This corrects any misconception that he was only a mystic.
5
Reflect on his legacy
Note that people recorded his wisdoms and many scholars narrated from him. The reverence shown by later shaykhs calling him 'the noble shaykh who speaks with wisdom' underscores his lasting impact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم الشيخ أبو الحسين بن سمعون البغدادي المذكى رحمه الله ) كتب إلى الشيخ أبو الحسن عبد الغافر بن إسماعيل بن عبد الغافر الفارسي من نيسابور قال أنا أبو بكر محمد بن يحيى بن ابراهيم المزكي قال ثنا أبو عبد الرحمن محمد بن الحسين بن موسى السلمي قال : محمد بن أحمد بن سمعون كنيته أبو الحسين من مشايخ البغداديين له لسان عال في هذه العلوم، يعنى علوم أهل التصوف لا ينتمى الى أستاذ وهو لسان الوقت والمرجوع اليه في آداب الظاهر، يذهب إلى أسد المذاهب وهو إمام المتكلمين على هذا اللسان في الوقت لقيته وشاهدته زاد غير المزكي عن السلمي قال : أبو الحسين بن سمعون الذى هو لسان الوقت والمعبر عن الأحوال بالطف بيان مع ما يرجع اليه صحة الاعتقاد وصحبة الفقراء . أخبرنا الشريف أبو القسم على بن ابراهيم الحسيني وأبو الحسن على ابن أحمد الغساني وأبو منصور بن خيرون قالوا قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الحافظ محمد بن أحمد بن إسماعيل بن عنبس بن إسماعيل أبو الحسين الواعظ المعروف بابن سمعون كان واحد دهره وفرد عصره في الكلام على علم الخواطر والاشارات ولسان الوعظ، دوّن الناس حكمه وجمعوا كلامه وحدث عن عبد الله بن أبي داود السجستاني والأحمد بن محمد بن سلم المخرمي ومحمد بن مخلد الدوري ومحمد بن جعفر الطبري ومحمد بن محمد بن أبي حذيفة وأحمد بن سليمان بن زبان الدمشقيين وعمر بن الحسن الشيباني حدثنا عنه حمزة بن محمدبن طاهر الدقاق والقاضي أبو على بن أبي موسى الهاشمي والحسن بن محمد اخلال وأبو بكر الطاهرى وعبد العزيز بن على الأزجى وغيرهم، وكان بعض شيوخنا اذا حدث عنه قال ثنا الشيخ الجليل المنطق بالحكمة أبو الحسين بن سمعون، وحدثني الحسن بن أبي طالب قال سمعت أبا الحسين بن سمعون
And among them is the Sheikh Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un al-Baghdadi al-Muzakki, may Allah have mercy on him. He wrote to the Sheikh Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-Ghafir ibn Isma'il ibn 'Abd al-Ghafir al-Farsi from Nishapur, saying: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Ibrahim al-Muzakki told us, saying: Abu 'Abd al-Rahman Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Musa al-Sulami narrated to us, saying: Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Sam'un, his kunyah is Abu al-Husayn, one of the shaykhs of the Baghdadis, he had a high tongue in these sciences, meaning the sciences of the people of tasawwuf. He does not attribute himself to any teacher, and he is the tongue of the age and the reference in the etiquettes of the outward. He follows the strongest of schools and is the imam of the speakers (mutakallimin) on this tongue of the time. I met him and saw him. Another than al-Muzakki added from al-Sulami: Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un is the tongue of the age, the interpreter of states with the most subtle expression, along with soundness of belief and companionship of the poor. Al-Sharif Abu al-Qasim 'Ali ibn Ibrahim al-Husayni, Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Ahmad al-Ghassani, and Abu Mansur ibn Khayrun informed us, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn 'Ali ibn Thabit al-Hafiz told us: Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Isma'il ibn 'Anbas ibn Isma'il, Abu al-Husayn the preacher, known as Ibn Sam'un, was the unique one of his age and the singular of his time in discourse on the science of inner thoughts and allusions, and the tongue of preaching. People recorded his wisdoms and collected his speech. He narrated from 'Abdullah ibn Abi Dawud al-Sijistani, Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Salm al-Makhrami, Muhammad ibn Makhlad al-Duri, Muhammad ibn Ja'far al-Tabari, Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Hudhayfa, Ahmad ibn Sulayman ibn Zaban al-Dimashqis, and 'Umar ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani. Narrated from him: Hamza ibn Muhammad ibn Tahir al-Daqqaq, al-Qadi Abu 'Ali ibn Abi Musa al-Hashimi, al-Hasan ibn Muhammad Akhllal, Abu Bakr al-Tahiri, 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn 'Ali al-Azaji, and others. Some of our shaykhs, when narrating from him, used to say: 'The noble shaykh who speaks with wisdom, Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un, narrated to us.' Al-Hasan ibn Abi Talib narrated to me, saying: I heard Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un...
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un al-Baghdadi, a renowned preacher and Sufi master. The biography is transmitted through two chains: one via al-Farsi, al-Muzakki, and al-Sulami; another via al-Husayni, al-Ghassani, and Ibn Khayrun from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. The first chain describes him as a shaykh of Baghdad with a 'high tongue' in the sciences of tasawwuf, calling him the 'tongue of the age' and reference in outward etiquettes, following the strongest school and being an imam of the mutakallimun. The second chain, from al-Khatib, adds that he was unparalleled in his time in expounding the science of inner thoughts and allusions, and that his wisdom sayings were collected. It lists his teachers, including 'Abdullah ibn Abi Dawud and others, and his students, including Hamza al-Daqqaq and others. The biography notes the honorific title given to him: 'the noble shaykh who speaks with wisdom.' The account is cut off at 'I heard Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un...' but the provided text is what is available in the window.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Ibn Sam'un was exclusively a Sufi master with no engagement in theology or law.
Correction: The text explicitly says he was an 'imam of the mutakallimun' (theologians) and followed 'the strongest of schools', indicating his expertise in Islamic theology and jurisprudence. He was both a spiritual guide and a scholarly authority.

Key Takeaway

?

If you were to be remembered for your speech, would it be marked by wisdom and truth, or by carelessness and vanity? What specific change can you make today to ensure your words carry weight for Allah's sake?
?
The scholars preserved Ibn Sam'un's wisdoms and collected his speech. What would a transcript of your last week's conversations reveal about your priorities? Are you more concerned with being heard or with speaking what is true?
?

Ibn Sam'un's Spiritual Insight: The Bow and the Dream
Two anecdotes showing Ibn Sam'un's spiritual insight and care for his listeners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the spiritual insight (kashf) of righteous scholars like Ibn Sam'un manifests in their awareness of others' states and their care for their spiritual experiences.

Core Idea
Ibn Sam'un's insight reveals that saints can know hidden thoughts and honor prophetic dreams.

This passage presents two remarkable anecdotes from the life of Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un, showing his supernatural awareness of his listener's private circumstances and his deep respect for a dream of the Prophet. Through these stories, we see how saintly insight (kashf) operates in practice. The author includes them as documented miracles (karamat) of the righteous.

Guided Path
1
Read the first anecdote
Read the story of al-Qawwas's hardship and Ibn Sam'un's warning not to sell his bow and shoes. Notice that Ibn Sam'un knew al-Qawwas's private intention.
2
Read the second anecdote
Read the story of al-Qawwas falling asleep during the sermon and dreaming of the Prophet. Notice that Ibn Sam'un stopped speaking to avoid disturbing him.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider what these stories teach about the spiritual gifts (karamat) of saints and their role in guiding and respecting others' spiritual experiences.
Both stories are transmitted through reliable chains, indicating they are not mere legends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحسن بن البادا يقول سمعت أبا الفتح القواس يقول لحقني إضاقة وقتا من الزمان فنظرت فلم أجد فى البيت غير قوس لى وخفين كنت ألبسهما فأصبحت وقد عزمت على بيعهما وكان يوم مجلس أبى الحسين بن سمعون فقلت في نفسي أحضر المجلس ثم انصرف، فأبيع الخفين والقوس قال وكان القواس قلما يتخلف عن حضور مجلس ابن سمعون قال أبو الفتح فحضرت المجلس فلما أردت الانصراف نادي أبو الحسين يا أبا الفتح لا تبع الخفين ولا تبع القوس فإن الله سيأتيك برزق من عنده أو كما قال . وأخبرنا الشريف أبو القسم والشيخ أبو الحسن بن قبيس قالا ثنا وأبو منصور الخيروني قال انا أبو بكر أحمد بن على الخطيب قال حدثني رئيس الرؤساء شرف الوزراء أبو القسم على بن الحسن قال حدثني أبو طاهر محمد بن على بن العلاف قال حضرت أبا الحسين بن سمعون يوما في مجلس الوعظ وهو جالس على كرسيه يتكلم وكان ابو الفتح القواس جالسا إلى جنب الكرسى فغشيه النعاس ونام فأمسك أبو الحسين عن الكلام ساعة حتى استيقظ أبو الفتح ورفع رأسه فقال له أبو الحسين رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في نومك قال نعم فقال أبو الحسين لذلك أمسكت عن الكلام خوفا ان تنزعج وتنقطع عما كنت فيه او كما قال
Al-Hasan ibn al-Bada said: I heard Abu al-Fath al-Qawwas say: I experienced a time of hardship, and I looked and found nothing in the house except a bow of mine and two shoes I used to wear. I woke up having resolved to sell them. It was the day of the gathering of Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un. I said to myself: I will attend the gathering, then leave, and sell the shoes and the bow. He said: Al-Qawwas would hardly ever miss attending the gathering of Ibn Sam'un. Abu al-Fath said: So I attended the gathering. When I wanted to leave, Abu al-Husayn called out: O Abu al-Fath, do not sell the shoes, and do not sell the bow, for Allah will certainly bring you provision from Him—or something like that. And we were informed by al-Sharif Abu al-Qasim and al-Shaykh Abu al-Hasan ibn Qubays, they said: we were told by Abu Mansur al-Khayruni, he said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali al-Khatib told us, he said: Ra'is al-Ru'asa, Sharaf al-Wuzara Abu al-Qasim Ali ibn al-Hasan told me, he said: Abu Tahir Muhammad ibn Ali ibn al-Allaf told me, he said: I was present with Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un one day in the assembly of preaching, and he was sitting on his chair speaking, while Abu al-Fath al-Qawwas was sitting next to the chair. Drowsiness overcame him and he slept. Abu al-Husayn remained silent for a while until Abu al-Fath awoke and lifted his head. Abu al-Husayn said to him: Did you see the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, in your sleep? He said: Yes. So Abu al-Husayn said: For that reason I remained silent, fearing that you might be disturbed and cut off from what you were experiencing—or something like that.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage contains two separate anecdotes illustrating the spiritual insight (kashf) of Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un. In the first, narrated by al-Qawwas, Ibn Sam'un knows that al-Qawwas is in financial difficulty and intends to sell his bow and shoes. As al-Qawwas is about to leave the gathering, Ibn Sam'un calls out to him, telling him not to sell them, because Allah will provide for him. This demonstrates that Ibn Sam'un had knowledge of al-Qawwas's private thoughts, which is considered a sign of saintly insight. In the second anecdote, narrated by Ibn al-Allaf, al-Qawwas falls asleep during the preaching assembly. Ibn Sam'un stops speaking until al-Qawwas wakes up, and then asks him if he saw the Prophet in his dream. Al-Qawwas confirms this, and Ibn Sam'un explains that he stopped speaking to avoid disturbing him. This shows Ibn Sam'un's concern for his listener's spiritual experience and his awareness of the unseen state of his audience. Both stories are transmitted through reliable chains of narration, as indicated by the multiple isnads. The passage emphasizes the miraculous gifts (karamat) of righteous scholars.

أبو الفتح القواس
إضاقة
قوس
خفين
رئيس الرؤساء

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These stories are just legends or exaggerations.
Correction: The author includes them as documented miracles (karamat) with reliable chains, testifying to the spiritual gifts of righteous scholars.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Ibn Sam'un's ability to know al-Qawwas's private intention and his respect for the prophetic dream demonstrate the reality of saintly miracles (karamat).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face financial hardship, do you first turn to selling what you have, or do you truly expect Allah's provision from unseen sources? What would you need to change in your heart to trust Him more?
?
Ibn Sam'un knew al-Qawwas's secret thought without being told. Are you comfortable with the fact that Allah knows every intention you hide? Which intention are you most ashamed of today, and what will you do about it?
?
If you were in a gathering and fell asleep during a dream of the Prophet, would you expect others to wait for you? How can you show the same respect to the spiritual experiences of those around you, even if you don't understand them?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

Ibn Sam'un's Wisdom in Clearing Suspicion
Ibn Sam'un dispels the caliph's suspicion of his loyalty to Ali by beginning his sermon with praise of him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Sam'un's deliberate choice to start his sermon with praise of Ali ibn Abi Talib cleared the caliph's suspicion and demonstrated his loyalty.

Core Idea
Actions, especially in sensitive matters, can reveal true allegiance.

This lesson presents a biographical anecdote that illustrates how a wise preacher, Ibn Sam'un, handled a false accusation with timely action. The Caliph al-Ta'i' had heard that Ibn Sam'un disparaged Ali ibn Abi Talib and summoned him angrily. Ibn Sam'un, upon entering, began his sermon with praise and traditions of Ali, moving the caliph to tears and clearing all doubt. The story highlights the importance of outward signs in dispelling suspicion.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to understand the sequence of events: the caliph's anger, the summons, Ibn Sam'un's entrance and sermon, and the caliph's explanation.
Pay attention to the caliph's words at the end, which reveal his reasoning.
2
Identify the key action
Notice that Ibn Sam'un's first act upon entering was to mention Ali ibn Abi Talib and narrate from him. This was a deliberate choice that counteracted the suspicion.
The caliph explicitly notes that Ibn Sam'un could have reported from others but chose to start with Ali.
3
Understand the caliph's perspective
Reflect on why the caliph changed from anger to tears. He was testing the truth of the report, and Ibn Sam'un's actions provided evidence of his true stance.
The caliph says he wanted to verify before confronting, showing his justice.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this story teaches the importance of outward signs in proving innocence, and the role of divine inspiration (kushifa) in guiding actions.
The phrase 'perhaps he was inspired' suggests spiritual insight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وحدثنى رئيس الرؤساء ايضا قال حكي لي أبو على بن أبي موسى الهاشمي قال حكى لى دحى مولى الطائع الله قال أمرنى الطائع الله بأن أوجه الى ابن سمعون فأحضره دار الخلافة ورأيت الطائع على صفة من الغضب وكان يتقى في تلك الحال لأنه كان ذا حدة فبعثت الى ابن سمعون وانا منشغول القلب لأجله فلما حضر اعلمت الطائع حضوره فجلس مجلسه وأذن له فى الدخول فدخل وسلم عليه بالخلافة ثم اخذ في وعظه فأول ما ابتدأ به ان قال روى عن امير المؤمنين على بن أبي طالب رضى الله عنه وذكر خبرا وأحاديث بعده ثم قال روى عن أمير المؤمنين على بن أبي طالب كرم وجهه، وذكر عنه خبرا ولم يزل يجرى في ميدان الوعظ حتى بكى الطائع وسمع شهيقه وابتل منديل بين يديه بدموعه فأمسك ابن سمعون حينئذ ودفع إلى الطائع درجا فيه طيب وغيره فدفعته إليه وانصرف، وعدت إلى حضرة الطائع فقلت يا مولاي رأيتك على صفة من شدة الغضب على ابن سمعون ثم انتقلت عن تلك الصفة عند حضوره فما السبب ؟ فقال رفع إلى عنه أنه ينتقص على بن أبي طالب رضی الله عنه فأحببت ان أتيقن ذلك لأقابله عليه ان صح ذلك منه فلما حضر بين يدى افتتح كلامه بذكر على بن أبي طالب والصلاة عليه وأعاد وأبدى في ذلك وقد كان له مندوحة في الرواية عن غيره وترك الابتداء به فعلمت انه وفق لما تزول به عنه الظنة وتبرأ ساحته عندى ولعله كوشف بذلك، او كما قال
He said: And Ra'is al-Ru'asa narrated to me also, he said: Abu Ali ibn Abi Musa al-Hashimi told me, he said: Duhay, the mawla of al-Ta'i' li-Allah, told me, he said: Al-Ta'i' li-Allah commanded me to send for Ibn Sam'un and bring him to the caliphal palace. I saw al-Ta'i' in a state of anger, and he was feared in that state because he was sharp-tempered. So I sent for Ibn Sam'un, and I was anxious about him. When he came, I informed al-Ta'i' of his arrival. He took his seat and allowed him to enter. He entered and greeted him as caliph, then began his preaching. The first thing he started with was: 'It is narrated from the Commander of the Faithful Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him,' and he mentioned a report and traditions after it. Then he said: 'It is narrated from the Commander of the Faithful Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah honor his face,' and he mentioned a report about him. He continued running in the field of preaching until al-Ta'i' wept, and his sobbing was heard, and a handkerchief before him became wet with his tears. Then Ibn Sam'un stopped and handed to al-Ta'i' a scroll containing perfume and other items, and I gave it to him, and he left. I returned to the presence of al-Ta'i' and said: My lord, I saw you in a state of intense anger against Ibn Sam'un, then you changed from that state upon his arrival. What is the reason? He said: It was reported to me that he disparages Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him, so I wanted to verify that to confront him if it was true. When he came before me, he opened his speech by mentioning Ali ibn Abi Talib and sending blessings upon him, and he repeated and elaborated on that, though he could have reported from others and not started with him. So I knew that he was guided to what would remove suspicion from him and clear him in my eyes. Perhaps he was inspired with that—or something like that.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a biographical anecdote showing how Ibn Sam'un dispelled a false accusation. The Caliph al-Ta'i' had heard that Ibn Sam'un disparaged Ali ibn Abi Talib, which angered him. He summoned Ibn Sam'un intending to confront him. Ibn Sam'un, upon entering, began his sermon with praise and traditions of Ali, showing his deep respect. The caliph was moved to tears, and later explained that Ibn Sam'un's deliberate choice to start with Ali (when he could have started with another topic) demonstrated his loyalty and cleared the suspicion. The passage emphasizes that Ibn Sam'un was 'inspired' (kushifa) to act in that way, suggesting divine guidance. This story highlights the importance of outward actions in clearing suspicion, and the role of spiritual insight in awkward situations.

Key Terms
الطائع الله
دحى مولى الطائع
على بن أبي طالب
كوشف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the caliph's anger was based on a false report and he was merely venting.
Correction: The caliph deliberately tested Ibn Sam'un by observing his actions; he did not act on the report alone but sought verification, showing his justice.

Checkpoint
Why did Caliph al-Ta'i' originally become angry with Ibn Sam'un?
A) He failed to attend the caliph's gathering.
B) He was accused of disparaging Ali ibn Abi Talib.
C) He refused to preach in the palace.
D) He praised Ali too much.

Key Takeaway
In times of accusation, wise actions—especially those that directly address the suspicion—can restore trust and reveal one's true character.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face false accusations or suspicion, do you react defensively or do you strategically choose an action that directly addresses the heart of the matter? What would it take for you to adopt Ibn Sam'un's wisdom in your next conflict?
?
Ibn Sam'un could have easily spoken about other topics, but he deliberately began with Ali. Is there a strained relationship in your life where a deliberate, healing action—rather than more words—could change everything? What is one concrete step you can take this week to 'open with what heals'?
?
The caliph's heart softened at the sincerity of Ibn Sam'un's opening. Whose heart needs to be softened by your character today? Are you living in a way that your actions would move others toward trust and tears of repentance? If not, what small course correction can you make right now?
