Death and Burial of Abu al-Husayn Ibn Sam'un
Reports the death date, burial, and later transfer of Ibn Sam'un's remains.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life events of Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un as recorded by Ibn 'Asakir, focusing on his death, burial, and the miracle of his preserved shroud.

Core Idea
Even after decades, the shroud of Ibn Sam'un remained undecayed—a sign of his piety.

This passage reports the death of the preacher Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un in 387 AH, his initial burial in his house, and his later transfer to the Bab Harb cemetery. Most remarkably, his burial shroud was found intact after nearly forty years, indicating God's favor upon him. As we read, note how the historian Ibn 'Asakir transmits this account with careful attention to dates and chain of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to grasp the factual content.
Pay attention to the chain of narrators (isnad) that authenticates the report.
2
Identify the two death dates
Notice that two different dates are mentioned: the middle of Dhu al-Qa'dah (15th) and the 14th. Understand that such variations are common in early records.
The discrepancy may arise from different calender calculations or transmission chains.
3
Examine the burial and transfer details
Observe that he was initially buried in his house in the 'Attabiyin street, then moved to Bab Harb cemetery in 426 AH.
The transfer after 39 years indicates the community's continued reverence for him.
4
Reflect on the miracle of the shroud
The passage concludes with the statement that his shroud had not decayed. Consider why this detail is considered noteworthy.
This is seen as a sign of Allah's blessing on a righteous servant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشريف أبو القسم بن أبي الحسن والشيخ أبو الحسن بن قبيس وغيرهما قالوا ثنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على الحافظ قال أخبرنا أحمد بن محمد العتيقي قال سنة سبع وثمانين وثلاثمائة فيها توفى أبو الحسين بن سمعون الواعظ يوم النصف من ذى القعدة، وكان ثقة مأمونا، قال أبو بكر وذكر لي غير العتيقي انه توفى يوم الخميس الرابع عشر من ذي القعدة ودفن في داره بشارع العتابيين فلم يزل هناك حتى نقل في يوم الخميس الحادي عشر من رجب سنة ست وعشرين واربعمائة فدفن بباب حرب وقيل لي أن أكفانه لم تكن بليت بعد
Al-Sharif Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi al-Hasan and al-Shaykh Abu al-Hasan ibn Qubays and others informed us, they said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali al-Hafiz narrated to us, he said: Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-‘Atiqi told us, he said: In the year 387 AH, in it died Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un the preacher on the middle of Dhu al-Qa‘dah. He was trustworthy and reliable. Abu Bakr said: Someone other than al-‘Atiqi mentioned to me that he died on Thursday, the fourteenth of Dhu al-Qa‘dah, and was buried in his house in the Street of the ‘Attabiyin. He remained there until he was transferred on Thursday, the eleventh of Rajab, in the year 426 AH, and was buried at Bab Harb. It was said to me that his shrouds had not yet decayed.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage provides the death and burial details of Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un. It mentions two conflicting dates: the 15th and the 14th of Dhu al-Qa‘da 387 AH. He was initially buried in his own house in the ‘Attabiyin quarter, then transferred to the famous cemetery of Bab Harb in Baghdad in 426 AH. Notably, his shroud was reportedly found undecayed after nearly 40 years, which is considered a sign of his sanctity. The transmission highlights his reliability (thiqah ma'mun) as a narrator of hadith.

Key Terms
أبو الحسين بن سمعون
الواعظ
ثقة مأمونا
باب حرب
شارع العتابيين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The two death dates are contradictory and one must be false.
Correction: Different chains of transmission or calendar reckonings can produce slightly different dates; such variations are common in early biographical reports and do not necessarily indicate error.

Checkpoint
In which year did Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam'un die according to the main report?
A) 377 AH
B) 387 AH
C) 426 AH
D) 400 AH

Key Takeaway
The report of Ibn Sam'un's undecayed shroud serves as a testament to his exemplary life and the respect he commanded.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your own shroud were exhumed decades from now, would it be as well-preserved as Ibn Sam'un's? What does that reveal about the purity of your current actions and intentions?
?
The report emphasizes that Ibn Sam'un was 'trustworthy and reliable.' In which area of your life do people find you least reliable? What will you change today to earn that description?
?
Ibn Sam'un's body was moved after nearly forty years, yet his shroud was undecayed. What in your spiritual life—your prayers, your charity, your repentance—has not decayed? What one specific deed will you renew right now so it remains fresh before Allah?

Short entry on a scholar's expertise and death date.

One scholar could master theology, legal documents, and medicine.

This passage introduces us to Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Shuruti al-Jurjani, a mutakallim on the Sunnite school. His expertise in shurut (legal documents) and medicine shows that kalam scholars were often polymaths. Let's read the entry.

Ibn Sam'un: Cleared of Suspicion
Ibn Asakir narrates an anecdote about Ibn Sam'un and records his death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the importance of verifying rumors about scholars and the narrative of Ibn Sam'un's death and burial, including the miraculous preservation of his shroud.

Core Idea
A rumor can be dispelled by witnessing the truth firsthand.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's history recounts an incident where the author was initially angered by a rumor about the preacher Ibn Sam'un disparaging Ali ibn Abi Talib. However, when he met Ibn Sam'un, he observed him beginning his speech with praise of Ali, which immediately cleared the suspicion. The passage then records Ibn Sam'un's death and the remarkable condition of his burial shroud years later.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote of anger and suspicion
Read the passage carefully. Notice that the author admits to being angry at Ibn Sam'un based on a rumor. Then ask yourself: why did the author change his mind?
The author was not biased; he waited to verify.
2
Observe the method of verification
The author attended Ibn Sam'un's gathering. See how Ibn Sam'un began his speech—by praising Ali ibn Abi Talib and praying for him. The author realized the rumor was false.
The author says Ibn Sam'un 'was guided' to remove suspicion.
3
Examine the death record and the shroud
Read the death notice: Ibn Sam'un died in 387 AH, was initially buried in his house, and later moved to Bab Harb. The surprising detail is that his burial shroud had not decayed.
This detail suggests his piety and respect.
4
Reflect on the lessons
Consider how this story teaches us to verify accusations against scholars and the blessing of a pious life. The preservation of the shroud is seen as a miracle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الغضب على ابن سمعون ثم انتقلت عن تلك الصفة عند حضوره فما السبب ؟ فقال رفع إلى عنه أنه ينتقص على بن أبي طالب رضی الله عنه فأحببت ان أتيقن ذلك لأقابله عليه ان صح ذلك منه فلما حضر بين يدى افتتح كلامه بذكر على بن أبي طالب والصلاة عليه وأعاد وأبدى في ذلك وقد كان له مندوحة في الرواية عن غيره وترك الابتداء به فعلمت انه وفق لما تزول به عنه الظنة وتبرأ ساحته عندى ولعله كوشف بذلك، او كما قال . أخبرنا الشريف أبو القسم بن أبي الحسن والشيخ أبو الحسن بن قبيس وغيرهما قالوا ثنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على الحافظ قال أخبرنا أحمد بن محمد العتيقي قال سنة سبع وثمانين وثلاثمائة فيها توفى أبو الحسين بن سمعون الواعظ يوم النصف من ذى القعدة، وكان ثقة مأمونا، قال أبو بكر وذكر لي غير العتيقي انه توفى يوم الخميس الرابع عشر من ذي القعدة ودفن في داره بشارع العتابيين فلم يزل هناك حتى نقل في يوم الخميس الحادي عشر من رجب سنة ست وعشرين واربعمائة فدفن بباب حرب وقيل لي أن أكفانه لم تكن بليت بعد
(I heard) anger at Ibn Sam'un, then (my) repulsion from that description (of him) when he was present. So what is the reason? He said: It was reported to me that he disparages Ali ibn Abi Talib (رضی الله عنه), so I wanted to ascertain that in order to confront him about it if that turned out to be true from him. When he came before me, he opened his speech with the mention of Ali ibn Abi Talib and prayer upon him, and he repeated and began (with that), and he had ample room to narrate from others and to avoid beginning with him. So I knew that he was guided to what would remove the suspicion (against him) and clear his reputation with me. Perhaps he was made aware of that (unseen), or as he said. Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi al-Hasan and Shaykh Abu al-Hasan ibn Qubays and others informed us: they said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali al-Hafiz narrated to us, he said: Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Atiqi informed us, he said: In the year 387 AH, on the fifteenth of Dhu al-Qa‘da, Abu al-Husayn ibn Sam‘un the preacher died. He was trustworthy and reliable. Abu Bakr said: Someone other than al-Atiqi mentioned to me that he died on Thursday, the fourteenth of Dhu al-Qa‘da, and was buried in his house in the street of al-‘Attabiyyin, and he remained there until he was moved on Thursday, the eleventh of Rajab of the year 426 AH, and was buried at Bab Harb. And it was said to me that his shrouds had not yet decayed.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a biographical anecdote and death record. It begins with the author's reported anger at Ibn Sam'un due to a rumor that he disparaged Ali ibn Abi Talib. To verify this, he attended Ibn Sam'un's session and found that he actually began his speech by praising and praying for Ali, leaving no room for the rumor. Thus the suspicion was cleared. The author then gives a chain of narration for the death report: Ibn Sam'un died in 387 AH, with two slightly different dates given. He is described as trustworthy (thiqah ma'mun). He was buried in his house initially, then moved in 426 AH to Bab Harb, and it was said that his shrouds had not decayed. This indicates his piety and the respect held for him.

Key Terms
ابن سمعون
الظنة
ثقة مأمون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The anecdote condemns Ibn Sam'un as a disparager of Ali.
Correction: The anecdote actually clears Ibn Sam'un; the author's suspicion was removed when he witnessed Ibn Sam'un praising Ali.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Biography of Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Shuruti
Ibn Asakir gives a short biographical notice of Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Shuruti.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the biographical details and areas of expertise of Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Shuruti as recorded by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
A Sunni theologian who mastered documents and medicine.

This lesson presents a concise biography of Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Shuruti, a figure known for his expertise in theology, legal documents, and medicine. As we read Ibn Asakir's entry, we will see how the author highlights his scholarly breadth within a few lines.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and the chain
Notice how Ibn Asakir begins with the name 'Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Shuruti al-Jurjani' and provides a chain of narrators for this information. This typical format indicates reliability.
The chain includes three narrators: Abu al-Qasim ibn al-Samarqandi, Abu al-Qasim al-Jurjani, and Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf.
2
Understand his primary description
He is described as a mutakallim (theologian) 'ala madhhab al-sunnah (on the school of the Sunnah). This means he adhered to Sunni creed and engaged in theological discourse.
3
Note his additional knowledge
He was knowledgeable in al-shurut (documents/conditions) and al-tibb (medicine). This shows his multidisciplinary expertise beyond mere theology.
Al-shurut refers to legal documents and conditions in contracts.
4
His hadith studies
He 'wrote hadith' from Abu Ya'qub al-Nahwi and those of his rank. This indicates he was active in hadith transmission and recording.
His teachers include Abu Ya'qub al-Nahwi, a known grammarian and hadith scholar.
5
His death date
He died in the year 389 AH. This places him in the late 4th century Hijri, around the 10th century CE.

Biography of Abu Ali al-Sarakhsi
Ibn Asakir provides a detailed biography of Abu Ali al-Sarakhsi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, teachers, and scholarly legacy of Abu Ali al-Sarakhsi as recorded by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
A scholar’s journey—from Khurasan to Iraq—shapes a legacy in Qur’an, fiqh, and hadith.

Ibn Asakir presents a biographical entry for Zahir ibn Ahmad al-Sarakhsi, a renowned scholar of the 4th/10th century. This passage traces his educational travels, the great teachers he studied under, and his multifaceted expertise. Through this lesson, you will see how classical scholars documented the lives of their predecessors, preserving both their chains of transmission and their contributions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage with translation
Start by reading the source text in Arabic, then follow it with the English translation. Pay attention to the chain of transmission (isnad) at the beginning.
Notice that Ibn Asakir cites his own teacher, forming a chain back to al-Hakim al-Nishapuri.
2
Identify al-Sarakhsi's scholarly roles
The passage describes him as al-Muqri’, al-Faqih, al-Muhaddith. Make a mental note of each role and think about how they connect to his teachers.
He was not just a jurist but also a Qur'an reciter and hadith scholar.
3
Trace his educational journey
Notice the places he traveled to (Khurasan, Iraq) and his teachers listed. Then note his studies in Qur’an, fiqh, and adab. Finally, his death age and date.
His journey (rihla) in 315 AH and return to Nishapur in 338 AH show a long period of seeking knowledge.

And among them is Abu ‘Ali al-Faqih al-Sarakhsi, may Allah have mercy on him. His journey was in the year 315 AH, and he returned to Nishapur in 338 AH, when our shaykhs were abundant. He stayed with us for a year attending the circles of our shaykhs. I heard his debate at that time in the circle of Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ishaq and others. He had recited the Qur’an to Abu Bakr ibn Mujahid, studied fiqh under Abu Ishaq al-Marwazi, and studied literature under Abu Bakr ibn al-Anbari and Muhammad ibn Yawm al-Arba‘a’ al-Suli and their peers. Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about Zahir ibn Ahmad al-Sarakhsi, also known as Abu ‘Ali al-Faqih. It begins with the chain of transmission for this information. He is described as a reciter (muqri'), jurist (faqih), hadith scholar (muhaddith), and the shaykh of his time in Khurasan. His teachers are listed: in Khurasan, he heard from Abu Labid Muhammad ibn Idris and his contemporaries; in Iraq, he heard from several prominent scholars such as al-Baghawi and Ibn Sa‘id. His journey (rihla) occurred in 315 AH, and he returned to Nishapur in 338 AH, when many shaykhs were present. He stayed for a year attending their circles. The narrator (al-Hakim) says he heard his debate in the circle of Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ishaq. His education included Qur'an recitation under Ibn Mujahid, fiqh under Abu Ishaq al-Marwazi, and literature (adab) under Abu Bakr al-Anbari and others. The entry concludes with his death at the end of Rabi‘ al-Akhar 389 AH at the age of ninety-six.

Core Idea
A single biography can reveal the scholarly chains, travels, and intellectual legacy of early Islamic scholars.

This passage presents a detailed biographical entry for Zahir ibn Ahmad al-Sarakhsi, passed down through a chain of transmission that includes the famous hadith scholars al-Bayhaqi and al-Hakim al-Naysaburi. As you read, observe how the biography not only narrates his life events but also connects him to the broader network of Islamic learning across Khorasan and Iraq.

The Life and Legacy of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili
Biographical entry for Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili, highlighting his scholarly and pious life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life, scholarly contributions, and pious character of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili, a leading jurist and usuli of the fourth century.

Core Idea
Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili combined deep scholarship in fiqh, usul, and kalam with extraordinary piety and generosity.

This lesson introduces us to Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili, a towering figure from Jurjan. As a student of the students of Imam al-Ash'ari, he authored significant works on usul al-fiqh and taught generations of scholars. His biography, recorded by the historian al-Sahmi, highlights not only his intellectual achievements but also his character and the miraculous honours accorded to him at his death.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the full Arabic biography once, noting the flow from lineage to death. Let the author's own narration guide you through the scholar's life.
The passage is taken from Tarikh Jurjan by al-Sahmi.
2
Identify his scholarly achievements
Note his mastery in fiqh, usul, Arabic, calligraphy, and kalam, and his authored books Tahdhib al-Nazar and al-Ashriba.
This shows the breadth of his learning.
3
Reflect on his character
The text lists many praiseworthy qualities. Count how many are mentioned and consider them as ideals for a scholar.
Piety, generosity, and good character are emphasised.
4
Examine the honors at death
Notice the two honors: dying while reciting the Quran in prayer and losing all his wealth before death. Think about why these are considered honors.
This aligns with the tradition of prophets and saints dying poor.
5
Connect to his legacy
How does this biography reflect the ideal of a scholar in the Ash'ari tradition? Consider the combination of knowledge, action, and divine favor.
This biography is a model for aspiring scholars.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر بعض الطبقة الثانية وهم أصحاب أصحابه كه ممن سلك مسلكه في الأصول وتأدب بآدابه فمنهم أبو سعد بن أبي بكر الإسماعيلى الجرجانی رحمه الله ) أخبرنا أبو القسم بن أبي بكر الدلال قال أنا أبو القسم بن أبي الفضل الجرجان قال أنا أبو القسم حمزة بن يوسف بن إبراهيم السهمي في كتاب تاريخ جرجان قال : إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل بن العباس أبو سعد الإسماعيلى كان أمام زمانه مقدما في الفقه وأصول الفقه والعربية والكتابة والشروط والكلام صنف في أصول الفقه كتاباً كبيراً سماه ( تهذيب النظر ( وله كتاب الأشربة رد على الجصاص درس الفقه سنين كثيرة وتخرج على يده جماعة من الفقهاء من أهل جرجان وطبرستان وغيرهما من البلدان وكان فيه من الخصال المحمودة التي لا تحصى من الورع الثخين والمجاهدة في العبادة والعلم والاهتمام بأمور الدين والنصيحة للإسلام وحسن الخلق وطلاقة الوجه والسخاء في الاطعام وبذل المال ومالا أقدر أن أحصيه رحمة الله عليه ورضوانه ، حججت معه سنة أربع وثمانين حيث رجع من نصف البادية وحج في سنة خمس وثمانين إلى أن رجع إلى وطنه كنت معه لم أره تغير عن خلقه النفس كان معظما مبجلا في جميع البلدان . روى عن أبي بكر محمد بن إبراهيم الشافعي ومحمد بن أسحق الفاكهى ودعلج وعن الأصم محمد بن يعقوب حديثاً واحداً وعن عبد الله ابن عدى كتاب الضعفاء وجمعه مسند مالك بن أنس ، توفى ليلة الجمعة النصف من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة ست وتسعين وثلاثمائة وصلى عليه أخوه أبو نصر الإسماعيلى فى صحراء باب الخندق فى جمع عظيم لم أر مثل ذلك الجمع بجرجان في تشييع جنازة أحد قط ودفن عند رأس والده أبى بكر الإسماعيلي توفى وهو ابن ثلاث وستين سنة ومما أكرمه الله به ورفع قدره به أنه مات وهو في صلاة المغرب يقرأ ( إياك نعبد وإياك نستعين ففاضت نفسه ومما أكرمه الله به أنه حين قربت وفاته ذهب منه ما كان يملكه من المال والضياع وكان يوجه القطن إلى باب الأبواب جميع فغرق الجميع في البحر وكانت له بضاعة تحمل من أصبهان فوقع عليها
Mention of some of the second stratum, and they are the students of his students, among those who followed his path in principles and were nurtured by his manners. Among them is Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Bakr al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani, may Allah have mercy on him. Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Bakr al-Dallal informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi al-Fadl al-Jurjani narrated to us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf ibn Ibrahim al-Sahmi narrated to us in the book Tarikh Jurjan, saying: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-'Abbas, Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili, was the imam of his time, foremost in jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, Arabic language, calligraphy, conditions of contracts, and kalam. He authored a large book on principles of jurisprudence called Tahdhib al-Nazar, and he wrote the book al-Ashriba as a refutation of al-Jassas. He taught jurisprudence for many years, and under his hand there graduated a group of jurists from the people of Jurjan, Tabaristan, and other lands. He possessed praiseworthy qualities that cannot be enumerated, such as intense piety, striving in worship, knowledge, concern for religious affairs, sincere advice to Islam, good character, a cheerful face, generosity in feeding others, and spending of wealth – I cannot enumerate them all. May Allah's mercy and pleasure be upon him. I performed Hajj with him in the year 384, when he returned from the middle of the desert, and he performed Hajj in the year 385 until he returned to his homeland. I was with him and did not see him change from his nature; he was revered and respected in all lands. He narrated from Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Shafi'i, Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Fakihi, Da'laj, and from al-Asamm Muhammad ibn Ya'qub one hadith, and from 'Abd Allah ibn 'Adi the book al-Du'afa', and he collected the Musnad of Malik ibn Anas. He died on Friday night, the middle of Rabi' al-Akhir of the year 396 AH. His brother Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili prayed over him in the desert of Bab al-Khandaq in a huge gathering; I have never seen such a crowd in Jurjan for a funeral procession. He was buried at the head of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. He died at the age of sixty-three. Among the honors that Allah bestowed upon him and elevated his rank was that he died while reciting in the Maghrib prayer 'Iyyaka na'budu wa iyyaka nasta'in' and his soul departed. And among the honors that Allah bestowed upon him was that when his death approached, he lost all the wealth and properties he possessed. He used to send cotton to Bab al-Abwab all together, and all of it sank in the sea. He also had merchandise being carried from Isfahan, and it [the ship?] met with [an accident]...

Commentary
This passage introduces the second stratum of scholars associated with the author's teacher's students. It then provides a biography of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili. The text first gives his full name and then lists his scholarly achievements in fiqh, usul, Arabic, etc. It mentions his authored works and his teaching. It highlights his virtuous qualities. Then it describes his Hajj journey with the narrator. It lists his teachers and narrations. Finally, it records his death in 396 AH at age 63, with a miraculous sign: he died while reciting a verse in prayer. It also notes that he lost his wealth before his death.

والكتابة والشروط والكلام صنف في أصول الفقه كتاباً كبيراً سماه تهذيب النظر وله كتاب الأشربة رد على الجصاص درس الفقه سنين كثيرة وتخرج على يده جماعة من الفقهاء من أهل جرجان وطبرستان وغيرهما من البلدان وكان فيه من الخصال المحمودة التي لا تحصى من الورع الثخين والمجاهدة في العبادة والعلم والاهتمام بأمور الدين والنصيحة للإسلام وحسن الخلق وطلاقة الوجه والسخاء في الإطعام وبذل المال ومالا أقدر أن أحصيه رحمة الله عليه ورضوانه حججت معه سنة أربع وثمانين حيث رجع من نصف البادية وحج في سنة خمس وثمانين إلى أن رجع إلى وطنه كنت معه لم أره تغير عن خلقه النفس كان معظما مبجلا في جميع البلدان روى عن أبي بكر محمد بن إبراهيم الشافعي ومحمد بن أسحق الفاكهى ودعلج وعن الأصم محمد بن يعقوب حديثاً واحداً وعن عبد الله ابن عدى كتاب الضعفاء وجمعه مسند مالك بن أنس توفى ليلة الجمعة النصف من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة ست وتسعين وثلاثمائة وصلى عليه أخوه أبو نصر الإسماعيلى فى صحراء باب الخندق فى جمع عظيم لم أر مثل ذلك الجمع بجرجان في تشييع جنازة أحد قط ودفن عند رأس والده أبى بكر الإسماعيلي توفى وهو ابن ثلاث وستين سنة ومما أكرمه الله به ورفع قدره به أنه مات وهو في صلاة المغرب يقرأ إياك نعبد وإياك نستعين ففاضت نفسه ومما أكرمه الله به أنه حين قربت وفاته ذهب منه ما كان يملكه من المال والضياع وكان يوجه القطن إلى باب الأبواب جميع فغرق الجميع في البحر وكانت له بضاعة تحمل من أصبهان فوقع عليها الأكراد فأخذوها وكان يحمل له من خراسان شئ من الحنطة فوقع عليه قوم وأغاروا عليه وكان له ضيعة بقرية تعرف بكوشكى أمر قابوس بن وشمكير أن يقلع أشجارها فقلع جميع ذلك وكبست القناة وقبض جميع ضياعه وخلف من الأولاد أبا معمر المفضل وأبا العلاء السرى وأبا سعيد سعد وأبا الفضل مسعدة وأبا الحسن مبشر وابنتين فأما أبو معمر فصار أماماً مقدماً في العلوم وأبو العلاء فإنه أيضاً صار عالماً في الفقه والأدب حضرت يوما مجلس الإمام أبي بكر الإسماعيلي على باب داره ننتظر خروجه فخرج الإمام أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم الإسماعيلي وهو مستبشر وبيده جزء فجلس وقال أنشدنى ابنى أبو سعد وأنشدنا ثم أنشدنا الإمام أبو سعد بعد ما أنشدنا والده عنه أنى أدخرت ليوم ورد منیتی عند الإله من الأمور خطيرا وهو اليقين بأنه الأحد الذي مازلت منه بفضله مغمورا وشهادتي أن النبي محمدا كان الرسول مبشراً ونذيرا وبراءتي من كل شرك قاله من لا يقر بفعله مبرورا ومحبتي آل النبي وصحبه كلا أراه بالجميل جديرا وتمسكى بالشافعي وعلمه ذاك الذي فتق العلوم بحورا وجميل ظني بالاله لما جنت نفسى وأن حرمت على شرورا أن الظلوم لنفسه إن يأته مستغفراً يجد الآله غفورا فاشهد الهي أننى مستغفر لا أستطيع لما مننت شكوراً هذا الذى أعددته لشدائدي وكفى بربی هاديا ونصيرا أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور الغساني وأبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى قالا قال لنا الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر أحمد ابن على بن ثابت الخطيب إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل ابن العباس أبو سعد الجرجاني المعروف بالإسماعيلى ورد بغداد غير مرة وآخر وروده كان في حياة أبي الحسن الدارقطني وحدث عن أبيه أبي بكر الإسماعيلي وعن أبي العباس الأصم النيسابورى ومحمد بن أحمد ابن
He mentioned some of the second stratum, who are the companions of his companions, those who followed his path in principles and were disciplined by his manners. Among them is Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Bakr al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani, may God have mercy on him. Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Bakr al-Dallal informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi al-Fadl al-Jurjani informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf ibn Ibrahim al-Sahmi informed us in the book 'History of Jurjan', saying: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili was the imam of his time, foremost in jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, Arabic language, writing, conditions, and theology. He authored a large book on principles of jurisprudence called 'Tahdhib al-Nazar', and he has a book on beverages refuting al-Jassas. He taught jurisprudence for many years, and a group of jurists from Jurjan, Tabaristan, and other regions graduated under him. He possessed praiseworthy qualities that cannot be counted: deep piety, striving in worship and knowledge, concern for religious affairs, sincerity to Islam, good character, cheerfulness, generosity in feeding others, and spending wealth—I cannot enumerate it all. May God's mercy and pleasure be upon him. I performed Hajj with him in the year 384, when he returned from halfway through the desert, and he performed Hajj in 385 until he returned to his homeland. I was with him; I never saw him change from his noble character. He was honored and revered in all countries. He narrated from Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Shafi'i, Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Fakihi, Da'laj, and from al-Asamm Muhammad ibn Ya'qub one hadith, and from Abdullah ibn Adi the book 'al-Du'afa', and he collected the Musnad of Malik ibn Anas. He died on the night of Friday, the middle of Rabi' al-Akhir, in the year 396. His brother Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili prayed over him in the desert of Bab al-Khandaq in a huge crowd—I never saw such a crowd in Jurjan for anyone's funeral procession. He was buried at the head of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. He died at the age of sixty-three. Among the honors God bestowed upon him and elevated his rank thereby was that he died while performing the Maghrib prayer reciting 'You alone we worship, and You alone we ask for help', and his soul departed. And among the honors God bestowed upon him was that when his death approached, the wealth and estates he owned left him. He used to send cotton to Bab al-Abwab, and all of it sank in the sea. He had merchandise carried from Isfahan, and Kurds attacked and took it. He had some wheat brought from Khurasan, and a group attacked and looted it. He had an estate in a village known as Kushki; Qabus ibn Wushmagir ordered its trees to be uprooted, so all that was uprooted, the canal was blocked, and all his estates were seized. He left behind from his children: Abu Mu'mar al-Mufaddal, Abu al-'Ala' al-Sari, Abu Sa'id Sa'd, Abu al-Fadl Mas'ada, Abu al-Hasan Mubashshir, and two daughters. As for Abu Mu'mar, he became an imam foremost in the sciences; and Abu al-'Ala', he also became a scholar in jurisprudence and literature. One day I attended the gathering of Imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili at the door of his house, waiting for his exit. Then Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Isma'ili came out, beaming, with a volume in his hand. He sat down and said: 'My son Abu Sa'd recited to me,' and he recited to us. Then Imam Abu Sa'd recited to us after his father had recited to us from him: 'I have stored up for the day of my death a serious matter with God: it is certainty that He is the One, with whose favor I have always been overwhelmed; and my testimony that Muhammad is the Prophet, a bringer of good news and a warner; and my disassociation from every polytheism uttered by one who does not acknowledge His action, approved; and my love for the family of the Prophet and his Companions, all of them I see as worthy of good; and my adherence to al-Shafi'i and his knowledge—that is he who split open the seas of knowledge; and my good opinion of God, even though my soul has committed evil and [even though] I am deprived of evils; that the one who is unjust to himself, if he comes to Him seeking forgiveness, he finds God forgiving. So bear witness, my God, that I am seeking forgiveness—I cannot be sufficiently grateful for what You have bestowed. This is what I have prepared for my hardships—sufficient is my Lord as a Guide and Helper.' The shaykh Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Ghassani and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri' informed us, both saying: The shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas Abu Sa'd al-Jurjani, known as al-Isma'ili, visited Baghdad more than once, and his last visit was during the lifetime of Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni. He narrated from his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, from Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm al-Naysaburi, and from Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn...
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili (d. 396 AH). It begins by placing him among the second stratum of scholars who followed the path of the author's teacher. The passage then details his full name, his status as an imam, his expertise in numerous fields including jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, Arabic, writing, conditions, and theology. He authored a major work on usul al-fiqh called 'Tahdhib al-Nazar' and a refutation of al-Jassas on beverages. He taught for many years and many students graduated from him. The author then lists his praiseworthy qualities: deep piety, striving, good character, generosity, etc. The author mentions that he performed Hajj with him twice and observed his consistent noble character. Next, the passage lists his teachers and narrations: from al-Shafi'i, al-Fakihi, Da'laj, al-Asamm, and Ibn 'Adi, and he collected Malik's Musnad. Then the death: on a Friday night in Rabi' al-Akhir 396, at age 63, prayed over by his brother, buried near his father. A notable honor: he died while reciting 'Iyyaka na'budu wa iyyaka nasta'in' in Maghrib prayer. Additionally, before his death, all his wealth and properties were taken from him through a series of misfortunes: cotton lost at sea, merchandise taken by Kurds, wheat looted, and an estate ordered destroyed by Qabus ibn Wushmagir. This was a sign of honor, as he left the world detached. He left several children, among whom two became scholars. The passage then includes a poem composed by Abu Sa'd, which he recited to his father and then to the author. The poem expresses his preparation for death: certainty in God's oneness, testimony of prophethood, disassociation from shirk, love for the Prophet's family and Companions, adherence to al-Shafi'i, and hope in God's forgiveness. The final part is a report from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi confirming that al-Isma'ili visited Baghdad multiple times, with his last visit during the lifetime of al-Daraqutni, and that he narrated from his father and al-Asamm. The text cuts off mid-chain likely continuing to list more teachers.

What is the name of Abu Sa'd's major work on principles of jurisprudence?
A) Tahdhib al-Nazar
B) Kitab al-Ashriba

D) Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya

Key Takeaway
Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili was a versatile scholar whose expertise spanned multiple Islamic sciences and who authored a foundational work on usul al-fiqh.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Sa'd was given mastery over multiple sciences. Which single discipline have you truly mastered for the sake of Allah? If none, what is your first step to change that starting today?
?
He taught for many years and produced students from distant lands. Who are the people you are investing in—are you actively teaching and mentoring others in the deen, or are you keeping knowledge to yourself?
?
He wrote a refutation of al-Jassas, showing courage in scholarly debate. When was the last time you stood up for a truth you knew, even if it meant confronting a popular opinion or a respected figure?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
The Virtues of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili
Enumeration of Abu Sa'd's moral and spiritual virtues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the virtues that defined Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili's character, including piety, striving, good character, and generosity.

Core Idea
A scholar of deep piety and generosity, whose virtues were too many to enumerate.

After establishing his scholarly credentials, the biography turns to Abu Sa'd's personal qualities. The passage lists a series of praiseworthy traits that defined his character, emphasizing his spiritual and moral excellence. This lesson focuses on understanding those virtues.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of virtues
Read the Arabic and translation, noting each virtue mentioned.
The list includes both internal traits (piety, striving) and external ones (generosity, cheerfulness).
2
Analyze the emphasis
The author says the virtues are uncountable. Reflect on what this suggests about his rank.
3
Connect to his scholarly life
Consider how these virtues complement his scholarly achievements.

ذكر بعض الطبقة الثانية وهم أصحاب أصحابه ممن سلك مسلكه في الأصول وتأدب بآدابه فمنهم أبو سعد بن أبي بكر الإسماعيلى الجرجانى رحمه الله أخبرنا أبو القسم بن أبي بكر الدلال قال أنا أبو القسم بن أبي الفضل الجرجان قال أنا أبو القسم حمزة بن يوسف بن إبراهيم السهمي في كتاب تاريخ جرجان قال إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل بن العباس أبو سعد الإسماعيلى كان أمام زمانه مقدما في الفقه وأصول الفقه والعربية والكتابة والشروط والكلام صنف في أصول الفقه كتاباً كبيراً سماه تهذيب النظر وله كتاب الأشربة رد على الجصاص درس الفقه سنين كثيرة وتخرج على يده جماعة من الفقهاء من أهل جرجان وطبرستان وغيرهما من البلدان رحمة الله عليه ورضوانه حججت معه سنة أربع وثمانين حيث رجع من نصف البادية وحج في سنة خمس وثمانين إلى أن رجع إلى وطنه كنت معه لم أره تغير عن خلقه النفس كان معظما مبجلا في جميع البلدان روى عن أبي بكر محمد بن إبراهيم الشافعي ومحمد بن أسحق الفاكهى ودعلج وعن الأصم محمد بن يعقوب حديثاً واحداً وعن عبد الله ابن عدى كتاب الضعفاء وجمعه مسند مالك بن أنس توفى ليلة الجمعة النصف من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة ست وتسعين أكرمه الله به ورفع قدره به أنه مات وهو في صلاة المغرب يقرأ إياك نعبد وإياك نستعين ففاضت نفسه ومما أكرمه الله به أنه حين قربت وفاته ذهب منه ما كان يملكه من المال والضياع وكان يوجه القطن إلى باب الأبواب جميع فغرق الجميع في البحر وكانت له بضاعة تحمل من أصبهان فوقع عليها الأكراد فأخذوها وكان يحمل له من خراسان شئ من الحنطة فوقع عليه قوم وأغاروا عليه وكان له ضيعة بقرية تعرف بكوشكى أمر قابوس بن وشمكير أن يقلع أشجارها فقلع جميع ذلك وكبست القناة وقبض جميع ضياعه وخلف من الأولاد أبا معمر المفضل وأبا العلاء السرى وأبا سعيد سعد وأبا الفضل مسعدة وأبا الحسن مبشر وابنتين فأما أبو معمر فصار أماماً مقدماً في العلوم وأبو العلاء فإنه أيضاً صار عالماً في الفقه والأدب حضرت يوما مجلس الإمام أبي بكر الإسماعيلي على باب داره ننتظر خروجه فخرج الإمام أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم الإسماعيلي وهو مستبشر وبيده جزء فجلس وقال أنشدنى ابنى أبو سعد وأنشدنا ثم أنشدنا الإمام أبو سعد بعد ما أنشدنا والده عنه أنى أدخرت ليوم ورد منیتی عند الإله من الأمور خطيرا وهو اليقين بأنه الأحد الذي مازلت منه بفضله مغمورا وشهادتي أن النبي محمدا كان الرسول مبشراً ونذيرا وبراءتي من كل شرك قاله من لا يقر بفعله مبرورا ومحبتي آل النبي وصحبه كلا أراه بالجميل جديرا وتمسكى بالشافعي وعلمه ذاك الذي فتق العلوم بحورا وجميل ظني بالاله لما جنت نفسى وأن حرمت على شرورا أن الظلوم لنفسه إن يأته مستغفراً يجد الآله غفورا فاشهد الهي أننى مستغفر لا أستطيع لما مننت شكوراً هذا الذى أعددته لشدائدي وكفى بربی هاديا ونصيرا أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور الغساني وأبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى قالا قال لنا الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر أحمد ابن على بن ثابت الخطيب إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل ابن العباس أبو سعد الجرجاني المعروف بالإسماعيلى ورد بغداد غير مرة وآخر وروده كان في حياة أبي الحسن الدارقطني وحدث عن أبيه أبي بكر الإسماعيلي وعن أبي العباس الأصم النيسابورى ومحمد بن أحمد ابن
He mentioned some of the second stratum, who are the companions of his companions, those who followed his path in principles and were disciplined by his manners. Among them is Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Bakr al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani, may God have mercy on him. Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Bakr al-Dallal informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi al-Fadl al-Jurjani informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf ibn Ibrahim al-Sahmi informed us in the book 'History of Jurjan', saying: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili was the imam of his time, foremost in jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, Arabic language, writing, conditions, and theology. He authored a large book on principles of jurisprudence called 'Tahdhib al-Nazar', and he has a book on beverages refuting al-Jassas. He taught jurisprudence for many years, and a group of jurists from Jurjan, Tabaristan, and other regions graduated under him. He possessed praiseworthy qualities that cannot be counted: deep piety, striving in worship and knowledge, concern for religious affairs, sincerity to Islam, good character, cheerfulness, generosity in feeding others, and spending wealth—I cannot enumerate it all. May God's mercy and pleasure be upon him. I performed Hajj with him in the year 384, when he returned from halfway through the desert, and he performed Hajj in 385 until he returned to his homeland. I was with him; I never saw him change from his noble character. He was honored and revered in all countries. He narrated from Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Shafi'i, Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Fakihi, Da'laj, and from al-Asamm Muhammad ibn Ya'qub one hadith, and from Abdullah ibn Adi the book 'al-Du'afa', and he collected the Musnad of Malik ibn Anas. He died on the night of Friday, the middle of Rabi' al-Akhir, in the year 396. His brother Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili prayed over him in the desert of Bab al-Khandaq in a huge crowd—I never saw such a crowd in Jurjan for anyone's funeral procession. He was buried at the head of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. He died at the age of sixty-three. Among the honors God bestowed upon him and elevated his rank thereby was that he died while performing the Maghrib prayer reciting 'You alone we worship, and You alone we ask for help', and his soul departed. And among the honors God bestowed upon him was that when his death approached, the wealth and estates he owned left him. He used to send cotton to Bab al-Abwab, and all of it sank in the sea. He had merchandise carried from Isfahan, and Kurds attacked and took it. He had some wheat brought from Khurasan, and a group attacked and looted it. He had an estate in a village known as Kushki; Qabus ibn Wushmagir ordered its trees to be uprooted, so all that was uprooted, the canal was blocked, and all his estates were seized. He left behind from his children: Abu Mu'mar al-Mufaddal, Abu al-'Ala' al-Sari, Abu Sa'id Sa'd, Abu al-Fadl Mas'ada, Abu al-Hasan Mubashshir, and two daughters. As for Abu Mu'mar, he became an imam foremost in the sciences; and Abu al-'Ala', he also became a scholar in jurisprudence and literature. One day I attended the gathering of Imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili at the door of his house, waiting for his exit. Then Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Isma'ili came out, beaming, with a volume in his hand. He sat down and said: 'My son Abu Sa'd recited to me,' and he recited to us. Then Imam Abu Sa'd recited to us after his father had recited to us from him: 'I have stored up for the day of my death a serious matter with God: it is certainty that He is the One, with whose favor I have always been overwhelmed; and my testimony that Muhammad is the Prophet, a bringer of good news and a warner; and my disassociation from every polytheism uttered by one who does not acknowledge His action, approved; and my love for the family of the Prophet and his Companions, all of them I see as worthy of good; and my adherence to al-Shafi'i and his knowledge—that is he who split open the seas of knowledge; and my good opinion of God, even though my soul has committed evil and [even though] I am deprived of evils; that the one who is unjust to himself, if he comes to Him seeking forgiveness, he finds God forgiving. So bear witness, my God, that I am seeking forgiveness—I cannot be sufficiently grateful for what You have bestowed. This is what I have prepared for my hardships—sufficient is my Lord as a Guide and Helper.' The shaykh Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Ghassani and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri' informed us, both saying: The shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas Abu Sa'd al-Jurjani, known as al-Isma'ili, visited Baghdad more than once, and his last visit was during the lifetime of Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni. He narrated from his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, from Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm al-Naysaburi, and from Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn...
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili (d. 396 AH). It begins by placing him among the second stratum of scholars who followed the path of the author's teacher. The passage then details his full name, his status as an imam, his expertise in numerous fields including jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, Arabic, writing, conditions, and theology. He authored a major work on usul al-fiqh called 'Tahdhib al-Nazar' and a refutation of al-Jassas on beverages. He taught for many years and many students graduated from him. The author then lists his praiseworthy qualities: deep piety, striving, good character, generosity, etc. The author mentions that he performed Hajj with him twice and observed his consistent noble character. Next, the passage lists his teachers and narrations: from al-Shafi'i, al-Fakihi, Da'laj, al-Asamm, and Ibn 'Adi, and he collected Malik's Musnad. Then the death: on a Friday night in Rabi' al-Akhir 396, at age 63, prayed over by his brother, buried near his father. A notable honor: he died while reciting 'Iyyaka na'budu wa iyyaka nasta'in' in Maghrib prayer. Additionally, before his death, all his wealth and properties were taken from him through a series of misfortunes: cotton lost at sea, merchandise taken by Kurds, wheat looted, and an estate ordered destroyed by Qabus ibn Wushmagir. This was a sign of honor, as he left the world detached. He left several children, among whom two became scholars. The passage then includes a poem composed by Abu Sa'd, which he recited to his father and then to the author. The poem expresses his preparation for death: certainty in God's oneness, testimony of prophethood, disassociation from shirk, love for the Prophet's family and Companions, adherence to al-Shafi'i, and hope in God's forgiveness. The final part is a report from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi confirming that al-Isma'ili visited Baghdad multiple times, with his last visit during the lifetime of al-Daraqutni, and that he narrated from his father and al-Asamm. The text cuts off mid-chain likely continuing to list more teachers.

The Blessed Death of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili
Report of Abu Sa'd's death and the honor of dying in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circumstances of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili's death, including his age, funeral, and the honor of dying in prayer.

Core Idea
He died while reciting the Quran in prayer, a sign of divine honor.

This lesson focuses on the final moments of Abu Sa'd's life, which were marked by spiritual grace. The passage reports the exact date of his death, the large funeral, and the remarkable fact that he passed away during prayer while reciting a verse. It illustrates how a righteous scholar's death can be a continuation of his devotion.

Guided Path
1
Read the death account
Read the passage about his death, noting the date, age, and funeral details.
The date is the night of Friday, mid-Rabi' al-Akhir 396 AH.
2
Focus on the honor
The passage states that he died in Maghrib prayer reciting 'Iyyaka na'budu wa iyyaka nasta'in'. Reflect on the significance.
This verse is from Surah al-Fatiha, the opening of the prayer.
3
Connect to his life
Consider how this death reflects his lifelong devotion.

ذكر بعض الطبقة الثانية وهم أصحاب أصحابه ممن سلك مسلكه في الأصول وتأدب بآدابه فمنهم أبو سعد بن أبي بكر الإسماعيلى الجرجانى رحمه الله أخبرنا أبو القسم بن أبي بكر الدلال قال أنا أبو القسم بن أبي الفضل الجرجان قال أنا أبو القسم حمزة بن يوسف بن إبراهيم السهمي في كتاب تاريخ جرجان قال إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل بن العباس أبو سعد الإسماعيلى كان أمام زمانه مقدما في الفقه وأصول الفقه والعربية بن إبراهيم الشافعي ومحمد بن أسحق الفاكهى ودعلج وعن الأصم محمد بن يعقوب حديثاً واحداً وعن عبد الله ابن عدى كتاب الضعفاء وجمعه مسند مالك بن أنس توفى ليلة الجمعة النصف من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة ست وتسعين وثلاثمائة وصلى عليه أخوه أبو نصر الإسماعيلى فى صحراء باب الخندق فى جمع عظيم لم أر مثل ذلك الجمع بجرجان في تشييع جنازة أحد قط ودفن عند رأس والده أبى بكر الإسماعيلي توفى وهو ابن ثلاث وستين سنة ومما أكرمه الله به ورفع قدره به أنه مات وهو في صلاة المغرب يقرأ إياك نعبد وإياك نستعين ففاضت نفسه ومما أكرمه الله به أنه حين قربت وفاته ذهب منه ما كان يملكه من المال والضياع وكان يوجه القطن إلى باب الأبواب جميع فغرق الجميع في البحر وكانت له بضاعة تحمل من أصبهان فوقع عليها الأكراد فأخذوها وكان يحمل له من خراسان شئ من الحنطة فوقع عليه قوم وأغاروا عليه وكان له ضيعة بقرية تعرف بكوشكى أمر قابوس بن وشمكير أن يقلع أشجارها فقلع جميع ذلك وكبست القناة وقبض جميع ضياعه وخلف من الأولاد أبا معمر المفضل وأبا العلاء السرى وأبا سعيد سعد وأبا الفضل مسعدة وأبا الحسن مبشر وابنتين فأما أبو معمر فصار أماماً مقدماً في العلوم وأبو العلاء فإنه أيضاً صار عالماً في الفقه والأدب حضرت يوما مجلس الإمام أبي بكر الإسماعيلي على باب داره ننتظر خروجه فخرج الإمام أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم الإسماعيلي وهو مستبشر وبيده جزء فجلس وقال أنشدنى ابنى أبو سعد وأنشدنا ثم أنشدنا الإمام أبو سعد بعد ما أنشدنا والده عنه أنى أدخرت ليوم ورد منیتی عند الإله من الأمور خطيرا وهو اليقين بأنه الأحد الذي مازلت منه بفضله مغمورا وشهادتي أن النبي محمدا كان الرسول مبشراً ونذيرا وبراءتي من كل شرك قاله من لا يقر بفعله مبرورا ومحبتي آل النبي وصحبه كلا أراه بالجميل جديرا وتمسكى بالشافعي وعلمه ذاك الذي فتق العلوم بحورا وجميل ظني بالاله لما جنت نفسى وأن حرمت على شرورا أن الظلوم لنفسه إن يأته مستغفراً يجد الآله غفورا فاشهد الهي أننى مستغفر لا أستطيع لما مننت شكوراً هذا الذى أعددته لشدائدي وكفى بربی هاديا ونصيرا أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور الغساني وأبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى قالا قال لنا الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر أحمد ابن على بن ثابت الخطيب إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل ابن العباس أبو سعد الجرجاني المعروف بالإسماعيلى ورد بغداد غير مرة وآخر وروده كان في حياة أبي الحسن الدارقطني وحدث عن أبيه أبي بكر الإسماعيلي وعن أبي العباس الأصم النيسابورى ومحمد بن أحمد ابن
He mentioned some of the second stratum, who are the companions of his companions, those who followed his path in principles and were disciplined by his manners. Among them is Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Bakr al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani, may God have mercy on him. Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Bakr al-Dallal informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi al-Fadl al-Jurjani informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf ibn Ibrahim al-Sahmi informed us in the book 'History of Jurjan', saying: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili was the imam of his time, foremost in jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, Arabic language, writing, conditions, and theology. He authored a large book on principles of jurisprudence called 'Tahdhib al-Nazar', and he has a book on beverages refuting al-Jassas. He taught jurisprudence for many years, and a group of jurists from Jurjan, Tabaristan, and other regions graduated under him. He possessed praiseworthy qualities that cannot be counted: deep piety, striving in worship and knowledge, concern for religious affairs, sincerity to Islam, good character, cheerfulness, generosity in feeding others, and spending wealth—I cannot enumerate it all. May God's mercy and pleasure be upon him. I performed Hajj with him in the year 384, when he returned from halfway through the desert, and he performed Hajj in 385 until he returned to his homeland. I was with him; I never saw him change from his noble character. He was honored and revered in all countries. He narrated from Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Shafi'i, Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Fakihi, Da'laj, and from al-Asamm Muhammad ibn Ya'qub one hadith, and from Abdullah ibn Adi the book 'al-Du'afa', and he collected the Musnad of Malik ibn Anas. He died on the night of Friday, the middle of Rabi' al-Akhir, in the year 396. His brother Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili prayed over him in the desert of Bab al-Khandaq in a huge crowd—I never saw such a crowd in Jurjan for anyone's funeral procession. He was buried at the head of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. He died at the age of sixty-three. Among the honors God bestowed upon him and elevated his rank thereby was that he died while performing the Maghrib prayer reciting 'You alone we worship, and You alone we ask for help', and his soul departed. And among the honors God bestowed upon him was that when his death approached, the wealth and estates he owned left him. He used to send cotton to Bab al-Abwab, and all of it sank in the sea. He had merchandise carried from Isfahan, and Kurds attacked and took it. He had some wheat brought from Khurasan, and a group attacked and looted it. He had an estate in a village known as Kushki; Qabus ibn Wushmagir ordered its trees to be uprooted, so all that was uprooted, the canal was blocked, and all his estates were seized. He left behind from his children: Abu Mu'mar al-Mufaddal, Abu al-'Ala' al-Sari, Abu Sa'id Sa'd, Abu al-Fadl Mas'ada, Abu al-Hasan Mubashshir, and two daughters. As for Abu Mu'mar, he became an imam foremost in the sciences; and Abu al-'Ala', he also became a scholar in jurisprudence and literature. One day I attended the gathering of Imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili at the door of his house, waiting for his exit. Then Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Isma'ili came out, beaming, with a volume in his hand. He sat down and said: 'My son Abu Sa'd recited to me,' and he recited to us. Then Imam Abu Sa'd recited to us after his father had recited to us from him: 'I have stored up for the day of my death a serious matter with God: it is certainty that He is the One, with whose favor I have always been overwhelmed; and my testimony that Muhammad is the Prophet, a bringer of good news and a warner; and my disassociation from every polytheism uttered by one who does not acknowledge His action, approved; and my love for the family of the Prophet and his Companions, all of them I see as worthy of good; and my adherence to al-Shafi'i and his knowledge—that is he who split open the seas of knowledge; and my good opinion of God, even though my soul has committed evil and [even though] I am deprived of evils; that the one who is unjust to himself, if he comes to Him seeking forgiveness, he finds God forgiving. So bear witness, my God, that I am seeking forgiveness—I cannot be sufficiently grateful for what You have bestowed. This is what I have prepared for my hardships—sufficient is my Lord as a Guide and Helper.' The shaykh Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Ghassani and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri' informed us, both saying: The shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas Abu Sa'd al-Jurjani, known as al-Isma'ili, visited Baghdad more than once, and his last visit was during the lifetime of Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni. He narrated from his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, from Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm al-Naysaburi, and from Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn...

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

The Loss of Wealth: A Divine Favor
Narrative of Abu Sa'd's loss of wealth before death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the loss of Abu Sa'd's wealth before his death is presented as an honor from God, not a punishment.

Core Idea
He was stripped of all worldly possessions before death, enabling him to meet God detached from worldly concerns.

In a striking series of events, Abu Sa'd lost all his wealth and property in the time leading up to his death. The biographer explicitly counts this among the honors God bestowed upon him. This lesson explores those incidents and their spiritual significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of losses
Read the passage detailing the different ways his wealth was taken: cotton sunk at sea, merchandise stolen by Kurds, wheat looted, and estate destroyed.
The passage presents these as separate incidents.
2
Understand the honor
The passage begins by saying 'Mimma akramahu Allah bihi' (among the honors God bestowed upon him). Reflect on why this is considered an honor.
It allowed him to depart from the world without attachment to wealth.
3
Contrast with worldly view
Contrast this perspective with the common view that loss of wealth is a punishment.
This aligns with the common_misunderstanding field.

أكرمه الله به ورفع قدره به أنه مات وهو في صلاة المغرب يقرأ إياك نعبد وإياك نستعين ففاضت نفسه ومما أكرمه الله به أنه حين قربت وفاته ذهب منه ما كان يملكه من المال والضياع وكان يوجه القطن إلى باب الأبواب جميع فغرق الجميع في البحر وكانت له بضاعة تحمل من أصبهان فوقع عليها الأكراد فأخذوها وكان يحمل له من خراسان شئ من الحنطة فوقع عليه قوم وأغاروا عليه وكان له ضيعة بقرية تعرف بكوشكى أمر قابوس بن وشمكير أن العلوم وأبو العلاء فإنه أيضاً صار عالماً في الفقه والأدب حضرت يوما مجلس الإمام أبي بكر الإسماعيلي على باب داره ننتظر خروجه فخرج الإمام أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم الإسماعيلي وهو مستبشر وبيده جزء فجلس وقال أنشدنى ابنى أبو سعد وأنشدنا ثم أنشدنا الإمام أبو سعد بعد ما أنشدنا والده عنه أنى أدخرت ليوم ورد منیتی عند الإله من الأمور خطيرا وهو اليقين بأنه الأحد الذي مازلت منه بفضله مغمورا وشهادتي أن النبي محمدا كان الرسول مبشراً ونذيرا وبراءتي من كل شرك قاله من لا يقر بفعله مبرورا ومحبتي آل النبي وصحبه كلا أراه بالجميل جديرا وتمسكى بالشافعي وعلمه ذاك الذي فتق العلوم بحورا وجميل ظني بالاله لما جنت نفسى وأن حرمت على شرورا أن الظلوم لنفسه إن يأته مستغفراً يجد الآله غفورا فاشهد الهي أننى مستغفر لا أستطيع لما مننت شكوراً هذا الذى أعددته لشدائدي وكفى بربی هاديا ونصيرا أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور الغساني وأبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى قالا قال لنا الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر أحمد ابن على بن ثابت الخطيب إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل ابن العباس أبو سعد الجرجاني المعروف بالإسماعيلى ورد بغداد غير مرة وآخر وروده كان في حياة أبي الحسن الدارقطني وحدث عن أبيه أبي بكر الإسماعيلي وعن أبي العباس الأصم النيسابورى ومحمد بن أحمد ابن
He mentioned some of the second stratum, who are the companions of his companions, those who followed his path in principles and were disciplined by his manners. Among them is Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Bakr al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani, may God have mercy on him. Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Bakr al-Dallal informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi al-Fadl al-Jurjani informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf ibn Ibrahim al-Sahmi informed us in the book 'History of Jurjan', saying: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili was the imam of his time, foremost in jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, Arabic language, writing, conditions, and theology. He authored a large book on principles of jurisprudence called 'Tahdhib al-Nazar', and he has a book on beverages refuting al-Jassas. He taught jurisprudence for many years, and a group of jurists from Jurjan, Tabaristan, and other regions graduated under him. He possessed praiseworthy qualities that cannot be counted: deep piety, striving in worship and knowledge, concern for religious affairs, sincerity to Islam, good character, cheerfulness, generosity in feeding others, and spending wealth—I cannot enumerate it all. May God's mercy and pleasure be upon him. I performed Hajj with him in the year 384, when he returned from halfway through the desert, and he performed Hajj in 385 until he returned to his homeland. I was with him; I never saw him change from his noble character. He was honored and revered in all countries. He narrated from Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Shafi'i, Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Fakihi, Da'laj, and from al-Asamm Muhammad ibn Ya'qub one hadith, and from Abdullah ibn Adi the book 'al-Du'afa', and he collected the Musnad of Malik ibn Anas. He died on the night of Friday, the middle of Rabi' al-Akhir, in the year 396. His brother Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili prayed over him in the desert of Bab al-Khandaq in a huge crowd—I never saw such a crowd in Jurjan for anyone's funeral procession. He was buried at the head of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. He died at the age of sixty-three. Among the honors God bestowed upon him and elevated his rank thereby was that he died while performing the Maghrib prayer reciting 'You alone we worship, and You alone we ask for help', and his soul departed. And among the honors God bestowed upon him was that when his death approached, the wealth and estates he owned left him. He used to send cotton to Bab al-Abwab, and all of it sank in the sea. He had merchandise carried from Isfahan, and Kurds attacked and took it. He had some wheat brought from Khurasan, and a group attacked and looted it. He had an estate in a village known as Kushki; Qabus ibn Wushmagir ordered its trees to be uprooted, so all that was uprooted, the canal was blocked, and all his estates were seized. He left behind from his children: Abu Mu'mar al-Mufaddal, Abu al-'Ala' al-Sari, Abu Sa'id Sa'd, Abu al-Fadl Mas'ada, Abu al-Hasan Mubashshir, and two daughters. As for Abu Mu'mar, he became an imam foremost in the sciences; and Abu al-'Ala', he also became a scholar in jurisprudence and literature. One day I attended the gathering of Imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili at the door of his house, waiting for his exit. Then Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Isma'ili came out, beaming, with a volume in his hand. He sat down and said: 'My son Abu Sa'd recited to me,' and he recited to us. Then Imam Abu Sa'd recited to us after his father had recited to us from him: 'I have stored up for the day of my death a serious matter with God: it is certainty that He is the One, with whose favor I have always been overwhelmed; and my testimony that Muhammad is the Prophet, a bringer of good news and a warner; and my disassociation from every polytheism uttered by one who does not acknowledge His action, approved; and my love for the family of the Prophet and his Companions, all of them I see as worthy of good; and my adherence to al-Shafi'i and his knowledge—that is he who split open the seas of knowledge; and my good opinion of God, even though my soul has committed evil and [even though] I am deprived of evils; that the one who is unjust to himself, if he comes to Him seeking forgiveness, he finds God forgiving. So bear witness, my God, that I am seeking forgiveness—I cannot be sufficiently grateful for what You have bestowed. This is what I have prepared for my hardships—sufficient is my Lord as a Guide and Helper.' The shaykh Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Ghassani and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri' informed us, both saying: The shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas Abu Sa'd al-Jurjani, known as al-Isma'ili, visited Baghdad more than once, and his last visit was during the lifetime of Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni. He narrated from his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, from Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm al-Naysaburi, and from Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn...
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili (d. 396 AH). It begins by placing him among the second stratum of scholars who followed the path of the author's teacher. The passage then details his full name, his status as an imam, his expertise in numerous fields including jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, Arabic, writing, conditions, and theology. He authored a major work on usul al-fiqh called 'Tahdhib al-Nazar' and a refutation of al-Jassas on beverages. He taught for many years and many students graduated from him. The author then lists his praiseworthy qualities: deep piety, striving, good character, generosity, etc. The author mentions that he performed Hajj with him twice and observed his consistent noble character. Next, the passage lists his teachers and narrations: from al-Shafi'i, al-Fakihi, Da'laj, al-Asamm, and Ibn 'Adi, and he collected Malik's Musnad. Then the death: on a Friday night in Rabi' al-Akhir 396, at age 63, prayed over by his brother, buried near his father. A notable honor: he died while reciting 'Iyyaka na'budu wa iyyaka nasta'in' in Maghrib prayer. Additionally, before his death, all his wealth and properties were taken from him through a series of misfortunes: cotton lost at sea, merchandise taken by Kurds, wheat looted, and an estate ordered destroyed by Qabus ibn Wushmagir. This was a sign of honor, as he left the world detached. He left several children, among whom two became scholars. The passage then includes a poem composed by Abu Sa'd, which he recited to his father and then to the author. The poem expresses his preparation for death: certainty in God's oneness, testimony of prophethood, disassociation from shirk, love for the Prophet's family and Companions, adherence to al-Shafi'i, and hope in God's forgiveness. The final part is a report from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi confirming that al-Isma'ili visited Baghdad multiple times, with his last visit during the lifetime of al-Daraqutni, and that he narrated from his father and al-Asamm. The text cuts off mid-chain likely continuing to list more teachers.

القناه
قابوس بن وشمكير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Loss of wealth before death is a sign of God's displeasure.
Correction: For the righteous, it can be an honor, as it removes worldly attachments before meeting God.

Checkpoint
What happened to the cotton Abu Sa'd sent to Bab al-Abwab?
A) It was stolen by Kurds
B) It sank in the sea
C) It was looted by a group
D) It was destroyed by Qabus

Key Takeaway
Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili's loss of all wealth before death is considered a divine honor, freeing him from worldly attachment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Abu Sa'd lost his wealth in multiple ways, did you feel pity or admiration? What does your reaction reveal about your own attachment to worldly things?
?
Can you recall a loss in your life that you initially saw as a disaster? In light of this lesson, could it have been a hidden honor from God? What would it take for you to see it that way?
?
The phrase 'Mimma akramahu Allah bihi' frames these losses as honors. Is there any attachment in your life—wealth, status, or relationships—that you would struggle to lose with such trust? What is one step you can take today to loosen that attachment?

The Children of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili
Listing of Abu Sa'd's children and their scholarly attainments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the names of Abu Sa'd's children and the scholarly achievements of some of them.

Core Idea
He left behind a legacy of scholarly children who continued his tradition.

The biography mentions the names of Abu Sa'd's children, highlighting that two of his sons became notable scholars themselves. This lesson focuses on his family legacy and how his learning was passed on.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of children
Read the names of his children from the passage.
There are five sons and two daughters.
2
Focus on the scholarly sons
The passage specifically notes that Abu Mu'mar became an imam in sciences and Abu al-Ala' became a scholar in jurisprudence and literature.
3
Reflect on legacy
Consider how this reflects the long-term impact of Abu Sa'd's teaching.

This passage is a biographical entry about Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili (d. 396 AH). It begins by placing him among the second stratum of scholars who followed the path of the author's teacher. The passage then details his full name, his status as an imam, his expertise in numerous fields including jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, Arabic, writing, conditions, and theology. He authored a major work on usul al-fiqh called 'Tahdhib al-Nazar' and a refutation of al-Jassas on beverages. He taught for many years and many students graduated from him. The author then lists his praiseworthy qualities: deep piety, striving, good character, generosity, etc. The author mentions that he performed Hajj with him twice and observed his consistent noble character. Next, the passage lists his teachers and narrations: from al-Shafi'i, al-Fakihi, Da'laj, al-Asamm, and Ibn 'Adi, and he collected Malik's Musnad. Then the death: on a Friday night in Rabi' al-Akhir 396, at age 63, prayed over by his brother, buried near his father. A notable honor: he died while reciting 'Iyyaka na'budu wa iyyaka nasta'in' in Maghrib prayer. ?

The Poem of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili: A Testament of Faith
Abu Sa'd's poem expressing his faith and hope in God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the content of Abu Sa'd's poem, which expresses his core beliefs and hopes for the afterlife.

Core Idea
His poem summarizes his theological convictions and his preparation for death.

This lesson presents a poem composed by Abu Sa'd, which he recited to his father and later to the author. The poem encapsulates his faith: belief in God's oneness, prophethood of Muhammad, love for the Prophet's family and Companions, adherence to al-Shafi'i, and hope for divine forgiveness. It serves as a spiritual testament.

Guided Path
1
Read the poem
Read the Arabic poem slowly, then the translation, paying attention to its themes.
The poem is a series of declarations.
2
Identify the key themes
Note the themes: certainty in God, testimony of prophethood, disassociation from shirk, love for Ahl al-Bayt, adherence to Shafi'i, and hope for forgiveness.
3
Connect to his life
Consider how this poem reflects his lifelong priorities and prepares him for the afterlife.

ذكر بعض الطبقة الثانية وهم أصحاب أصحابه ممن سلك مسلكه في الأصول وتأدب بآدابه فمنهم أبو سعد بن أبي بكر الإسماعيلى الجرجانى رحمه الله أخبرنا أبو القسم بن أبي بكر الدلال قال أنا أبو القسم بن أبي الفضل الجرجان قال أنا أبو القسم حمزة بن يوسف بن إبراهيم السهمي في كتاب تاريخ جرجان قال إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل بن العباس أبو سعد الإسماعيلى كان أمام زمانه مقدما في الفقه وأصول الفقه والعربية والكتابة والشروط والكلام صنف في أصول الفقه كتاباً كبيراً سماه تهذيب النظر وله كتاب الأشربة رد على الجصاص درس الفقه سنين كثيرة وتخرج على يده جماعة من الفقهاء من أهل جرجان وطبرستان وغيرهما من البلدان وكان فيه من الخصال المحمودة التي لا تحصى من الورع الثخين والمجاهدة في العبادة والعلم والاهتمام بأمور الدين والنصيحة للإسلام وحسن الخلق وطلاقة الوجه والسخاء في الإطعام وبذل المال ومالا أقدر أن أحصيه رحمة الله عليه ورضوانه حججت معه سنة أربع وثمانين حيث رجع من نصف البادية وحج في سنة خمس وثمانين إلى أن رجع إلى وطنه كنت معه لم أره تغير عن خلقه النفس كان معظما مبجلا في جميع البلدان روى عن أبي بكر محمد بن إبراهيم الشافعي ومحمد بن أسحق الفاكهى ودعلج وعن الأصم محمد بن يعقوب حديثاً واحداً وعن عبد الله ابن عدى كتاب الضعفاء وجمعه مسند مالك بن أنس توفى ليلة الجمعة النصف من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة ست وتسعين وثلاثمائة وصلى عليه أخوه أبو نصر الإسماعيلى فى صحراء باب الخندق فى جمع عظيم لم أر مثل ذلك الجمع بجرجان في تشييع جنازة أحد قط ودفن عند رأس والده أبى بكر الإسماعيلي توفى وهو ابن ثلاث وستين سنة ومما أكرمه الله به ورفع قدره به أنه مات وهو في صلاة المغرب يقرأ إياك نعبد وإياك نستعين ففاضت نفسه ومما أكرمه الله به أنه حين قربت وفاته ذهب منه ما كان يملكه من المال والضياع وكان يوجه القطن إلى باب الأبواب جميع فغرق الجميع في البحر وكانت له بضاعة تحمل من أصبهان فوقع عليها الأكراد فأخذوها وكان يحمل له من خراسان شئ من الحنطة فوقع عليه قوم وأغاروا عليه وكان له ضيعة بقرية تعرف بكوشكى أمر قابوس بن وشمكير أن يقلع أشجارها فقلع جميع ذلك وكبست القناة وقبض جميع ضياعه وخلف من الأولاد أبا معمر المفضل وأبا العلاء السرى وأبا سعيد سعد وأبا الفضل مسعدة وأبا الحسن مبشر وابنتين فأما أبو معمر فصار أماماً مقدماً في العلوم وأبو العلاء فإنه أيضاً صار عالماً في الفقه والأدب حضرت يوما مجلس الإمام أبي بكر الإسماعيلي على باب داره ننتظر خروجه فخرج الإمام أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم الإسماعيلي وهو مستبشر وبيده جزء فجلس وقال أنشدنى ابنى أبو سعد وأنشدنا ثم أنشدنا الإمام أبو سعد بعد ما أنشدنا والده عنه أنى أدخرت ليوم ورد منیتی عند الإله من الأمور خطيرا وهو اليقين بأنه الأحد الذي مازلت منه بفضله مغمورا وشهادتي أن النبي محمدا كان الرسول مبشراً ونذيرا وبراءتي من كل شرك قاله من لا يقر بفعله مبرورا ومحبتي آل النبي وصحبه كلا أراه بالجميل جديرا وتمسكى بالشافعي وعلمه ذاك الذي فتق العلوم بحورا وجميل ظني بالاله لما جنت نفسى وأن حرمت على شرورا أن الظلوم لنفسه إن يأته مستغفراً يجد الآله غفورا فاشهد الهي أننى مستغفر لا أستطيع لما مننت شكوراً هذا الذى أعددته لشدائدي وكفى بربی هاديا ونصيرا أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور الغساني وأبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى قالا قال لنا الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر أحمد ابن على بن ثابت الخطيب إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل ابن العباس أبو سعد الجرجاني المعروف بالإسماعيلى ورد بغداد غير مرة وآخر وروده كان في حياة أبي الحسن الدارقطني وحدث عن أبيه أبي بكر الإسماعيلي وعن أبي العباس الأصم النيسابورى ومحمد بن أحمد ابن
He mentioned some of the second stratum, who are the companions of his companions, those who followed his path in principles and were disciplined by his manners. Among them is Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Bakr al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani, may God have mercy on him. Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Bakr al-Dallal informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi al-Fadl al-Jurjani informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf ibn Ibrahim al-Sahmi informed us in the book 'History of Jurjan', saying: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili was the imam of his time, foremost in jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, Arabic language, writing, conditions, and theology. He authored a large book on principles of jurisprudence called 'Tahdhib al-Nazar', and he has a book on beverages refuting al-Jassas. He taught jurisprudence for many years, and a group of jurists from Jurjan, Tabaristan, and other regions graduated under him. He possessed praiseworthy qualities that cannot be counted: deep piety, striving in worship and knowledge, concern for religious affairs, sincerity to Islam, good character, cheerfulness, generosity in feeding others, and spending wealth—I cannot enumerate it all. May God's mercy and pleasure be upon him. I performed Hajj with him in the year 384, when he returned from halfway through the desert, and he performed Hajj in 385 until he returned to his homeland. I was with him; I never saw him change from his noble character. He was honored and revered in all countries. He narrated from Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Shafi'i, Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Fakihi, Da'laj, and from al-Asamm Muhammad ibn Ya'qub one hadith, and from Abdullah ibn Adi the book 'al-Du'afa', and he collected the Musnad of Malik ibn Anas. He died on the night of Friday, the middle of Rabi' al-Akhir, in the year 396. His brother Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili prayed over him in the desert of Bab al-Khandaq in a huge crowd—I never saw such a crowd in Jurjan for anyone's funeral procession. He was buried at the head of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. He died at the age of sixty-three. Among the honors God bestowed upon him and elevated his rank thereby was that he died while performing the Maghrib prayer reciting 'You alone we worship, and You alone we ask for help', and his soul departed. And among the honors God bestowed upon him was that when his death approached, the wealth and estates he owned left him. He used to send cotton to Bab al-Abwab, and all of it sank in the sea. He had merchandise carried from Isfahan, and Kurds attacked and took it. He had some wheat brought from Khurasan, and a group attacked and looted it. He had an estate in a village known as Kushki; Qabus ibn Wushmagir ordered its trees to be uprooted, so all that was uprooted, the canal was blocked, and all his estates were seized. He left behind from his children: Abu Mu'mar al-Mufaddal, Abu al-'Ala' al-Sari, Abu Sa'id Sa'd, Abu al-Fadl Mas'ada, Abu al-Hasan Mubashshir, and two daughters. As for Abu Mu'mar, he became an imam foremost in the sciences; and Abu al-'Ala', he also became a scholar in jurisprudence and literature. One day I attended the gathering of Imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili at the door of his house, waiting for his exit. Then Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Isma'ili came out, beaming, with a volume in his hand. He sat down and said: 'My son Abu Sa'd recited to me,' and he recited to us. Then Imam Abu Sa'd recited to us after his father had recited to us from him: 'I have stored up for the day of my death a serious matter with God: it is certainty that He is the One, with whose favor I have always been overwhelmed; and my testimony that Muhammad is the Prophet, a bringer of good news and a warner; and my disassociation from every polytheism uttered by one who does not acknowledge His action, approved; and my love for the family of the Prophet and his Companions, all of them I see as worthy of good; and my adherence to al-Shafi'i and his knowledge—that is he who split open the seas of knowledge; and my good opinion of God, even though my soul has committed evil and [even though] I am deprived of evils; that the one who is unjust to himself, if he comes to Him seeking forgiveness, he finds God forgiving. So bear witness, my God, that I am seeking forgiveness—I cannot be sufficiently grateful for what You have bestowed. This is what I have prepared for my hardships—sufficient is my Lord as a Guide and Helper.' The shaykh Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Ghassani and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri' informed us, both saying: The shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas Abu Sa'd al-Jurjani, known as al-Isma'ili, visited Baghdad more than once, and his last visit was during the lifetime of Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni. He narrated from his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, from Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm al-Naysaburi, and from Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn...

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili (d. 396 AH). It begins by placing him among the second stratum of scholars who followed the path of the author's teacher. The passage then details his full name, his status as an imam, his expertise in numerous fields including jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, Arabic, writing, conditions, and theology. He authored a major work on usul al-fiqh called 'Tahdhib al-Nazar' and a refutation of al-Jassas on beverages. He taught for many years and many students graduated from him. The author then lists his praiseworthy qualities: deep piety, striving, good character, generosity, etc. The author mentions that he performed Hajj with him twice and observed his consistent noble character. Next, the passage lists his teachers and narrations: from al-Shafi'i, al-Fakihi, Da'laj, al-Asamm, and Ibn 'Adi, and he collected Malik's Musnad. Then the death: on a Friday night in Rabi' al-Akhir 396, at age 63, prayed over by his brother, buried near his father. A notable honor: he died while reciting 'Iyyaka na'budu wa iyyaka nasta'in' in Maghrib prayer. Additionally, before his death, all his wealth and properties were taken from him through a series of misfortunes: cotton lost at sea, merchandise taken by Kurds, wheat looted, and an estate ordered destroyed by Qabus ibn Wushmagir. This was a sign of honor, as he left the world detached. He left several children, among whom two became scholars. The passage then includes a poem composed by Abu Sa'd, which he recited to his father and then to the author. The poem expresses his preparation for death: certainty in God's oneness, testimony of prophethood, disassociation from shirk, love for the Prophet's family and Companions, adherence to al-Shafi'i, and hope in God's forgiveness. The final part is a report from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi confirming that al-Isma'ili visited Baghdad multiple times, with his last visit during the lifetime of al-Daraqutni, and that he narrated from his father and al-Asamm. The text cuts off mid-chain likely continuing to list more teachers.

Checkpoint
In the poem, what does Abu Sa'd say he has stored up for the day of his death?
A) Wealth
B) Serious matters with God
C) Good deeds only

Key Takeaway
Abu Sa'd's poem reveals his deep faith, hope in God's mercy, and his spiritual preparation for the afterlife.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What have you stored up for the day of your death? List the specific beliefs and actions you have prepared as Abu Sa'd did. If you haven't, what is stopping you from beginning today?
?
Abu Sa'd says he has a good opinion of God even though his soul has committed evil. Do you truly believe that God will forgive you despite your sins, or do you secretly despair of His mercy? How does that affect your relationship with Him?
?
He ends by saying he cannot be sufficiently grateful. In your daily life, where do you fall short in gratitude for God's blessings? What one change can you make tonight to show more thankfulness?
